# Zeno Transformation — Discussion Agenda

Date: 2026-06-11

Sources: `docs/tools as wokflow scenarios/zeno_tool_catalog.md` (conceptual target) + `zeno_workflow.feature` (Gherkin behaviour spec), assessed against the codebase at branch `claude/unruffled-pike-1535df`.

Method: 13 topic analysts (code-grounded), each adversarially fact-checked against the code; a completeness critic walked every Gherkin scenario for coverage and cross-topic conflicts. Recommendations are made on **architectural merit only** — implementation effort was explicitly excluded as a decision factor.

How to read: each topic has numbered decision points (`T<n>.D<m>`) with options; the recommended option is marked **✅ Recommended**. "Fact-check corrections" list where the analyst's prose was corrected against the code — trust the correction over the prose. Intended use: walk one decision point at a time, in the suggested order at the end.

---

## T1. Legality engine: available_actions / blocked_actions computed per turn

> Topic key: `legality-engine`

### Current state (code-grounded)

VERIFIED CURRENT STATE (all paths relative to code root C:/GitHub/Zeno/.claude/worktrees/unruffled-pike-1535df):

1) Tool exposure today is STATIC, not state-derived. The per-turn LLM tool list is computed in lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:417-419 as stepAllowedTools = withDefaultDiscoveryTools(workflowSession?.currentStep.allowedTools ?? []) and consumed at lines 789-794: effectiveTools = (effectivePacks.length > 0 ? computeAllowedTools(stepAllowedTools, effectivePacks) : stepAllowedTools); tools = getToolsForLLM(effectiveTools). BOTH dynamic inputs are dead: (a) WorkflowSession records are never created anywhere in lib/ or app/ (confirmed by grep; lib/tools/pipeline.ts:8-12 states this explicitly — the workflow gate/transition machinery was retired), so workflowSession is always null; (b) skill packs never activate because recommendedSlugs is hardcoded [] at lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:597 since commit ce1b27d (reasoning-gate retirement — verified via git log -L; previously recommendedSlugs = gateOutput?.recommendedSkillPacks). Net effect: the LLM sees exactly the 10 tools in DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS (lib/chat/default-tools.ts:9-20: list_products, get_product_info, set_candidate_product, record_gdpr_consent, acknowledge_ai_disclosure, get_current_state, set_answer, change_selection, switch_product, preview_product_requirements) every turn, in every phase. computeAllowedTools (lib/skills/skill-pack-loader.ts:169-190, union semantics) is dead code in the live path.

2) Consequence: funnel commit tools — sign_dnt, start_dnt_questionnaire, save_dnt_answer, start_application, save_application_answer, generate_quote, accept_quote, initiate_payment, cancel_application, resume_application, collect_customer_field, escalate_to_human — are registered in lib/tools/registry.ts but are NOT callable by the agent in the standard chat path; they are reachable only via UI synthetic tool calls (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts → input.syntheticToolCall branch at orchestrator.ts:798). Meanwhile deriveState's nextBestAction (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:51-66) instructs the agent to "sign_dnt" (CONSENT), "call generate_quote" (QUOTE), "proceed to accept_quote" (CLOSING) — tools it cannot call. This directly violates the spec scenario "Every demanded action maps to an exposed tool" (docs/tools as wokflow scenarios/zeno_workflow.feature:49-52) and appears to be a live regression introduced when the gate (which used to recommend packs that granted these tools) was retired.

3) Enforcement at the executor is role-based only. lib/tools/executor.ts:67-191 does: definition exists → validateToolArgs → checkPermission (lib/tools/permissions.ts — pure role hierarchy CUSTOMER<OPERATOR<ADMIN) → cache → circuit breaker → handler. There is NO check that the called tool is in the turn's allowed list and NO state-based legality check. The synthetic tool path executes any registered tool unconditionally.

4) De-facto legality lives as scattered ad-hoc guards inside handlers returning untyped error strings: startApplication checks dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:35-40) and tier/level validity; saveApplicationAnswer requires an OPEN application (application-handlers.ts:133-141); generateQuote checks GDPR consents, application.status==='COMPLETED', and tierId/levelId presence (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:20-52). There is no consequence taxonomy — failures are {success:false, error:string}.

5) deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts) computes a 6-phase DerivedState (DISCOVERY/SELECTION/CONSENT/QUESTIONNAIRE/QUOTE/CLOSING + product/selection/consents/dnt/application/quote/answers/nextBestAction) from DB once per turn at Step 3 (orchestrator.ts:426-450, in parallel with context assembly), and feeds (a) prompt section selection via getRequiredSectionsForPhase and (b) the situationalBriefing via formatDerivedBriefing (lib/chat/phase-sections-map.ts). It computes NO available_actions/blocked_actions. It is NOT re-derived after tool execution within a turn: the tools array is built once before the tool loop (orchestrator.ts:794), and the toolContext refresh at orchestrator.ts:1298-1302 is gated on pipelineResult.transition which is never set (pipeline.ts returns only toolResult). The only mid-turn state feedback is that set_answer (lib/tools/handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts:103-107) and get_current_state (lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.ts) embed a fresh DerivedState in their tool result data.

6) The prompt's capabilityManifest (lib/chat/context-loaders.ts:76-94, "My tools for this conversation... I can only act through these tools") renders the same static stepAllowedTools list. Prompt sections are assembled via SECTION_REGISTRY in lib/chat/prompt-builder.ts:70-92 (stateGrounding priority 2.5 alwaysInclude; situationalBriefing priority 10 dynamic alwaysInclude).

7) Workflow/WorkflowStep/StepTransition/WorkflowSession models exist in prisma/schema.prisma:367-431 with per-step allowedTools/autoTool/agentInstructions, and prisma/seeds/seed-workflows.ts seeds two workflows (product-discovery, life-insurance-purchase) with detailed step toolsets and TOOL_RESULT/DATA_CHECK transitions — but no runtime code ever creates a WorkflowSession; lib/chat/turn-context.ts:95-107 still eagerly joins workflowSession+currentStep every turn (always null), and the dead shapes thread through WorkflowSessionData (context-loaders.ts:37-43), StateGroundingInput, and PipelineResult.transition (lib/tools/types.ts:112-121).

8) Drift evidence: registry alwaysAllowed metadata (lib/tools/registry.ts:380-392 ALWAYS_ALLOWED_SET comment block and per-tool flags) disagrees with DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS — compare_products, get_objection_strategy, get_customer_profile, update_customer_profile, check_dnt_status are alwaysAllowed:true but not exposed; set_answer and change_selection are exposed but alwaysAllowed:false; isAlwaysAllowed (registry.ts:72) has no live callers. Skill-pack seeds (prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts) grant tool names that do not exist in the registry (get_quote, save_customer_field, get_policy_details). Additionally, two phase vocabularies coexist: deriveState's 6-phase model vs getConversationPhase's 3-phase model (lib/chat/phase.ts) still used by the compliance checker at orchestrator.ts:651.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** current_state #2 and gaps[1]: the 12 funnel commit tools (sign_dnt, start_dnt_questionnaire, save_dnt_answer, start_application, save_application_answer, generate_quote, accept_quote, initiate_payment, cancel_application, resume_application, collect_customer_field, escalate_to_human) "are reachable only via UI synthetic tool calls (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts ...)" / "(only via UI synthetic actions through lib/chat/action-adapter.ts)".
  **Correction:** True for 10 of the 12, but adaptAction has NO mapping for initiate_payment or cancel_application — its switch covers select_tier, select_level, answer_question, accept_quote, modify_quote, submit_field, bd_continue, start_dnt, answer_dnt, sign_dnt, start_application, resume_application, generate_quote, and escalate only, and app/api/chat/route.ts:66-73 (the sole producer of syntheticToolCall) returns 400 for unknown action types. No other app/ code invokes these two tools. So initiate_payment and cancel_application are not reachable via the UI synthetic path either — they are unreachable from the entire chat surface (registered but dead). _(lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:31-152 (full switch; no case emits initiate_payment or cancel_application); app/api/chat/route.ts:63-75 (adaptAction is the only syntheticToolCall producer, unknown actions -> 400); grep of app/**/*.ts for initiate_payment|cancelApplication|cancel_application: zero matches.)_
- **Claim:** current_state #3: "The synthetic tool path executes any registered tool unconditionally." (echoed in gaps[3]: "the synthetic tool path will execute any registered tool unconditionally").
  **Correction:** Overstated. The enforcement-absence part is verified — once a synthetic call reaches the orchestrator (orchestrator.ts:798-833) it goes straight to executeToolWithPipeline -> executeTool with no allowed-list or state-legality check (executor.ts checks only existence, args, role, cache, circuit). But the synthetic path cannot carry an arbitrary registered tool name: clients send UIAction types, not tool names, and adaptAction's fixed mapping bounds the reachable set to 11 distinct tools; unrecognized action types are rejected with 400 at the API route. "Any registered tool" is only executable by a caller that bypasses the action adapter (e.g. code calling executeTool directly), not by the existing UI synthetic path. _(lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:31-152 (closed switch, default returns null); app/api/chat/route.ts:66-73 (null -> 400 'Unknown action type'); lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:798-836 + lib/tools/executor.ts:67-192 (no allowlist/state check — this half of the claim is correct).)_
- **Claim:** decision_points[1] (exposure mechanism), option 'Reject-at-executor only': "the model sees a 32-tool surface with accept_quote visible during DISCOVERY".
  **Correction:** The registry registers 33 tools, not 32 (34 'registerTool(' matches minus the function definition). getToolsForLLM(undefined) iterates all definitions, including the internal profile_extractor and summarizer, so 'send all tools' would expose a 33-tool surface. (The registry's own '// REGISTER ALL 25 TOOLS' banner at registry.ts:402 is also stale.) _(lib/tools/registry.ts — registerTool calls at lines 407, 429, 463, 488, 509, 525, 557, 578, 608, 623, 648, 665, 683, 702, 723, 743, 762, 784, 800, 814, 830, 854, 871, 890, 906, 922, 940, 956, 976, 1003, 1020, 1091, 1109 (= 33); getToolsForLLM at registry.ts:82-105 filters only when allowedTools is provided.)_
- **Claim:** decision_points[4] (mid-turn re-derivation), option 'Re-derive after every commit round' tradeoff: "deriveState is the designed-cheap per-turn baseline and several handlers already call it per execution".
  **Correction:** Exactly two handlers call deriveState per execution — setAnswer (set-answer-handlers.ts:103) and getStateHandler (state-handlers.ts:16). 'Several' overstates the count; no other handler imports or calls deriveState. _(Repo-wide grep for deriveState: only lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:437 (turn start), lib/tools/handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts:103, and lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.ts:16 call it; lib/chat/derive-state.ts:77 is the definition.)_

### Gaps

- No available_actions/blocked_actions computation exists anywhere; the only steering is deriveState.nextBestAction free text (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:51-66), which names tools the agent cannot call.
- The agent's tool surface is a static 10-tool list in every phase (lib/chat/default-tools.ts via orchestrator.ts:417,794): sign_dnt, start_application, save_dnt_answer, start_dnt_questionnaire, generate_quote, accept_quote, initiate_payment, cancel_application, resume_application, collect_customer_field, escalate_to_human are unreachable by the LLM in the standard chat path (only via UI synthetic actions through lib/chat/action-adapter.ts). This is a live funnel deadlock risk and a direct violation of the spec's 'Every demanded action maps to an exposed tool'; it dates from commit ce1b27d which hardcoded recommendedSlugs=[] when retiring the reasoning gate.
- escalate_to_human is not exposed to the LLM at all, contradicting the catalog's 'always' exposure for it (zeno_tool_catalog.md cross-cutting table).
- The executor (lib/tools/executor.ts) enforces only role permissions — it never checks the turn's allowed-tool list nor any state-based legality; the synthetic tool path will execute any registered tool unconditionally. No defense-in-depth exists.
- Legality rules are scattered as handler-local guards returning untyped error strings (application-handlers.ts:35-40, quote-handlers.ts:20-52); there is no consequence taxonomy (the catalog's 14 values: applied/rejected/advance_phase/requires_consent/requires_identity/etc.) and no machine-readable blocked reason.
- DerivedState lacks facts the catalog's 'Exposed when' conditions require: customer identity (isAnonymous), DNT session state (no session entity exists), disclosure acknowledgment (IDD/IPID), quote expiry/validity, payment status, policy existence, open-items for returning users.
- State is not re-derived after commits within a turn: the tools array is computed once before the tool loop (orchestrator.ts:794) and the refresh path at orchestrator.ts:1298-1302 is dead (pipeline never returns transition) — a commit that changes phase cannot change exposure until the next user turn.
- Workflow/WorkflowSession/WorkflowStep/StepTransition tables and seeds are dead at runtime but still eagerly joined every turn (turn-context.ts:95-107) and woven through types (WorkflowSessionData, StateGroundingInput, PipelineResult.transition) — false structure suggesting a gating mechanism that does not run.
- Registry alwaysAllowed metadata, the ALWAYS_ALLOWED_SET constant, and DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS have drifted into three inconsistent 'always available' definitions; isAlwaysAllowed() has no live callers.
- Skill-pack allowedTools in seeds reference unregistered tools (get_quote, save_customer_field, get_policy_details) — no validation ties pack allowlists to the registry.
- Two phase vocabularies coexist (deriveState 6-phase vs lib/chat/phase.ts 3-phase used by the compliance checker at orchestrator.ts:651) — a legality engine keyed on one of them would silently disagree with compliance triggering keyed on the other.

### Decision points

#### T1.D1 — Where should the legality computation (available_actions / blocked_actions + reasons) live?

- **Extend deriveState**: Add availableActions/blockedActions fields to DerivedState and compute them inside lib/chat/derive-state.ts alongside phase derivation.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Keeps one call site and guarantees actions are always computed against the same snapshot. But it conflates facts (what is true) with policy (what is permitted): DerivedState is also consumed as a pure state snapshot by tool results (set_answer, get_current_state) and the debug drawer, where embedding agent-policy is noise; every policy change forces a change to the state-derivation module; and the GUI/swap-test consumer needs facts independently of agent exposure decisions.
- **✅ Recommended — New engine module (lib/engines/legality-engine.ts)**: A pure function computeLegality(state: DerivedState) -> { available: Action[], blocked: { action, reasonCode, reasonText }[] }, with per-action declarative predicates in one table. Fits the existing lib/engines/ convention (question-groups, questionnaire-engine, quote-engine). deriveState remains the single source of facts; legality is a pure projection over it.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One extra module boundary and the obligation to keep DerivedState rich enough to express every 'Exposed when' condition (which is healthy pressure: it forces missing facts — identity, DNT session, disclosures, payment status — to become explicit derived facts rather than ad-hoc handler queries). Pure-function form makes it trivially unit-testable scenario-by-scenario against the Gherkin spec, and lets a non-agent client (GUI endpoint) call the identical computation, satisfying the swap test.
- **Per-handler exposedWhen predicates colocated with tool registration**: Add an exposedWhen(state) predicate + blockedReason to each registerTool() call in lib/tools/registry.ts; the orchestrator filters by evaluating all predicates.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Maximum locality — the rule lives next to the tool. But the state machine becomes invisible as a whole: cross-action invariants from the catalog (e.g., start_dnt_session and update_dnt are mutually exclusive on session type; accept_quote requires disclosures which acknowledge_disclosures clears) are scattered across a 1100-line registry that already mixes presentation concerns (status messages, UI visibility); auditing 'what is legal in state X' requires reading every registration; and the registry currently has provably drifted boolean metadata (alwaysAllowed), demonstrating that per-tool flags rot.

**Rationale:** The catalog's contract is 'the engine computes available_actions/blocked_actions every turn' — a single auditable policy surface. A pure projection over DerivedState gives: (1) testability — each Gherkin exposure scenario becomes a one-assertion unit test on a synthetic DerivedState, plus a snapshot test rendering the full action matrix per canonical state; (2) the swap test — an API route can expose the same computation to a GUI; (3) clean separation — deriveState answers 'what is true', the legality engine answers 'what may be done and why not', and handlers keep only effect logic. The per-action predicate table inside the engine preserves the locality benefit of option 3 without scattering the machine.

**Depends on / interacts with:** phase-model, tool-mapping, dnt-sessions, identity, quote-lifecycle, payments

#### T1.D2 — How should legality be enforced and surfaced to the agent (exposure mechanism)?

- **Filter-only**: Send only available actions as tool definitions to the LLM (replacing the static DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS filter at orchestrator.ts:794); no executor change.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Smallest surface and the model physically cannot call a blocked tool via the API. But it is enforcement by presentation only: the executor today runs ANY registered tool (synthetic UI path included) with no allowlist or state check, so every non-LLM caller bypasses legality entirely; and mid-turn state changes (TOCTOU) make the turn-start filter stale by the time a second-round call executes.
- **Reject-at-executor only**: Send all tools to the LLM; executeTool evaluates legality against fresh state and returns a typed rejected consequence with the blocked reason.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Single enforcement point, always evaluated against fresh state. But the model sees a 32-tool surface with accept_quote visible during DISCOVERY — wasted tokens, more hallucinated-call turns burned on rejections (MAX_TOOL_ROUNDS=5 budget), and the agent learns the boundaries only by failing, which conflicts with the brand requirement to never narrate failed attempts.
- **✅ Recommended — Filter + executor enforcement + blocked_actions prompt injection**: Three consumers of one computation: (a) the LLM tool list is filtered to available actions; (b) executeTool re-evaluates legality against fresh DB state at execution time and hard-rejects illegal calls with { consequence: 'rejected', reason } — covering the synthetic/UI path and mid-turn staleness; (c) the situational briefing (formatDerivedBriefing in lib/chat/phase-sections-map.ts) is extended to render available_actions and blocked_actions with their reason codes, so the agent can explain a block instead of inventing a workaround (zeno_workflow.feature 'A blocked action is explained, not worked around').
  _Tradeoffs:_ Two enforcement surfaces must agree — mitigated by both calling the same computeLegality over a DerivedState (exposure uses the turn snapshot, enforcement re-derives). Changing tool lists between turns reduces provider prompt-cache hits on the tool block (bounded: one list per legality fingerprint; getToolsForLLM already caches per sorted-name key, registry.ts:76-105). The blocked_actions injection costs prompt tokens but is the only way the agent can honestly answer 'why can't I get a quote yet'.

**Rationale:** The spec demands both properties simultaneously: the agent 'changes reality only through an action present in available_actions' (filter) AND 'a commit that fails is surfaced, never narrated as success' with engine-owned reasons (typed rejection). Filter-only is not enforcement — today's executor provably executes anything, and the UI synthetic path plus any future GUI client must hit the same wall, or the swap test fails in reverse. The executor check must evaluate fresh state (not the turn snapshot) because a commit earlier in the same tool round legitimately changes legality. Prompt injection of blocked_actions with reasons is what converts blocks from agent failures into honest conversation: it is the mechanism behind the Gherkin scenarios on explaining blocks and on requires_identity routing.

**Depends on / interacts with:** commit-envelope, phase-model, tool-mapping

#### T1.D3 — What happens to SkillPack.allowedTools, WorkflowStep.allowedTools, and the Workflow/WorkflowSession/WorkflowStep tables?

- **Keep both as an additional intersection layer**: Engine computes legality; the final exposed set is legality ∩ workflow-step tools ∩ pack tools.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Defense-in-depth in theory. In practice both layers are dead today (WorkflowSession never created; recommendedSlugs hardcoded []) and provably drifted (pack seeds grant unregistered tools; intersection semantics already caused the historical zeroing bug documented in computeAllowedTools's own comment, skill-pack-loader.ts:160-167, and the advance-flow deadlock postmortem). Three sources of truth for one question guarantees future disagreement, and an intersection can silently veto an action the engine declared legal — the worst failure mode for a compliance-bearing state machine.
- **Demote to advisory**: Keep the columns and data; ignore them for gating; surface them only in debug/admin UIs.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Non-destructive and preserves the seeded step instructions as documentation. But advisory data that LOOKS like gating config (a column literally named allowedTools) is a standing trap — the codebase already demonstrates this failure mode with alwaysAllowed metadata and ALWAYS_ALLOWED_SET drifting from the real filter. Dead-but-present schema also keeps the per-turn eager join (turn-context.ts:95-107) and the dead types alive.
- **✅ Recommended — Retire both as gating sources; engine is sole authority**: Drop SkillPack.allowedTools semantics (packs remain prompt-content packs: domainGuidance/constraints, per PACK_WRITABLE_KEYS contract in skill-pack-loader.ts:33); delete Workflow/WorkflowSession/WorkflowStep/StepTransition models, seeds, the eager join in turn-context.ts, WorkflowSessionData, StateGroundingInput.workflowSession, and PipelineResult.transition. Any still-valuable agentInstructions prose from seed-workflows.ts migrates into phase-keyed prompt sections. DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS and alwaysAllowed are replaced by an 'exposedWhen: always' predicate in the legality table.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Loses the hypothetical future where multiple configurable workflows gate tools per step — but that future is exactly what the legality engine replaces with a better primitive (predicates over domain state instead of a parallel step machine that must be kept in sync with reality). Single source of truth for legality; packs keep a clean, already-enforced contract (prompt-content only); removes three inconsistent 'always allowed' definitions.

**Rationale:** Legality must derive from domain state (DNT signed, application complete, quote valid), not from which coaching pack happens to be active or which step row a parallel session machine sits on. The workflow-step machine is a second state machine that must mirror the domain to be correct — it never ran, and when something like it did influence gating (gate-recommended packs), its silent death took the funnel tools with it, which is precisely the class of failure a single-authority engine eliminates. The pack contract has already been narrowed once (PACK_WRITABLE_KEYS, prompt sections only) on the same reasoning; allowedTools is the analogous cleanup on the tool side.

**Depends on / interacts with:** phase-model, tool-mapping, testing-bdd

#### T1.D4 — How are 'Exposed when' conditions expressed?

- **✅ Recommended — Declarative per-action predicates over DerivedState**: A single table in the engine: { action, kind: 'read'|'commit', exposedWhen: (s: DerivedState) => boolean, blockedReason: (s) => { code: ReasonCode, params } | null }, where ReasonCode is a typed enum aligned with the catalog's consequence taxonomy (requires_consent, requires_identity, requires_disclosures, ...).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Predicates are code, not introspectable data — mitigated by a snapshot test that renders the full availability matrix for a set of canonical states (one per Gherkin Background) so reviewers see the machine as a table. In exchange: the catalog's 'Exposed when' column is literally predicate-shaped ('a quote exists', 'session finished', 'anonymous + funnel action needs identity'); conditions cross-cut phases and do not reduce to phase membership; and the same failed predicate yields both the blocked reason and the right consequence code, so exposure and rejection can never disagree on the 'why'.
- **Imperative per-phase functions**: switch(state.phase) returning a tool list per phase, mirroring getRequiredSectionsForPhase in phase-sections-map.ts.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Easy to read for the happy path and mirrors an existing pattern. But the catalog's conditions are mostly sub-phase ('DNT valid AND questionnaire incomplete', 'disclosures acknowledged AND quote not expired', 'last payment failed') — encoding them imperatively per phase duplicates facts DerivedState already holds, produces no per-action blocked reason without a second parallel structure, and pushes toward phase explosion (CONSENT_WITH_ACTIVE_SESSION, CONSENT_SESSION_FINISHED, ...) to express what a predicate states in one line.
- **Transition/availability matrix as data**: A (phase × action) boolean matrix, possibly DB-stored, consulted at runtime.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Fully introspectable and editable without deploys. But it can only express phase-membership conditions — every real guard in the catalog ('quote not expired', 'identified', 'session finished') still needs predicate escape hatches, ending with both a matrix AND predicates; DB-stored rules reintroduce exactly the config-drift failure mode of WorkflowStep.allowedTools (dead/stale rows silently gating a live funnel); and reasons still need a third structure.

**Rationale:** The unit of truth in the target spec is the per-tool 'Exposed when' condition, and those conditions are boolean expressions over domain facts, not phase labels. Predicates keep one row per action containing condition + reason + consequence mapping — the whole machine in one screenful — and each row maps 1:1 to Gherkin scenarios for TDD ('Given get_dnt_state reports no valid DNT... Then the questionnaire is blocked with reason requires_consent' becomes a direct assertion on computeLegality output). Phase remains an input fact predicates may reference, not the keying dimension, which keeps the engine correct even as the phase model evolves.

**Depends on / interacts with:** phase-model, questionnaire-consequences, testing-bdd, tool-mapping

#### T1.D5 — How does a commit's state change (e.g. advance_phase) feed back into exposure within the turn?

- **Next-turn only**: Keep today's shape: DerivedState and the tools array are fixed at turn start; commits change exposure starting from the next user message.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simplest concurrency story (one snapshot per turn). But it structurally re-creates the advance-flow deadlock: after sign_dnt succeeds, the questionnaire tools are still hidden for the rest of the turn, so the agent must stall or narrate an un-performable next step — the exact stall pathology already documented and fixed once. It also contradicts the catalog loop (commit → advance_phase → new available_actions) and the seeded UX where signing flows directly into the application.
- **✅ Recommended — Re-derive after every commit round**: After each tool round that executed at least one successful side-effecting tool, re-run deriveState + computeLegality, rebuild the tools array for the next LLM round (getToolsForLLM already caches per name-set), refresh the situational briefing by appending a system message with the new phase + available/blocked actions (reusing the existing injection pattern at orchestrator.ts:1280-1295, replacing the dead [Workflow Transition] block), and refresh toolContext (replacing the dead transitionOccurred trigger at orchestrator.ts:1298-1302).
  _Tradeoffs:_ A few extra DB reads per commit round (bounded by MAX_TOOL_ROUNDS=5; deriveState is the designed-cheap per-turn baseline and several handlers already call it per execution). Requires care that the appended system message stays small (actions + reasons, not the full state dump) to protect the token budget. In exchange, the agent always negotiates the next round against current legality, and a same-turn sign_dnt → start_application → first question sequence is legal end-to-end.
- **Re-derive only on advance_phase consequence**: Recompute exposure only when a commit's result carries consequence === 'advance_phase'.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Cheaper than per-round and targets the headline transition. But legality changes on non-advance consequences too: cascade_invalidate flips the questionnaire back to incomplete (generate_quote must disappear), re_rating/requires_confirmation alter what accept may follow, and an answer completing the questionnaire (today implicit in save_application_answer marking COMPLETED, application-handlers.ts:329-333) changes exposure without any phase advance. Keying the refresh on one consequence value couples the orchestrator to taxonomy details and silently misses the rest.

**Rationale:** Correctness of the agent-engine loop is the whole point: 'available_actions are computed by the engine and injected every turn' only holds if 'turn' means every decision point the model gets, including intra-turn tool rounds. The executor-level legality check (decision 2) already evaluates fresh state, so refusing to refresh exposure mid-turn buys no safety — it only guarantees the model's view is stale relative to the wall it will hit. Re-deriving per round (not per individual call) keeps cost bounded while making the canonical happy path — commit succeeds, phase advances, the newly legal next action is taken in the same breath — work without prompt hacks like the start-once-then-save directives that were needed last time.

**Depends on / interacts with:** commit-envelope, application-lifecycle, phase-model

### Risks

- The funnel-tools exposure gap is live NOW: with recommendedSlugs hardcoded [] (orchestrator.ts:597) and WorkflowSession never created, the agent cannot call sign_dnt/start_application/generate_quote/accept_quote in the standard chat path. Any rollout plan that assumes 'packs or workflow steps currently grant these' will mis-sequence the migration; the legality engine is not just an improvement, it is the fix for a probable regression introduced by the gate retirement (ce1b27d).
- TOCTOU between turn-start snapshot and execution: exposure computed at step 3 can be stale by round 2. If executor enforcement evaluates the turn snapshot instead of re-deriving fresh state, a same-turn commit chain (sign_dnt then start_application) gets wrongly rejected — or, inverted, a cancelled application stays actionable. Enforcement must re-derive; exposure may snapshot.
- DerivedState incompleteness fails silently: 'Exposed when' conditions needing facts that do not exist yet (DNT session state, isAnonymous identity, disclosure acknowledgment, quote expiry, payment status) will be written against approximations. Policy needed: commits whose predicate inputs are missing/undecidable must fail closed (blocked with a reason), while reads and escalate_to_human stay open — otherwise either compliance gates leak or the agent loses its escape hatch.
- deriveState failure fallback currently degrades to DISCOVERY sections (orchestrator.ts:441-446). Under a legality engine the same fallback would silently strip all funnel tools from a customer mid-application — a deadlock indistinguishable from a block. The error path needs an explicit degraded mode (reads + escalate only, with an honest 'temporary' reason), not a phase impersonation.
- Bypass surfaces must converge or the swap test fails in reverse: the UI synthetic tool path (action-adapter.ts) and any admin/replay/simulator entry points execute tools through the same executor — if executor enforcement lands after exposure filtering, GUIs can perform illegal transitions during the gap; if a separate GUI API ever calls handlers directly, it skips legality entirely.
- Dynamic per-turn tool lists break provider prompt-cache stability on the tool-definition block (today the 10-tool list is constant). Bounded (one list per distinct availability fingerprint, LRU-cached in getToolsForLLM) but should be measured; mitigation is keeping reads stably exposed and letting only commits vary.
- Deleting Workflow/WorkflowSession/WorkflowStep reaches further than the orchestrator: turn-context eager join, StateGroundingInput/loadStateGrounding, WorkflowSessionData, PipelineResult.transition, the [Workflow Transition] message branches (orchestrator.ts:896-909, 1280-1295), seeds, and possibly debug/admin readers. An incomplete sweep leaves half-dead types that future work will again mistake for live gating (the exact trap being removed).
- Two phase vocabularies (deriveState 6-phase vs phase.ts 3-phase feeding the compliance checker) must be unified before the legality engine keys on one — otherwise compliance prompting and action legality can disagree about where the conversation is (dependency on phase-model topic).
- Blocked-reason text reaches the customer through the agent: reason codes must be authored as customer-safe explanations (requires_consent, requires_identity), never internal diagnostics, or the agent will either leak internals or paraphrase-invent — the pathology the engine exists to prevent.
- The catalog's idempotency invariant (double-submit of a commit applies once) is NOT delivered by the legality engine — exposure/enforcement does not deduplicate accept_quote retries. It must be explicitly owned by the commit envelope, or the gap will be wrongly assumed covered (dependency on commit-envelope topic).

---

## T2. Uniform commit envelope: consequence taxonomy, idempotency, concurrency

> Topic key: `commit-envelope`

### Current state (code-grounded)

ENVELOPE TODAY. All tools return `ToolResult { success: boolean; data?; error?: string; message?; uiAction?; confirmation? }` (lib/tools/types.ts:49-68). There is NO consequence concept anywhere in lib/ (grep for consequence|requires_confirmation|advance_phase|cascade matches only a Stripe comment in lib/payments/providers/stripe.ts:81). Every failure class — business rejection, missing precondition, validation error, permission denial, circuit-open, timeout, unknown tool — collapses to `{success:false, error:<prose string>}` (lib/tools/executor.ts:74-191); the LLM cannot distinguish "blocked by rule" from "infra failure". Handlers' catch blocks return `error: String(error)` raw Prisma/JS errors (e.g. lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:252,440).

RESULT FLOW. Tool calls go through executeToolWithPipeline (lib/tools/pipeline.ts — thin wrapper; workflow gate retired) → executeTool (lib/tools/executor.ts: validate → permission → cache → circuit breaker → 15s timeout). The orchestrator (lib/chat/orchestrator.ts) partitions calls into readOnly (parallel, :1098-1177) and writing (sequential, :1179-1258). LLM sees JSON of {success, data, error, message, confirmation} via serializeToolResultForModel (lib/chat/tool-result-serializer.ts); `uiAction` is stripped from the LLM and emitted as SSE `ui_action` (orchestrator.ts:873-878, 1267-1272); `confirmation` drives system-rendered "✓" lines and the anti-renarration validator validateSideEffectClaims (orchestrator.ts:1311-1338). Full results are persisted per-turn via debug:tool_result events (TurnDebug). DerivedState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts: 6-phase model + prose nextBestAction) is computed once per turn (orchestrator.ts:437) and injected as a prompt section (lib/chat/phase-sections-map.ts:37) — the closest thing to engine-injected state; there is no available_actions/blocked_actions computation.

AD-HOC COMMIT SHAPES (catalog of current returns): sign_dnt (dnt-handlers.ts:273-317) → {signed, signedAt, validUntil}; consent refusal is a prose error; NOT idempotent — re-call re-signs and extends validity another 365d with no already-signed guard. start_application (application-handlers.ts:29-121) → {alreadyExists, applicationId} if an OPEN app exists (partial natural-key idempotency), but if the existing app is COMPLETED it attempts create → P2002 on Application.conversationId @unique (schema.prisma:492) → raw error. save_application_answer → {answerSaved, isComplete?, escalated?, readyForQuote?, nextQuestion, progress}; escalation ("referred") is success:true+escalated:true; flagsForReview accumulated via read-modify-write JSON (race-prone, :208-221). set_answer (set-answer-handlers.ts) → {state: DerivedState} + save confirmation — the only handler returning fresh state; pure upsert, no cascade logic. change_selection (change-selection-handlers.ts) → {selectionChanged, quoteExpired, ...} + no-op detection; quote-expire + answer upserts + app update are separate awaits. generate_quote (quote-handlers.ts:19-255) → rich quote data + show_quote uiAction; always prisma.quote.create (:189) against Quote.applicationId @unique (schema.prisma:516); no referred path; consent failure is prose error. accept_quote (:316-443) → has confirmAcceptance flag (existing one-shot confirmation idiom, like sign_dnt's confirmSignature); guards status===DRAFT and expiry; then THREE non-transactional writes (quote→ACCEPTED, Policy create PENDING_SUBMISSION — before payment, conversation→COMPLETED). modify_quote (:449-530) → 4 sequential writes (expire quote, reset application, deleteMany answers, next question), no transaction. cancel_application (application-handlers.ts:496-528) sets status COMPLETED — no CANCELLED status; terminal states conflated. initiate_payment (payment-handlers.ts) creates a NEW provider PaymentIntent + NEW Payment row on every call; Payment has no unique constraint (only an index on providerPaymentId, schema.prisma:581). check_bd_eligibility (bd-handlers.ts) is a commit disguised as a read — mutates Application.includesAddon=false on rejection. record_gdpr_consent / acknowledge_ai_disclosure (registry.ts:1042-1089) timestamp-overwrite (naturally idempotent). set_candidate_product (candidate-handlers.ts:54-69) has explicit unchanged detection.

IDEMPOTENCY PRECEDENT. Exactly one CAS exists in the repo: runPostPaymentFlow (lib/payments/post-payment.ts:28-36) does `payment.updateMany({where:{id,status:'PENDING'}, data:{status:'COMPLETED'}})` — "only first caller wins" — explicitly designed for concurrent webhook+confirm calls. Natural keys in schema: Application.conversationId, Quote.applicationId, Policy.quoteId all @unique; Answer @@unique([questionId, conversationId]).

CONCURRENCY. Zero `prisma.$transaction` calls in lib/ (grep verified). No version columns on Conversation/Application/Quote (schema.prisma:300-536). The chat route's only guard is an in-memory, per-process Map permitting up to 3 CONCURRENT turns per conversation (app/api/chat/route.ts:39-61) — i.e., concurrency is allowed, not serialized. GUI buttons go through the same pipeline as synthetic tool calls (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts; route `action` param → orchestrator.ts:798-893), so a GUI click and an agent commit can interleave as separate turns with no serialization. Datasource is PostgreSQL (schema.prisma:6-8), so advisory locks are available but unused. Error conventions: lib/errors/types.ts defines only CircuitOpenError/TimeoutError; no error-code envelope exists.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** Gap #8: "double start_dnt/cancel return errors" — i.e., a repeated start_dnt call is reported as an error.
  **Correction:** Only the cancel half is true. A repeated start_dnt_questionnaire call never returns an error: if all DNT questions are answered it returns success:true with data.alreadyComplete:true ('All DNT questions have already been answered. Ready for signature.'); otherwise it simply returns success with the next unanswered question. The handler has no duplicate-call guard at all — it is effectively a read (getNextQuestion) and is naturally replay-tolerant. Double cancel_application does return an error ('No active application found to cancel.', application-handlers.ts:504-508), and double accept_quote does return 'Quote is not in DRAFT status' (quote-handlers.ts:339-341). _(lib/tools/handlers/dnt-handlers.ts:70-121 (alreadyComplete success branch at :75-81; no error path for repeat calls); lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:504-508; lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:339-341)_
- **Claim:** set_answer (set-answer-handlers.ts) → {state: DerivedState} + save confirmation — "the only handler returning fresh state".
  **Correction:** Not the only handler: get_current_state (getStateHandler in lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.ts) also calls deriveState and returns {data: {state}}. set_answer is the only WRITE/commit handler that returns fresh DerivedState; get_current_state is a read tool that returns the same shape. _(lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.ts:14-21 (const state = await deriveState(...); return { success: true, data: { state }, ... }); lib/tools/handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts:103-107)_
- **Claim:** modify_quote (:449-530) → "4 sequential writes (expire quote, reset application, deleteMany answers, next question), no transaction" (also stated as "modify_quote (4 writes)" in gaps and "modify_quote's 4 tables" in DP5).
  **Correction:** modify_quote performs 3 writes, not 4: quote.update→EXPIRED (:467-470), application.update reset (:473-482), answer.deleteMany (:491-497). The fourth listed step, 'next question', is getNextQuestion (:500) — a read, not a write. Three tables are written (Quote, Application, Answer). The 'no transaction' and line-range (:449-530) parts are correct. _(lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:467-500 (writes at 467, 473, 491; read-only getNextQuestion at 500))_

### Gaps

- No consequence taxonomy exists anywhere in the codebase — none of the 14 catalog values is representable; success:false prose strings conflate business rejection (rejected), precondition blocks (requires_consent/identity/disclosures), validation errors, and infrastructure failures (timeout/circuit-open), so the agent cannot decide retry-vs-surface-vs-escalate deterministically.
- No machine-readable advance_phase signal: phase changes happen implicitly via DB writes and are only re-derived next turn by deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts); within a multi-tool turn the LLM has no authoritative signal that the phase moved.
- requires_confirmation is approximated by boolean args (accept_quote.confirmAcceptance, sign_dnt.confirmSignature) that the model itself supplies — nothing prevents the LLM from passing true on the first call without asking the user, and nothing binds the confirmation to the state that was previewed (TOCTOU: terms can change between preview and confirm; the feature backlog explicitly lists 'price/terms changed between view and accept').
- No transactions: every multi-write commit is non-atomic — accept_quote (3 writes incl. Policy creation), modify_quote (4 writes), switch_product (3), change_selection (N), start_application (create + N answer upserts). A crash or concurrent interleave mid-commit leaves partial state (e.g. quote ACCEPTED but no Policy).
- initiate_payment is unboundedly non-idempotent: each call mints a new provider PaymentIntent and a new PENDING Payment row; Payment has no unique constraint (schema.prisma:563-582), enabling double charge on double-submit. The only idempotency in the payment chain is downstream (runPostPaymentFlow CAS).
- sign_dnt has no already-signed guard — re-signing silently extends dntValidUntil by another 365 days (compliance-relevant document re-dated without a new needs analysis).
- Quote regeneration deadlock: change_selection/modify_quote/switch_product expire a quote by setting status=EXPIRED but keep the row; generate_quote then does quote.create against Quote.applicationId @unique → P2002 raw error. The schema's 1:1 contradicts the expire-and-regenerate flows the handlers implement (also a quote-lifecycle topic issue, but it surfaces as a broken 're_rating' consequence).
- Idempotent replays are reported as errors, not as the original outcome: double accept_quote returns 'Quote is not in DRAFT status', double start_dnt/cancel return errors — violating the Gherkin scenario 'A committing action is idempotent on double-submit' which requires apply-once semantics, not error-on-second.
- check_bd_eligibility mutates Application.includesAddon despite being presented as a check — a hidden eligibility_recheck consequence invisible to the envelope, the UI, and the side-effect claim validator (it has no sideEffect category and returns no confirmation).
- cancel_application records cancellation as status COMPLETED — terminal consequences (terminal vs applied completion) are indistinguishable in data, blocking any honest 'terminal' consequence and corrupting downstream analytics/derived phase.
- Application.flagsForReview is accumulated via read-modify-write on a JSON column (application-handlers.ts:208-250) — concurrent answers can silently drop flags (underwriting-relevant data loss).
- The 3-concurrent-turns guard is in-memory and per-process (app/api/chat/route.ts:39) — it neither serializes commits nor survives multi-instance deployment; GUI synthetic actions and agent turns interleave with no ordering guarantee, despite the contract scenario 'Concurrent GUI and agent actions stay consistent'.

### Decision points

#### T2.D1 — What shape should the uniform CommitResult envelope take, and how does the 14-value catalog taxonomy map onto it?

- **Single consequence enum field**: Add `consequence: <one of the 14 catalog values>` + `reason?` to ToolResult and have every commit handler set exactly one value, mirroring the catalog table literally.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Faithful to the catalog text but lossy: the taxonomy values are not mutually exclusive — modify_answer can simultaneously be re_rating AND cascade_invalidate; accept_quote is applied AND advance_phase; the catalog itself writes chains like 'requires_confirmation → terminal'. A single enum forces arbitrary priority choices, and the LLM/UI lose information the BDD scenarios assert on (the Scenario Outline expects specific consequences per change type, several of which co-occur).
- **✅ Recommended — Layered discriminated union: outcome + effects[] + requirement**: CommitResult = { outcome: 'applied' | 'blocked' | 'rejected' | 'referred'; requirement?: 'confirmation' | 'identity' | 'consent' | 'disclosures' (only when outcome='blocked'); effects: Array<'re_rating' | 'cascade_invalidate' | 'cascade_expand' | 'questions_removed' | 'eligibility_recheck' | 'advance_phase' | 'terminal'> (only when outcome='applied'); reason?: { code: string; detail: string }; data: Record<string, unknown>; state: DerivedState }. The 14 catalog values are preserved exactly as vocabulary: 4 become outcomes, 4 become requirements under blocked, 7 become composable effects (applied maps to outcome 'applied' with empty effects). Strict TS union with exhaustiveness checks; serializer emits it verbatim to the LLM; UI consumes outcome/effects to drive confirmations and uiActions.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Type-safe and exhaustive (a missing effect is a compile/test failure, not a silent omission); composable consequences match reality (one commit, several downstream truths); reason gains a machine-readable code separating business rejection from infra failure; bundling fresh DerivedState in every commit (extending the set_answer precedent) eliminates the agent narrating stale phase. Slightly diverges from the catalog's flat table — but the catalog is declared a conceptual target, and every value survives verbatim as vocabulary so the Gherkin assertions still bind.
- **Status quo extended per-handler**: Keep ToolResult as-is and let each handler encode its consequence semantics inside data (escalated:true, quoteExpired:true, selectionChanged:false...), documenting conventions.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Zero structural change but perpetuates exactly the problem under repair: 17 handler files each invent fields, the LLM must memorize per-tool conventions, the side-effect validator and BDD suite cannot assert uniformly, and 'rejected with reason' remains indistinguishable from a timeout.

**Rationale:** Correctness over literalism: the taxonomy values demonstrably co-occur (re_rating + cascade_invalidate on a rated answer change; applied + advance_phase on set_application/generate_quote/accept_quote), so a single-value enum cannot be a truthful contract and would force handlers to drop consequences the BDD spec asserts on. A discriminated union gives exhaustive compile-time handling for the agent-facing serializer and the UI, makes 'blocked' (precondition unmet, retry after satisfying requirement) structurally distinct from 'rejected' (illegal move, state unchanged) — a distinction the engine's blocked_actions computation (legality-engine topic) needs anyway — and embeds fresh DerivedState so the swap test holds: a GUI client receives the same machine-readable transition the agent does. The envelope should live in the domain layer (e.g. lib/domain/commit.ts) and be adapted to ToolResult at the tool boundary, not defined in lib/tools — tools are clients of the engine, not its type authority.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, tool-mapping, questionnaire-consequences, phase-model, testing-bdd

#### T2.D2 — Where is the envelope produced and enforced — who guarantees that every commit actually returns a CommitResult?

- **Per-handler adoption**: Refactor each of the ~17 committing handlers to construct and return the new envelope directly; ToolHandler signature changes to Promise<CommitResult> for commits.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Smallest conceptual change but the guarantee is conventional, not structural: nothing stops the next handler from returning success:false prose; cross-cutting concerns (locking, idempotent replay, state re-derivation, audit) get copy-pasted 17 times and drift — exactly how today's ad-hoc shapes arose.
- **✅ Recommended — Central commit gateway in the domain layer**: Introduce a single commit entry point (e.g. lib/domain/commands/execute.ts): commands are pure-ish functions over a transaction handle returning a typed CommitResult; the gateway uniformly opens the transaction, takes the per-conversation lock, runs legality preconditions, executes the command, re-derives state, and shapes the envelope. Tool handlers shrink to arg-translation + gateway call; GUI/API routes call the identical gateway (swap test by construction).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Structural guarantee: a commit cannot exist without an envelope, a transaction, or a lock because the gateway is the only path to one; concerns are implemented once and property-tested once; the LLM tool layer and a future REST/GUI layer become equal clients. Couples all commits to one chokepoint — mitigated by keeping commands as plain data-in/data-out functions so they remain individually unit-testable.
- **Serializer-level adaptation**: Keep handlers untouched; infer the consequence in serializeToolResultForModel / the orchestrator by pattern-matching on data fields (escalated→referred, quoteExpired→re_rating...).
  _Tradeoffs:_ No handler changes, but the consequence becomes a heuristic over ad-hoc fields rather than a domain decision — the inference layer must be updated in lockstep with every handler, misclassification is silent, and the UI/DB never see the real consequence (only the LLM-facing string does). Violates 'the engine decides every consequence'.

**Rationale:** The catalog's engine invariants ('every commit returns a consequence', 'a GUI client could call the identical operations') are properties of a boundary, not of 17 independently-written functions. A gateway makes the invariants structural: transaction + lock + legality check + envelope are unskippable, testable as one property suite, and shared verbatim with non-agent clients — which is the literal swap test. It also gives the legality engine (separate topic) its natural enforcement point: available/blocked computation and commit validation read the same precondition predicates, eliminating today's duplicated inline gating (DNT validity re-checked ad hoc in start_application, generate_quote, etc.).

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, tool-mapping, testing-bdd, application-lifecycle

#### T2.D3 — How do requires_confirmation two-step commits work for an LLM agent (and a GUI) — where does the pending confirmation live and what makes the confirm trustworthy?

- **Stateless confirm flag (extend the current idiom)**: First call without confirm returns outcome blocked/requirement confirmation plus a preview in data; the same tool is re-called with confirm:true. Pending state lives only in the conversation transcript. This generalizes today's accept_quote.confirmAcceptance / sign_dnt.confirmSignature.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simple, already familiar to the model, no server state. But the confirmer is the same untrusted client being constrained: the LLM can pass confirm:true on the first call (nothing in code prevents this today), and nothing binds the confirmation to what was previewed — if state changes between preview and confirm (re-rating, expiry, GUI edit in parallel) the engine applies terms the user never saw.
- **Server-side pending-commit record**: First call writes a PendingCommit row {id, conversationId, tool, argsHash, preview, expiresAt}; a generic confirm_commit(pendingId) tool applies it. The engine refuses to apply if the row expired or underlying state changed.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Fully auditable and engine-owned, supports GUI confirm buttons naturally. But introduces a second mutable source of truth with its own lifecycle (expiry sweeps, orphan cleanup, exactly-one-active semantics) and a new generic tool the legality engine must gate; the integrity it buys — binding confirm to previewed state — is achievable without storage.
- **✅ Recommended — Signed state-fingerprint confirm token (stateless, verifiable)**: The blocked response carries confirmToken = HMAC(serverSecret, conversationId | toolName | canonicalArgs | stateVersion) where stateVersion is the version/updatedAt of the entity being committed (e.g. quote.updatedAt). Re-calling the same tool with {confirm: true, confirmToken} applies only if the recomputed fingerprint matches — i.e. the args and the underlying state are exactly what was previewed. Token issuance/redemption is recorded in the existing TurnDebug stream for audit.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Closes both holes of the flag approach: the model cannot mint a valid token without first receiving the preview (forced two-step), and a state change between preview and confirm invalidates the token deterministically (engine re-issues with the new terms — directly implementing the 'price/terms changed between view and accept' backlog scenario). No new storage or lifecycle; pure function, trivially property-testable. Cost: the engine must define a stateVersion per confirmable entity, which optimistic-versioning (concurrency DP) provides anyway; a GUI confirm button simply round-trips the same token.

**Rationale:** The decisive requirement is that confirmation be verifiable against the previewed state, not merely asserted by the client — 'never trust the client' applies doubly when the client is an LLM that today can and does set confirmAcceptance:true unprompted. The fingerprint token achieves engine-enforced two-step semantics and TOCTOU protection as a pure function over state the concurrency design already versions, with the audit trail riding the existing TurnDebug persistence; a PendingCommit table adds mutable lifecycle state without adding integrity, and the bare flag adds neither. The blocked/requirement:'confirmation' envelope response should include both the human-readable preview (for the agent to relay) and the token, so one response serves agent and GUI identically.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, quote-lifecycle, dnt-sessions, application-lifecycle, payments

#### T2.D4 — What is the idempotency strategy for dangerous double-submits (sign_dnt, accept_quote, initiate_payment, start_application, generate_quote)?

- **✅ Recommended — Natural-key CAS + DB constraints, replay returns original outcome**: Every state-transition commit is an atomic compare-and-swap on its natural key inside the commit transaction (extending the runPostPaymentFlow precedent at lib/payments/post-payment.ts:28-36): accept_quote = updateMany({id, status:'DRAFT'}→ACCEPTED; count 0 → look up actual state and return the ORIGINAL consequence (applied/advance_phase, idempotentReplay:true) instead of an error; sign_dnt = guarded on dntSignedAt null-or-expired; start_application keyed on Application.conversationId @unique with create-or-return-existing; generate_quote keyed on one-active-quote-per-application. Payment gets a missing natural key added: partial unique index (policyId) WHERE status='PENDING' so at most one open payment exists, and the Payment.id is forwarded as the provider idempotency key (Stripe supports this natively) so even a re-fired createPaymentIntent cannot double-charge.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Idempotency is enforced where the truth lives (the DB), works identically for agent, GUI, and webhook callers, requires no client cooperation, and satisfies the Gherkin 'applies it once / no duplicate effect' scenario with apply-once-then-replay semantics rather than today's error-on-second. Requires defining the natural key per commit — which is exactly the state-machine modeling the legality engine needs anyway.
- **Explicit client-supplied idempotency keys**: Every commit takes an idempotencyKey; the engine stores key→envelope and replays the stored envelope on repeat.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Uniform and provider-style, but the client here is an LLM: a model retry is a fresh tool_call with fresh arguments, so it will mint a fresh key precisely when deduplication matters most — the mechanism protects against the one failure mode (same-key resend) that LLM agents don't exhibit, while missing the one they do (semantically-duplicate calls). Also adds a stored-response table whose contents can diverge from real state.
- **Idempotency keys only, no schema constraints**: Rely purely on a key/result store, leave Payment and Quote schemas as-is.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Leaves the double-charge window structurally open (two PENDING Payment rows remain legal in the schema) and keeps the quote-regeneration P2002 failure; integrity by convention instead of by constraint.

**Rationale:** Zeno's commits are state-machine transitions, and state machines carry their own idempotency keys: the (entity, from-state) pair. CAS on that pair inside a transaction is the only mechanism that is simultaneously client-agnostic (agent, GUI button, Stripe webhook all collide safely — proven in-repo by runPostPaymentFlow), constraint-backed (unique indexes make duplicates unrepresentable, not just unlikely), and able to honor the spec's apply-once semantics by returning the original consequence on replay instead of a confusing error the agent then has to interpret. The payment boundary additionally forwards Payment.id as the provider idempotency key because money crosses a system boundary where our transaction cannot reach. Resolving this DP requires fixing the Quote 1:1 modeling (expired quote rows currently block regeneration via Quote.applicationId @unique — either applicationId becomes non-unique with a partial unique index on active status, or expired quotes are superseded in place), which is owned by quote-lifecycle.

**Depends on / interacts with:** payments, quote-lifecycle, dnt-sessions, application-lifecycle, legality-engine

#### T2.D5 — How are concurrent commits serialized when the GUI and the agent act in the same conversation (and across multiple server instances)?

- **✅ Recommended — Per-conversation Postgres advisory lock around each commit transaction**: Every commit (via the gateway) opens a prisma.$transaction whose first statement is pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext(conversationId)); preconditions are re-checked inside the lock; the lock releases automatically at commit/rollback. Reads (R-tools, deriveState) never take the lock. The in-memory 3-per-conversation route counter is kept only as backpressure.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Serializes exactly the dangerous unit — commits within one conversation funnel — across processes and instances (DB-backed, unlike the current in-memory map), while leaving talk and reads fully concurrent ('talk is free, commits are constrained' made literal). Multi-row commits (accept_quote's quote+policy+conversation writes, modify_quote's 4 tables) become atomic-and-serialized without per-row reasoning. Requires Postgres (already the datasource) and a raw SQL statement inside the transaction; lock granularity is the whole conversation, so two truly-independent commits in one conversation queue — acceptable because the conversation IS the funnel aggregate today (Application/Answers/Quote all hang off conversationId).
- **Optimistic versioning on Conversation/Application/Quote**: Add version Int columns; every commit does updateMany({id, version:n}, {.., version:n+1}) and returns outcome 'rejected'/stale_state on count 0, letting the caller re-read and retry.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No locks, scales reads/writes independently, and the version column doubles as the stateVersion the confirm-token needs. But it protects single rows, not invariants spanning rows: accept_quote's three-table write cannot be expressed as one CAS, so partial application remains possible without a transaction anyway; and it externalizes retry loops onto every client including the LLM, which handles 'stale, please retry' badly (risk of narrating failure or looping).
- **Serialize whole turns per conversation**: Reduce MAX_CONCURRENT_PER_CONVERSATION to 1 backed by a distributed lock, so a GUI action waits for the agent's turn to finish.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Trivially correct but conflates conversation (long, LLM-latency-bound, mostly reads) with commits (milliseconds): a user clicking a GUI button mid-stream would block for the whole turn, and read-only turns get serialized for no integrity benefit. Punishes exactly the concurrency the architecture wants to allow.
- **Transactions with in-tx CAS only, no explicit lock**: Wrap each commit in prisma.$transaction with state-guard re-checks and rely on unique constraints to break races.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Atomicity yes, serialization no: two concurrent accept_quotes both pass the DRAFT read, one loses at the Policy.quoteId unique constraint and surfaces a P2002-shaped failure that the envelope must then launder into 'idempotent replay'. Workable but every race resolves via constraint-violation-as-control-flow, which is harder to reason about and to test than ordered execution.

**Rationale:** The Gherkin contract is explicit: 'the engine serialises them and the resulting state is consistent'. Serialization must therefore be an engine property, and it must hold across processes — the current in-memory counter is neither (it allows 3 concurrent turns and evaporates under multi-instance deployment). An advisory xact lock keyed on the conversation gives whole-aggregate mutual exclusion with automatic release, makes the in-lock precondition re-check sufficient for correctness (the CAS patterns from the idempotency DP then handle replay semantics, not races), and matches the aggregate boundary of the data model where everything funnel-related is conversation-scoped. Optimistic version columns are still worth adding — not as the serialization mechanism but as the stateVersion feeding the confirm-token fingerprint — so options 1 and 2 compose rather than compete; what is rejected is versioning as the sole mechanism. When the CustomerProfile SSOT direction moves data to customer scope, the lock key extends to (customerId) for customer-scoped commits like identify_customer — the gateway centralization (DP2) makes that a one-line policy.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, payments, application-lifecycle, identity, dnt-sessions

### Risks

- Double-charge window exists today: initiate_payment creates a new PaymentIntent + PENDING Payment row on every call with no unique constraint and no provider idempotency key (lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts; schema.prisma:563-582) — an agent retry or impatient GUI click can present two live checkout sessions for the same policy.
- accept_quote's three non-transactional writes create Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION) BEFORE payment and mark the Conversation COMPLETED; a mid-sequence failure leaves an ACCEPTED quote with no policy, or a policy on a conversation still ACTIVE — and the envelope work will inherit this ordering unless the payments/policy-post-sale topics resolve who creates the Policy and when.
- Quote regeneration P2002 deadlock: every expire-then-regenerate path (change_selection, modify_quote, switch_product → generate_quote) collides with Quote.applicationId @unique because expired rows are retained and generate_quote always creates (quote-handlers.ts:189); the re_rating consequence is structurally broken until the quote-lifecycle schema decision lands.
- Taxonomy fidelity risk: if implementation flattens to a single consequence enum to match the catalog table literally, co-occurring consequences (re_rating + cascade_invalidate) will be silently dropped and the BDD Scenario Outline for modify_answer becomes untestable — the envelope union must be settled BEFORE questionnaire-consequences implements cascade logic, or handlers will bake in lossy single values.
- LLM behavioral regression: switching from prose error strings to structured outcome/effects changes what the model reads every turn; prior project history (advance-flow deadlock) shows unit-green ≠ agent-working — the new envelope needs scripted live-sim verification of agent reactions to each outcome class (blocked vs rejected vs idempotent replay), not just serializer unit tests.
- Confirm-token TOCTOU protection depends on a stable stateVersion; if versioning is added only to some entities, confirmable commits on unversioned entities (e.g. sign_dnt against Conversation.dntSignedAt) silently lose the binding and regress to the trust-the-flag model.
- Advisory locks held across slow work are a liveness hazard: the commit transaction must contain only DB work — provider calls like createPaymentIntent (network, seconds) must happen outside the lock with a two-phase record-then-confirm pattern, otherwise one stuck Stripe call blocks every commit in the conversation for up to the 15s tool timeout.
- Idempotent-replay semantics can mask real bugs if over-applied: returning 'applied' for a second sign_dnt is correct, but returning 'applied' when the agent meant to sign a DIFFERENT session (dnt-sessions topic introduces session ids) would hide a targeting error — replay detection must key on the full natural key including the session/entity id, not just the verb.
- The in-memory route guard (3 concurrent turns) currently gives a false sense of safety in dev (single process) that disappears in any multi-instance deployment — concurrency fixes must be DB-backed and tested with genuinely parallel processes, or the GUI+agent consistency scenario will pass locally and fail in production.

---

## T3. DNT as a real entity: customer-scoped DNT + session model (new/update)

> Topic key: `dnt-sessions`

### Current state (code-grounded)

DNT today is conversation-scoped metadata plus shared questionnaire rows; no DNT entity, session, or dedicated answer store exists (verified absent from prisma/schema.prisma — no Dnt/DntSession/DntAnswer models).

TOOLS (4, not 9): registered in lib/tools/registry.ts:648-719. check_dnt_status (alwaysAllowed, read) accepts an insuranceType arg that the handler never reads. start_dnt_questionnaire, save_dnt_answer, sign_dnt are pack-gated (granted by sales + questionnaire packs in prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts ~lines 163-230). The UI adapter routes button actions to the same 4 tools (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:55-63, 100-119).

HANDLERS (lib/tools/handlers/dnt-handlers.ts): check_dnt_status computes progress over QuestionGroup.phase='dnt' groups (resolveGroupCodes/resolveActiveProductId in lib/engines/question-groups.ts) and reads Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil (lines 36-43). start_dnt_questionnaire creates NO entity — "starting" is just returning the first unanswered question (lines 70-121); there is nothing to resume, no active-session invariant, no preview-vs-start distinction. save_dnt_answer upserts a conversation-scoped Answer row keyed @@unique([questionId, conversationId]) (prisma/schema.prisma:473-484; handler lines 177-193) with no session. sign_dnt (lines 273-317) takes confirmSignature+gdprConsent booleans, requires 100% progress, then stamps Conversation.dntSignedAt and dntValidUntil = now+365d hardcoded (lines 295-301). The gdprConsent boolean is checked and then DISCARDED — no consent record is persisted by sign_dnt; there is no ai_disclosure input at all.

SCHEMA: Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil at prisma/schema.prisma:307-308 (added by migration 20260528000000_add-group-phase-and-dnt-columns). Conversation.customerId is mandatory (line 302) and Customer.isAnonymous defaults true (line 279) — every conversation has a Customer row, but DNT signing has no identity gate today. Consent fields live on Customer (gdprConsentAt/gdprConsentScope/aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt, lines 285-287), written by the separate alwaysAllowed tools record_gdpr_consent and acknowledge_ai_disclosure (lib/tools/registry.ts:1042-1117). withdraw_consent and identify_customer do NOT exist anywhere in lib/ (verified by grep).

QUESTIONS (prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts): 6 DNT groups, 26 questions — dnt_consent (3 IDD consents: consultation, marketing, electronic communication), dnt_general (6, incl. DNT_CNP), dnt_life_type (1: DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE), dnt_life_financial (11), dnt_life_investment (3), dnt_sustainability (2). DNT is NOT flat today: DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_PREFERENCE branches on DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_IMPORTANCE via parentQuestionCode/showWhenValue (lines 557-569). Worse, the life_financial/investment/sustainability group descriptions claim conditionality on DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE but NO mechanism enforces it — the engine asks all 26 questions to everyone, including investment risk questions to simple-protection customers.

ENGINE: lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.ts — pure functions (shouldShowQuestion, validateAnswer) plus DB wrappers getNextQuestion/calculateProgress keyed by (groupCodes, conversationId); shared across DNT, application, and BD medical flows.

DOWNSTREAM READERS of conversation-scoped DNT state: deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:109-113 reads the stamps; line 46 makes phase CONSENT require customer.gdprConsentAt AND conversation.dntSignedAt; line 58 nextBestAction says "record_gdpr_consent and sign_dnt"); start_application re-checks dntSignedAt (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:35-40); quote-time compliance verifyConsents re-checks the stamps + the 3 dnt_consent Answer rows (lib/compliance/consent-check.ts:48-57); the IDD suitability PDF reads DNT answers via policy→quote→application→conversation.answers (lib/compliance/dnt-report.ts:83-105).

The CustomerProfile-SSOT spec referenced as the strategic direction is NOT present in the repo docs (searched docs/**) — it exists only as prior session context.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** "TOOLS (4, not 9): registered in lib/tools/registry.ts:648-719" — i.e., the current tool surface that touches DNT consists of exactly the 4 tools check_dnt_status, start_dnt_questionnaire, save_dnt_answer, sign_dnt.
  **Correction:** There is a fifth registered tool that writes and edits DNT answers: set_answer (lib/tools/registry.ts:762-782), described as 'Answer any question by its code, within the active DNT or application groups. Supports editing previously answered questions.' Its handler (lib/tools/handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts:18-49) resolves the question code via resolveGroupCodes(productId, 'dnt') plus the application codes (lines 25-30) and upserts the same conversation-scoped Answer row (lines 45-49). The 4 dedicated DNT tools at registry.ts:648-719 are correctly identified, but the claim of a 4-tool DNT surface is incomplete — and it is load-bearing for the report's 'write vs modify' analysis, since a generic modify-by-code path for DNT answers already exists today. _(lib/tools/registry.ts:762-782; lib/tools/handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts:25-30, 45-49)_
- **Claim:** "The UI adapter routes button actions to the same 4 tools (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:55-63, 100-119)."
  **Correction:** The adapter routes button actions to only 3 of the 4 DNT tools: answer_question (groupType 'dnt') → save_dnt_answer (lines 55-63), and the legacy mappings start_dnt → start_dnt_questionnaire, answer_dnt → save_dnt_answer, sign_dnt → sign_dnt (lines 100-119). check_dnt_status has no action mapping anywhere in the file (grep for 'check_dnt_status' in lib/chat/action-adapter.ts returns no matches). _(lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:55-63, 100-119 (no check_dnt_status occurrence in the file))_
- **Claim:** "the engine asks all 26 questions to everyone, including investment risk questions to simple-protection customers" (current_state) and "every customer is asked all 26 questions" (gaps).
  **Correction:** Overstated by one question: DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_PREFERENCE is conditionally visible (parentQuestionCode: 'DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_IMPORTANCE', showWhenValue: 'somewhat,quite_important,very_important' at prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts:564-565), and shouldShowQuestion (lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.ts:68-104) hides it — getNextQuestion skips hidden questions and excludes them from progress (lines 447-451). So a customer answering 'not_necessary' is asked 25 questions, not 26. The substantive point IS verified: no DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE gating exists — line 564 is the only parentQuestionCode in the entire seed file, so all 11 dnt_life_financial and 3 dnt_life_investment questions are unconditional and are asked to simple-protection customers, despite group descriptions claiming subtype conditionality (seed-questions.ts:325, 479, 536). _(prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts:556-569 (sole conditional question); lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.ts:68-104, 441-451)_
- **Claim:** "Answer table does double duty for DNT + underwriting + BD medical, distinguished only by group phase."
  **Correction:** Imprecise: only the DNT-vs-rest split is a phase distinction. The bd_medical group has phase: 'application' (prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts:667), the same phase as the application group (line 585) — confirmed by the migration backfill (prisma/migrations/20260528000000_add-group-phase-and-dnt-columns/migration.sql: UPDATE "QuestionGroup" SET "phase" = 'application' WHERE "code" IN ('application', 'bd_medical')). Underwriting vs BD-medical answers are distinguished by group code, not phase. The core point (one shared Answer table, separable only via the question's group metadata) holds. _(prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts:585, 667; prisma/migrations/20260528000000_add-group-phase-and-dnt-columns/migration.sql)_

### Gaps

- No DNT entity: signing is two timestamps on Conversation (prisma/schema.prisma:307-308). Validity dies with the conversation — a returning customer must redo the DNT in every new conversation, contradicting the ~365-day customer-scoped validity in the catalog.
- No session model at all: no new/update session types, no one-active-session invariant, no resume across conversations, no pre-fill of an expired DNT from prior answers, no started_at/answered-count session details.
- No products_covered: DNT validity is product-blind. check_dnt_status accepts insuranceType but the handler ignores it (lib/tools/registry.ts:653 vs lib/tools/handlers/dnt-handlers.ts:27-64), so get_dnt_state cannot answer 'does this DNT cover this application's product type'.
- sign_dnt discards its consent inputs: gdprConsent is validated then thrown away (dnt-handlers.ts:277-301); no ai_disclosure parameter exists; no immutable consent evidence is attached to the signed DNT. Customer.gdprConsentAt is only set by the separate record_gdpr_consent tool, so the engine's CONSENT gate (derive-state.ts:46) can be satisfied or not independently of an actually-signed DNT — two divergent consent truths.
- No preview-without-session: start_dnt_questionnaire conflates preview and start (and actually starts nothing); the catalog's get_dnt_questions scenario (zeno_workflow.feature:184-188) has no implementation.
- DNT questions are not flat and the intended subtype gating is unenforced: dnt_sustainability has a real parent/child branch (seed-questions.ts:557-569) while the life_financial/investment/sustainability groups describe conditionality on DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE that nothing implements — every customer is asked all 26 questions.
- Answer table does double duty for DNT + underwriting + BD medical, distinguished only by group phase; future modify-with-cascade logic for underwriting (questionnaire-consequences topic) would have to permanently special-case DNT rows out of cascade rules.
- No identity interaction: an anonymous customer can sign a DNT today (signDnt has no isAnonymous check); identify_customer does not exist; the catalog expects requires_identity before the application phase that hosts DNT.
- withdraw_consent does not exist, so the catalog's consent-withdrawal scenario (zeno_workflow.feature:237-241) has no tool.
- 365-day validity is a hardcoded handler constant (dnt-handlers.ts:296), not an engine policy; renewal semantics (what happens at expiry) are undefined.
- Three downstream readers re-derive DNT validity ad hoc (start_application, verifyConsents, deriveState) instead of one engine-owned predicate — drift risk across gates.

### Decision points

#### T3.D1 — What is the DNT data model — and at what scope?

- **✅ Recommended — Dedicated customer-scoped aggregate: Dnt + DntSession + DntAnswer**: Three new Prisma models.
