Dnt = the signed artifact: id, customerId, signedAt, validUntil, productTypesCovered, status (ACTIVE/EXPIRED/SUPERSEDED/WITHDRAWN), consent snapshot (gdprConsentAt, aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt, scope), sourceSessionId, supersededById. DntSession = the working sub-flow: id, customerId, type (NEW/UPDATE), status (ACTIVE/FINISHED/SIGNED/CANCELLED), baseDntId? (for UPDATE pre-fill), originConversationId? (audit pointer only, never scoping), startedAt/finishedAt. DntAnswer: sessionId, questionId, value, answeredAt, @@unique([sessionId, questionId]). Partial unique on DntSession (customerId, status=ACTIVE) enforces one active session. Anonymous customers: sessions may be created for any Customer row (every conversation has one — schema line 302), but the engine returns requires_identity at sign_dnt for isAnonymous customers; signed Dnt rows exist only for identified customers.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: matches the domain — the DNT outlives any conversation and is reused across products for ~a year; the signed Dnt is an immutable compliance artifact while the session is the mutable workspace; the one-active-session invariant becomes a database constraint rather than handler discipline; DNT answers are physically separated from underwriting answers, so cascade logic never needs to exclude them; renewal is a new session + new Dnt row with full history (SUPERSEDED chain) for IDD audit. Con: the questionnaire engine's DB wrappers must be generalized from conversationId to an answer-scope parameter, and the suitability report gains a second answer source for new sales (session) alongside the legacy one (conversation).
- **Reuse Answer with a session discriminator**: Add DntSession, but store its answers in the existing Answer table: add nullable dntSessionId, make conversationId nullable, replace the @@unique([questionId, conversationId]) with two partial uniques, and a CHECK that exactly one scope is set.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: one answer table keeps getNextQuestion/calculateProgress single-pathed and the suitability report query shape unchanged. Con: nullable-FK-discriminator is an integrity smell — the schema can no longer express 'an underwriting answer always belongs to a conversation'; every future underwriting query (especially the cascade engine from questionnaire-consequences) must filter dntSessionId IS NULL forever, a permanent coupling between two lifecycles the target explicitly separates (flat/no-consequence vs branching/cascading); a missed filter silently corrupts cascade behavior and is hard to test for.
- **Conversation-scoped sessions (DntSession hangs off Conversation)**: Introduce DntSession/DntAnswer but key them by conversationId, keeping the signed state on Conversation as today.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: no cross-conversation identity questions; everything stays in one aggregate. Con: fails the core target semantic — a DNT valid ~365 days across conversations and products; pre-filling an update session would require trawling other conversations' sessions; check-on-return scenarios (expired DNT, returning customer) are unimplementable; perpetuates exactly the divergence the customer-data SSOT direction exists to kill.

**Rationale:** The DNT is legally a customer-level needs-analysis document, not a conversation artifact — the data model should say so. Separating DntAnswer from Answer encodes the catalog's central distinction (DNT answers are independent, underwriting answers cascade) in the schema instead of in ever-present query filters, which is the only arrangement where the cascade engine cannot accidentally touch DNT data. The immutable Dnt row with a SUPERSEDED chain gives compliance a clean audit trail, and the partial-unique active-session constraint turns a Gherkin scenario ('start_dnt_session refuses a second active session') into a database guarantee. Anonymous handling stays simple because Customer rows always exist: sessions attach to the (possibly anonymous) customer, and the legality engine — not the handler — blocks sign_dnt with requires_identity.

**Depends on / interacts with:** identity, legality-engine, questionnaire-consequences, application-lifecycle, phase-model

#### T3.D2 — How is existing conversation-scoped DNT state migrated?

- **✅ Recommended — One-shot backfill, then drop the Conversation columns**: Migration: for every Conversation with dntSignedAt, create a SIGNED DntSession (originConversationId set) and copy that conversation's phase='dnt' Answer rows into DntAnswer; create a Dnt row per customer from the LATEST signed conversation (signedAt/validUntil carried over, productTypesCovered=['LIFE'] from the conversation's product, earlier ones marked SUPERSEDED). Then drop Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil and re-point all four readers (dnt-handlers, application-handlers:35-40, consent-check.ts:48-57, derive-state.ts:109-113). Legacy Answer rows are left in place untouched as the historical record behind already-generated suitability reports.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: exactly one source of truth from day one — every gate (start_application, quote-time verifyConsents, deriveState) reads the same Dnt predicate; no dual-read logic to test or to rot; customers with a valid signed DNT keep it (and gain cross-conversation validity they never had); the deterministic latest-wins dedup is auditable in the migration itself. Con: the migration embeds business judgment (latest-wins; coverage inferred as LIFE) that must be reviewed; any conversation rows with dntSignedAt but incomplete answers (possible only via bugs) need a defined disposition.
- **Dual-read shim, no backfill**: New model for new signatures; readers fall back to Conversation.dntSignedAt when no Dnt row exists.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: nothing is rewritten retroactively. Con: institutionalizes two sources of truth for the funnel's most important gate — the precise pathology already recorded for customer data; the legality engine must encode both shapes; renewal/update flows cannot pre-fill from legacy state (answers aren't in DntAnswer), so the fallback path has permanently degraded semantics; every BDD scenario needs a legacy and a modern variant.
- **Clean break: drop the columns, no backfill**: Remove dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil; all customers start with no DNT and redo it on next contact.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: simplest possible invariant set, no inferred data. Con: destroys valid consent/needs-analysis state — customers who legitimately signed are silently un-signed, which is both a data-integrity and a compliance regression (the signed fact is evidence); contradicts the catalog's own expired-DNT flow, which prescribes update-with-pre-fill rather than re-do.

**Rationale:** The signed DNT is compliance evidence; a migration must preserve it, and preserving it anywhere other than the new canonical store recreates divergence. Backfill-then-drop is the only option that ends with a single engine-owned validity predicate while keeping every legitimately signed DNT alive. Latest-wins dedup with SUPERSEDED rows keeps the full history rather than guessing. Leaving the legacy Answer rows untouched keeps historical suitability reports reproducible.

**Depends on / interacts with:** phase-model, quote-lifecycle, testing-bdd

#### T3.D3 — How is product-type coverage (products_covered) modeled when only one LIFE product exists?

- **✅ Recommended — ProductType enum + Dnt.productTypesCovered as enum array, computed at sign time**: Introduce enum ProductType { LIFE } (extended as product-data adds types), promote Product.insuranceType (currently a free String, schema line 109) to it, and store Dnt.productTypesCovered ProductType[]. At sign_dnt the engine derives coverage from which DNT question groups the session actually contained (today: the life groups → [LIFE]). get_dnt_state answers 'covers this application's product type' with productTypesCovered.includes(application.product.insuranceType).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: fails closed — when home/car products arrive, existing DNTs explicitly do NOT cover them, which is the correct compliance behavior (a life needs-analysis says nothing about property needs); the coverage check is a one-line deterministic engine predicate; typing Product.insuranceType kills a latent stringly-typed field. Con: the enum starts with one value, so the multi-type code path is untestable against real catalog data until product-data ships a second type (a seeded test fixture must cover it instead).
- **String array mirroring Product.insuranceType**: Dnt.productTypesCovered String[]; compare by string equality with the product's insuranceType.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: no enum migration when a type is added; same fails-closed semantics. Con: no referential integrity — a typo ('LIFE ' vs 'LIFE') silently invalidates coverage and only surfaces as a customer-facing re-DNT; the set of legal types lives in convention rather than schema, weakening both validation and test generation.
- **Defer: no coverage field; DNT covers everything**: Omit products_covered until a second product type exists; validity is purely temporal.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: no speculative modeling. Con: bakes in a wrong invariant that will fail open — the day a property product ships, every existing life DNT silently 'covers' it, which is a suitability/compliance violation (IDD demands-and-needs must match the product class); retrofitting the field then requires inferring coverage for old rows, i.e., this same decision but with dirty data; also leaves get_dnt_state unable to honor the catalog's contract and the feature-file scenario 'A DNT not covering the product type triggers a fresh session' untestable.

**Rationale:** Coverage must fail closed: an absent claim of coverage is recoverable (run an update session), a false claim is a compliance breach. Deriving the list from the session's actual question groups makes coverage a fact about what was analyzed rather than a declaration, which keeps it honest as group composition evolves. The enum gives the legality engine and tests a closed vocabulary, and typing Product.insuranceType is independently correct.

**Depends on / interacts with:** product-data, application-lifecycle, legality-engine

#### T3.D4 — What is the DNT tool surface — faithful 9 tools or a collapsed set?

- **Faithful 9-tool catalog surface**: Implement get_dnt_state, get_dnt_questions, start_dnt_session, update_dnt, get_dnt_next_question, get_dnt_session_details, write_dnt_answer, modify_dnt_answer, sign_dnt exactly as catalogued.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: 1:1 with the spec and the Gherkin scenarios as written; write vs modify mirrors the underwriting questionnaire's vocabulary, so the agent learns one naming pattern. Con: it preserves two agent-made business decisions the engine should own — choosing start_dnt_session vs update_dnt (the engine already knows whether a prior Dnt exists/expired) and choosing write vs modify (in a no-consequence flat flow they are the same upsert); redundant tools widen the surface the legality engine must gate and the BDD suite must cover, and write/modify divergence is a standing source of inconsistent behavior for an operation the catalog itself says has no consequences either way.
- **✅ Recommended — Collapsed 6-tool surface (engine decides session type; one answer commit)**: Reads: get_dnt_state (valid, valid_until, products_covered, session_active, session_active_id — also injected ambiently via DerivedState); get_dnt_questions (preview, no session); get_dnt_next_question (next question + answered/unanswered counts + started_at, absorbing get_dnt_session_details). Commits: start_dnt_session (engine derives type — NEW when no prior Dnt, UPDATE pre-filled from the prior Dnt's answers when expired/amend; rejected-with-active_id when a session is already active); save_dnt_answer (session_id, question_id, value — idempotent upsert serving both first-write and modification, returns next_question | finish); sign_dnt (session_id, consent{gdpr, ai_disclosure}).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: removes both agent business decisions — 'which session type' and 'is this a write or a modify' become engine facts, which is precisely the 'agent never decides a business rule' invariant; every remaining tool has a distinct, non-inferable purpose; the swap test still holds because a GUI calls the identical six operations; fewer legality conditions and consequence rows to verify. Con: diverges from catalog/feature-file naming, so the Gherkin scenarios for update_dnt and modify_dnt_answer must be rewritten against the collapsed surface; folding session-details into get_dnt_next_question slightly overloads a read (mitigable by also exposing counts in get_dnt_state).
- **Minimal 4-tool surface (reads go ambient)**: Only get_dnt_questions, start_dnt_session, save_dnt_answer, sign_dnt as callable tools; DNT state and next-question are injected every turn via DerivedState/available_actions rather than being callable.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: smallest commit surface; leans on the engine-injected-state invariant the catalog already endorses for R tools. Con: breaks the swap test asymmetrically — a GUI needs state and next-question as request/response endpoints, so they exist anyway and hiding them from the agent just makes the agent a special client; the agent loses on-demand refresh after a failed commit (it must trust possibly stale injected state); progress questions from the customer ('how far along am I?') have no deterministic read to answer from.

**Rationale:** The framing explicitly allows simplification, and both collapses follow from the architecture's own first principle: legality and business choice belong to the engine. start vs update is a fact about prior Dnt state the engine already holds; write vs modify is a distinction without a difference in a flow whose answers are declared independent — keeping both invites divergent implementations of the same upsert. Six tools keep every catalog behavior reachable (preview, resume, refuse-second-session-with-active-id, pre-fill, progress, consent-signing) while shrinking the gated surface the legality engine and the BDD suite must guarantee.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, tool-mapping, testing-bdd

#### T3.D5 — Where do GDPR and AI-disclosure consent records land — folded into sign_dnt or kept as separate tools?

- **✅ Recommended — Fold into sign_dnt as the sole consent-writing commit**: sign_dnt(session_id, consent{gdpr, ai_disclosure}) atomically: validates session completeness, snapshots consent evidence immutably onto the Dnt row, and mirrors current-state to Customer.gdprConsentAt/gdprConsentScope/aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt (one-way, at sign time). record_gdpr_consent and acknowledge_ai_disclosure are retired from the agent surface; a new withdraw_consent commit (currently nonexistent) handles revocation by marking the Dnt WITHDRAWN and clearing customer-level current-state. Refused consent returns requires_consent and preserves the answered session (per zeno_workflow.feature:209-213).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: one atomic commit means no half-states (consent recorded but DNT unsigned, or vice versa — the divergence that exists today because signDnt discards its booleans while record_gdpr_consent writes independently); the consent evidence is bound to the document it authorizes, which is what an IDD/GDPR audit actually asks for; matches the catalog's explicit assumption #1 (no standalone CONSENT phase) and lets the phase model retire its CONSENT special case (derive-state.ts:46). Con: GDPR consent becomes available only at DNT signing, so any pre-DNT personal-data processing (discovery-phase profile extraction, collect_customer_field) needs its own legal basis — that burden moves to the identity flow; AI-disclosure acknowledgment captured this late cannot be the only transparency mechanism.
- **Keep separate consent tools as prerequisites; sign_dnt only verifies**: record_gdpr_consent and acknowledge_ai_disclosure remain agent commits; the engine blocks sign_dnt with requires_consent until both customer timestamps exist; sign_dnt itself writes no consent.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: consent can be captured as early as needed (covers pre-DNT data processing); tools already exist and are alwaysAllowed. Con: splits one user decision into a multi-commit dance — the documented permission-asking/deflection pathology in this codebase came from exactly this shape; consent evidence stays on Customer only, detached from the document signed, so the audit question 'what did the customer consent to when signing THIS DNT' has no immutable answer; two writers of the same fields with no ordering guarantee.
- **Hybrid: sign_dnt is canonical, record_gdpr_consent survives only for pre-DNT processing**: sign_dnt snapshots + mirrors as in option A, but record_gdpr_consent is kept, exposed by the engine only when personal data is being collected before any DNT (e.g., during identification); acknowledge_ai_disclosure is retired in favor of UI-level disclosure at conversation start plus the sign_dnt acknowledgment.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: covers the genuine pre-DNT GDPR-basis gap without a standalone consent phase; AI transparency is handled where it belongs (system/UI at first contact) with the explicit acknowledgment still recorded at signing. Con: two writers of Customer.gdprConsentAt remain, so a precedence rule (sign_dnt snapshot is authoritative for the Dnt; latest write wins for current-state) must be specified and tested; the engine needs an extra exposure condition for the residual tool.

**Rationale:** On consent the decisive properties are atomicity and evidentiary binding: consent must be inseparable from the document it authorizes, and the system must never sit in a half-consented state — only the folded commit guarantees both. The catalog states this assumption outright, and the conversational-pathology history of this project argues against any multi-step consent dance. The pre-DNT data-processing gap is real but belongs to the identity topic (identify_customer can carry its own legal basis); if that topic concludes a pre-DNT consent commit is required, the hybrid's residual tool can be added there under an engine exposure condition without changing sign_dnt's shape. AI disclosure at first contact is a UI/system obligation regardless of which option is chosen — sign_dnt records the explicit acknowledgment, not the disclosure itself.

**Depends on / interacts with:** identity, commit-envelope, phase-model, legality-engine

#### T3.D6 — Are DNT questions strictly flat, and does the shared questionnaire engine serve DNT sessions?

- **✅ Recommended — Visibility-only branching; 'flat' means no consequences on modify; one generalized engine**: Keep shouldShowQuestion-style conditional visibility inside DNT sessions (so DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE can genuinely gate the financial/investment/sustainability groups, fixing today's unenforced descriptions, and the existing sustainability follow-up survives). The flatness guarantee is reinterpreted as the catalog's actual consequence claim: modify never cascades — answers are never invalidated or cleared; visibility is re-derived on read; hidden answers are retained but excluded from progress, sign-time completeness, and the suitability report. Generalize the questionnaire engine's DB wrappers (lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.ts:389-534) to take an answer scope ({conversation} | {dntSession}) instead of forking; pure functions stay shared.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: matches the seeded reality (subtype-dependent groups are an intended product behavior, currently broken — everyone gets all 26 questions); preserves the catalog's load-bearing guarantee (modify_dnt_answer has no consequences) as an engine invariant rather than a data-shape claim; one engine means validation, fuzzy option matching, and visibility logic cannot drift between flows. Con: 'flat (no branching)' in the catalog is contradicted in letter (though not in consequence semantics), so the spec and feature file need an explicit amendment; retained-but-hidden answers need a defined exclusion rule at sign time or stale answers leak into the IDD report.
- **Strictly flat: strip all branching from DNT; group inclusion frozen at session creation**: Remove parentQuestionId/showWhenValue from all DNT questions; the session's question list is frozen when the session is created, derived from product type.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: the simplest possible session semantics — questions_remaining is a constant-minus-answered, no visibility recomputation, modify is trivially consequence-free. Con: DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE is itself a DNT question, so a frozen-at-creation list cannot adapt to the subtype answer — either everyone answers investment-risk questions (today's broken behavior, bad needs-analysis quality and suitability noise) or subtype must be asked before the session exists, which invents a pre-session questionnaire the catalog doesn't have; deletes the seeded sustainability follow-up semantics.
- **Fork a dedicated flat DNT engine**: New DNT-specific question walker over DntAnswer; the existing engine remains conversation-only for underwriting/BD.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: DNT logic can never be perturbed by underwriting-engine changes (cascade work in questionnaire-consequences touches nothing DNT). Con: duplicates validation/normalization/fuzzy-matching (validateAnswer, diacritics handling) — two implementations of 'what is a valid answer' is a correctness drift generator, visible to the same agent in the same conversation; the isolation argument is weak because the shared pure functions are already side-effect-free and the cascade machinery lives outside them.

**Rationale:** The catalog's flatness assumption exists to guarantee one thing: modifying a DNT answer is always consequence-free. That guarantee is about cascade semantics, not about whether a presentation-level follow-up can hide. The seeded form demonstrably needs conditional visibility (subtype gating is described but unenforced — a real correctness bug this redesign should fix, not entrench), and strict flatness can only achieve it by asking everyone everything, which degrades the needs analysis the DNT legally exists to perform. Generalizing the existing engine keeps a single definition of answer validity across DNT and underwriting while the consequence machinery (which is the genuinely divergent part) remains exclusive to the underwriting flow. The spec amendment should be recorded in the catalog's assumptions block, which invites corrections.

**Depends on / interacts with:** questionnaire-consequences, testing-bdd, product-data

### Risks

- Phase-model breakage at cutover: deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:46,109-113) keys CONSENT on conversation.dntSignedAt and customer.gdprConsentAt; if the Dnt entity ships without the phase derivation being re-pointed in the same change, the engine will demand a consent that can no longer be satisfied (or silently skip the gate). The migration and the phase-model change must land atomically.
- Three independent validity re-derivations exist today (dnt-handlers.ts:40, application-handlers.ts:39, consent-check.ts:53-54); if any reader is missed during re-pointing, a stale conversation-stamp check will pass/fail divergently from the new Dnt predicate — grep-verified list must be the migration checklist.
- Backfill judgment calls: latest-wins dedup for customers with multiple signed conversations, and coverage inferred as ['LIFE'], are business decisions embedded in a migration; an unreviewed wrong call becomes permanent compliance history. Conversations with dntSignedAt but incomplete DNT answers (possible via historical bugs) need an explicit disposition rule.
- AI-disclosure timing: capturing acknowledgment only inside sign_dnt is likely too late as the SOLE transparency mechanism (EU AI Act-style disclosure belongs at first interaction). The design assumes a UI/system-level disclosure at conversation start; if that assumption is false, folding acknowledge_ai_disclosure away creates a compliance hole rather than closing one.
- Pre-DNT GDPR basis: discovery-phase profile extraction and collect_customer_field process personal data before any DNT exists; folding consent into sign_dnt removes the only agent path to record a legal basis for that processing. This is delegated to the identity topic — if identify_customer does not carry consent capture, a gap opens.
- Anonymous-to-identified customer merge: Dnt/DntSession FKs point at Customer; if the identity topic resolves anonymous customers by merging rows rather than promoting them in place, DNT rows must be re-pointed or they orphan silently.
- Single-product degeneracy: with one LIFE product, products_covered is always ['LIFE'] and the not-covered → fresh-session path (zeno_workflow.feature:230-233) cannot be exercised against real catalog data; without a seeded second-type fixture the coverage predicate ships untested and may be wrong when home/car products arrive.
- Customer-level facts trapped in session answers: dnt_consent's marketing and electronic-communication consents (seed-questions.ts:115-164) are durable customer preferences stored as per-session DntAnswer rows; without propagation to the customer profile (CustomerProfile SSOT direction), each new session can silently contradict the recorded preference — the same divergence pathology as extractedProfile/CustomerInsight.
- Suitability-report source split: lib/compliance/dnt-report.ts reads DNT answers via conversation; post-migration new sales must read from the signed Dnt's session while historical reports keep reading legacy Answer rows — if the report is not made source-aware, new policies will render empty DNT sections.
- Update-session pre-fill correctness: pre-filling from a prior Dnt's answers across question-set versions (questions added/removed/recoded since the original signing) needs a defined matching rule (by question code, not id); silent mismatches would carry stale answers into a renewed legal document.
- Hidden-answer leakage under visibility-only branching: answers retained after their gating answer changes must be excluded from sign-time completeness and from the IDD report; if exclusion is implemented in only one of those two places, the signed document and the report can disagree about what the customer declared.

---

## T4. Customer identification: what "identified" means and how identify_customer works

> Topic key: `identity`

### Current state (code-grounded)

No identification process exists; what exists is an unauthenticated customer-id cookie plus a dashboard-only magic link, never reconciled.

DATA MODEL (prisma/schema.prisma:267-298): Customer has email (@unique), phone, name, dateOfBirth, cnpEncrypted/cnpIv/cnpTag, address Json, isAnonymous (default true), magicLinkToken (@unique) + magicLinkExpiresAt, gdprConsentAt/gdprConsentScope/aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt, and relations conversations/applications/quotes/policies/payments — Customer is already the cross-conversation join point. User (schema.prisma:692-704) is a separate auth entity (role CUSTOMER, customerId @unique) used only for dashboard JWT.

TRANSPORT IDENTITY: POST /api/session (app/api/session/route.ts) creates an anonymous Customer and sets cookie zeno_session = the RAW Customer.id (30 days, httpOnly). POST /api/chat (app/api/chat/route.ts:21,83) and POST /api/chat/create (app/api/chat/create/route.ts) accept customerId directly from the request body with no auth check — identity is fully client-asserted. If no customerId arrives, the orchestrator creates a fresh anonymous Customer per turn (lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:224-229).

DECLARED-DATA COLLECTION: collect_customer_field (lib/tools/handlers/data-handlers.ts) collects FIELD_ORDER = [name, cnp, dateOfBirth, email, phone] one at a time with regex validation: CNP = ^[1-9]\d{12}$ ONLY (no control-digit checksum, no cross-check vs dateOfBirth/sex encoded in the CNP), DOB age 18-64, RO phone pattern. CNP is AES-256-GCM encrypted with a RANDOM IV per operation (lib/security/encryption.ts:21-27) — therefore no equality lookup by CNP is possible. When the 5th field lands, it sets isAnonymous=false (data-handlers.ts:241-245). The tool is registered (lib/tools/registry.ts:956) but is reachable only via the GUI action submit_field (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:81-89): skill-pack seeds grant a NONEXISTENT tool name 'save_customer_field' (prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts:103,232 — dead grant, never registered) and no workflow step in prisma/seeds/seed-workflows.ts grants collect_customer_field.

CHANNEL VERIFICATION: magic link only, dashboard-coupled. POST /api/auth/magic-link (app/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts) emails a 30-min one-time token ONLY for an email already on a Customer; GET /api/auth/verify (app/api/auth/verify/route.ts) consumes it, creates/loads User, sets zeno_auth JWT (7d), redirects to /dashboard. This NEVER touches zeno_session or any Conversation — chat identity and dashboard identity are parallel systems that never reconcile. Post-payment (lib/payments/post-payment.ts:87-100) also mints a 7-day magic link to /dashboard?token=... and force-sets isAnonymous=false, but NO dashboard route consumes a token searchParam (app/dashboard/(protected)/* read only the zeno_auth cookie) — the emailed re-entry link dead-ends at the login redirect. No OTP/SMS code exists anywhere in lib (verified by grep).

GATES: none. start_application checks DNT only (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:39-40); accept_quote checks confirmAcceptance/DRAFT/expiry and creates Policy PENDING_SUBMISSION (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:316-371); initiate_payment checks policy status only (lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts:67-73); post-payment marks Policy SUBMITTED regardless of whether name/CNP/email exist. A fully anonymous customer can complete the entire funnel through payment and insurer submission with zero KYC fields. identify_customer, get_open_items, get_application_list, and the requires_identity consequence do not exist anywhere in the codebase (verified by grep over lib/ and the full registry list, lib/tools/registry.ts:407-1109). deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts) has no identity dimension — its 6 phases and nextBestAction never reference isAnonymous or missing customer fields; the only prompt surfacing is 'Status: Anonymous visitor' (lib/chat/context-loaders.ts:670-672, 750-752).

CROSS-CONVERSATION TODAY: continuity = same browser cookie. get_customer_profile (lib/tools/handlers/profile-handlers.ts:14-74) reads recent conversations + policies by context.customerId, exposing PII to whoever holds the cookie/customerId. Customer.email is @unique and collect_customer_field does a bare prisma update with catch-all error (data-handlers.ts:180-183, 255-257), so declaring an email that belongs to an existing Customer throws a unique-constraint error — there is no claim/merge/link path for a returning customer on a new device; each cleared cookie strands a new anonymous Customer row.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** "GATES: none. start_application checks DNT only (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:39-40)"
  **Correction:** The DNT check is indeed at lines 39-40 and there is no identity check (the load-bearing point stands), but 'checks DNT only' is literally inaccurate: start_application also short-circuits if an OPEN application already exists (lines 43-46), fails if no product is selected (lines 48-49, 'No product selected. Call set_candidate_product first'), and validates tierCode/levelCode against PricingTier/PricingLevel (lines 51-63). _(lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:39-49)_
- **Claim:** "User (schema.prisma:692-704) is a separate auth entity (role CUSTOMER, customerId @unique) used only for dashboard JWT."
  **Correction:** The User model lines and customerId @unique are correct, but role is an enum UserRole {CUSTOMER, ADMIN, OPERATOR} with @default(CUSTOMER), and User is NOT used only for the customer dashboard JWT: app/api/auth/login/route.ts implements ADMIN/OPERATOR email+password login issuing a 24h JWT, and app/api/admin/users/* manage User rows. The claim is accurate only for role-CUSTOMER users. _(prisma/schema.prisma:66-70, 692-704; app/api/auth/login/route.ts:25-40)_
- **Claim:** Gap: "no code path binds an anonymous chat Customer to a verified User"
  **Correction:** Overstated. A data-level binding path exists: POST /api/auth/magic-link upserts a User with customerId = the matched Customer (app/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts:43-51), and GET /api/auth/verify finds-or-creates a User bound to whatever Customer holds the token, with no isAnonymous check (app/api/auth/verify/route.ts:49-62) — so an anonymous chat Customer whose email was persisted CAN end up bound to a verified User. What is genuinely absent (and the same gap correctly states) is session/conversation reconciliation: verification never touches zeno_session or any Conversation, and chat APIs never consult zeno_auth. _(app/api/auth/verify/route.ts:49-62; app/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts:43-51)_
- **Claim:** Gap: "Magic-link request only works for emails already on a Customer (app/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts:29-36) — it cannot verify a NEW email declared mid-chat by an anonymous customer"
  **Correction:** The first half is correct (lines 29-36 return a silent success when no Customer matches). The second half is overstated: an email declared mid-chat via collect_customer_field IS persisted to Customer.email (lib/tools/handlers/data-handlers.ts:159-161, 180-183), after which the magic-link endpoint finds that Customer and sends the challenge. The real limitation is that the resulting verification lands in the dashboard JWT system (zeno_auth + /dashboard redirect) and never flows back into the chat session — not that the new email is unverifiable. _(app/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts:29-36; lib/tools/handlers/data-handlers.ts:159-161, 180-183; app/api/auth/verify/route.ts:82-88)_

### Gaps

- identify_customer does not exist as a tool, and the requires_identity consequence appears nowhere in code — the catalog's identity gate on set_application and accept_quote has no implementation to evolve from.
- Transport identity is spoofable: zeno_session cookie is the raw Customer.id and /api/chat + /api/chat/create accept any customerId in the request body unauthenticated; any engine-level identity gate built on top would be meaningless because the engine cannot trust who is calling.
- Two parallel identity systems (zeno_session customer cookie for chat; zeno_auth JWT/User for dashboard) with no reconciliation: verifying a magic link never updates the chat session or any Conversation, and no code path binds an anonymous chat Customer to a verified User.
- isAnonymous conflates two different facts: 'all 5 declared fields present' (data-handlers.ts:241-245) and 'completed a payment' (post-payment.ts:96). Neither involves channel proof, so isAnonymous=false cannot be read as 'verified'.
- No funnel commit checks identity at all — quote acceptance, Policy creation, payment, and insurer submission (Policy → SUBMITTED) all execute for a customer with zero KYC fields, although Allianz submission requires CNP.
- CNP validation is regex-only: no Romanian CNP control-digit checksum and no consistency check against the declared dateOfBirth/sex; an invalid CNP flows encrypted into the record that would back an insurer submission.
- collect_customer_field is unreachable by the agent: skill packs grant the nonexistent 'save_customer_field' (seed-skill-packs.ts:103,232) and no workflow step grants it; only the GUI submit_field action path works, so the conversational funnel cannot deterministically drive data collection.
- Returning-customer claim is a dead end: Customer.email @unique + bare update means declaring an existing email errors out; there is no verified claim-and-merge, so cross-device continuity (get_open_items-style re-engagement in the feature spec) is impossible.
- Post-payment magic-link URL (/dashboard?token=...) is consumed by no route — the only emailed re-entry path for a paying customer lands on the login redirect (verify endpoint expects /api/auth/verify?token=, dashboard pages read only the zeno_auth cookie).
- DerivedState has no identity tier, no missingFields, and nextBestAction never points at data collection or verification — the agent has no deterministic signal of what identity step unblocks which commit.
- cnpEncrypted uses a random IV per encryption, so no equality lookup by CNP exists; any future duplicate-detection or claim-by-CNP needs a blind index or hash column that does not exist today.
- Magic-link request only works for emails already on a Customer (app/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts:29-36) — it cannot verify a NEW email declared mid-chat by an anonymous customer, which is the primary identification moment in the target flow.

### Decision points

#### T4.D1 — What does 'identified' mean for this funnel?

- **verified-channel-only**: A customer is identified iff they have proven control of a contact channel (magic-link email click or SMS OTP). Declared fields alone never flip the status.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Strongest confidentiality guarantee and a single unambiguous status. But it makes channel proof a prerequisite for steps where nothing confidential is disclosed and nothing binding is committed (answering DNT/questionnaire about yourself), inserting an async out-of-band round-trip into the middle of a conversation for no protective benefit at that point; it also conflates two different protections (data confidentiality vs data quality) into one gate.
- **declared-fields-only**: Identified = name + CNP + DOB + contact collected and validated (checksum, cross-checks), without channel proof — essentially today's isAnonymous semantics done properly.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Keeps the funnel fully conversational and satisfies the insurer's data-quality need (valid CNP for submission). But it is an account-takeover and PII-disclosure vector: anyone typing a victim's known email/CNP would count as 'identified' and could read prior applications/policies cross-conversation — incompatible with GDPR confidentiality for history lookup, and gives payment/contract commits no repudiation anchor.
- **✅ Recommended — tiered-identity**: Two engine-computed tiers: DECLARED (KYC fields complete AND valid: CNP checksum + CNP↔DOB consistency) and VERIFIED (declared + proven control of email or phone). DerivedState exposes identity {tier, missingFields, verifiedChannels}; each commit declares the tier it requires.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Models the two distinct protections separately: declared tier protects data integrity (insurer gets a real, checksum-valid identity), verified tier protects confidentiality and repudiation (history reads and binding commits need proof the person is who the record says). Costs a slightly larger state surface and requires every gate to name its tier explicitly — which is exactly the determinism the legality engine wants anyway. Consistent with insurance reality in Romania: AML/KYC requires correct CNP data at contract time, GDPR requires not disclosing stored personal data to an unverified claimant.

**Rationale:** The two things identity protects in this funnel are different in kind: (1) the insurer-facing application/contract must carry CORRECT identity data (a data-integrity property satisfiable by validated declared fields), and (2) stored personal history must only be shown to its OWNER (a confidentiality property satisfiable only by channel proof). A single boolean either under-protects history (declared-only) or over-gates the conversational funnel with an async round-trip that protects nothing at that stage (verified-only). The tiered model also gives requires_identity a precise, actionable payload (which tier, what is missing), which the agent-as-client architecture needs to avoid deadlocks.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, phase-model, tool-mapping

#### T4.D2 — Where does the identity gate sit — which commits require which tier?

- **catalog-literal-early-gate**: Identity (one undifferentiated status) required at set_application, exactly as the catalog table states; everything after is identity-clean.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simple invariant: everything inside @application is identity-bound from birth, so DNT/answers/quotes are always attributable. But if 'identity' means verified-channel it forces the out-of-band round-trip before the customer may even answer needs-analysis questions; if it means declared-only, then accept_quote/payment (the binding, money-moving, insurer-submitting commits) run with zero proof of ownership — the gate is at the wrong strength for both ends.
- **late-gate-at-acceptance**: No identity requirement until accept_quote/payment; discovery, DNT, questionnaire and quote generation all run anonymously.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Maximally frictionless funnel and matches 'talk is free'. But the application snapshot, DNT and underwriting answers are personal data collected against an anonymous blob: premiums depend on age/CNP-derivable facts, so generate_quote can price against unvalidated declared data and the quote can change after late identification (re-rating surprise); it also contradicts the customer-scoped SSOT direction — personal records accrue on shells that may never become claimable.
- **✅ Recommended — tier-mapped-gates**: DECLARED tier required by set_application (the catalog's requires_identity on set_application is interpreted as the declared tier); VERIFIED tier required by accept_quote (and therefore everything in @payment); history/cross-conversation reads (get_customer_info rich view, get_open_items, get_application_list, resume of another conversation's items) require VERIFIED; sign_dnt requires only declared (the DNT is the consent gate, not the identity gate, per the catalog's 'DNT is the first gate of @application' AFTER set_application).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Each gate sits where its protection is needed: underwriting and pricing operate on checksum-valid identity data from the application's first moment (no re-rating surprises from late identity), while channel proof is demanded exactly when something binding or confidential happens (contract acceptance, payment, history disclosure). Requires the engine to model a 'verification pending' wait state between quote and acceptance, and requires the quote-validity window to tolerate that wait — both must be explicit in the legality engine to avoid deadlock.

**Rationale:** Mapping tiers to what each commit actually risks is the only assignment where every gate has a justification: set_application freezes a person-bound snapshot, so the person's declared identity must exist and be internally consistent (CNP checksum, CNP↔DOB) before underwriting starts; accept_quote creates a binding contract and triggers payment and insurer submission, where an unverified impostor causes real-world harm and the business needs a repudiation anchor; history reads disclose stored PII and are gated by confidentiality, not by funnel position. The catalog's own rows support this split: set_application returns requires_identity while accept_quote is 'exposed when ... identified' — two different mentions that the tiered reading makes non-redundant.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, quote-lifecycle, payments, application-lifecycle, dnt-sessions

#### T4.D3 — Tool shape: what is identify_customer, and what does requires_identity point the agent to do?

- **single-orchestrating-commit**: One identify_customer commit that does everything: collects/validates remaining fields, sends the magic link or OTP, polls/receives verification, and returns 'identity established'.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One tool matches the catalog row literally and is simple for the agent to select. But it fuses a synchronous, per-field, engine-validated data dialogue with an asynchronous external handoff into one opaque operation — the engine cannot expose precise blocked-action reasons ('missing CNP' vs 'verification email sent, awaiting click'), partial progress is invisible to a GUI client (breaking the swap test, where a form + a verify button are naturally two operations), and idempotent re-invocation semantics get murky (does calling it again re-send the link or re-ask fields?).
- **fields-only-derived-status**: Keep collect_customer_field as the only identity tool; the engine derives identity status purely from field completeness (formalizing today's isAnonymous flip). No verification commit at all.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Smallest tool surface and fully synchronous. But it structurally cannot produce the VERIFIED tier — no amount of field collection proves channel ownership — so either binding commits go unprotected or verification leaks into out-of-band UI glue the engine doesn't model, recreating today's unreconciled dual-identity problem (zeno_session vs zeno_auth).
- **✅ Recommended — two-layer-commits-plus-derived-state**: Layer 1: collect_customer_field stays as the declared-tier commit (each call engine-validated, returns applied/rejected with reason; CNP checksum + cross-checks added). Layer 2: identify_customer is the verification handoff commit — input: channel (email|sms); effect: engine issues the challenge (magic link / OTP bound to the CONVERSATION's customer, not the dashboard); completion is an engine event (link clicked / OTP entered via GUI action) that flips the tier. DerivedState gains identity {tier, missingFields[], verification: {channel, pending, expiresAt}}. requires_identity carries {tier_required, missing_fields[]} or {tier_required, verification_pending: true} so the agent (or GUI) knows deterministically whether to collect a field or to trigger/await identify_customer.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Two tools to gate instead of one, and the engine must own a challenge lifecycle (issue, expire, consume — the magic-link mechanics already implemented for the dashboard, retargeted at the conversation). In exchange: every blocked action has a precise machine-readable reason; the verification handoff mirrors the Stripe pattern the catalog already uses for payment (external system owns the sensitive step, engine monitors); the swap test holds (a GUI maps the same two operations to a form and a button); and the asynchronous wait state is explicit in state rather than implied by prose — the exact property whose absence caused the advance-flow deadlock previously.

**Rationale:** Declared identity is incremental, synchronous, per-field data entry — the engine should validate and acknowledge each field individually so the agent can surface precise rejections (wrong CNP checksum vs invalid phone). Verification is an asynchronous external challenge — categorically different, with its own pending/expired/consumed lifecycle, exactly like the payment handoff the architecture already embraces. Keeping them as separate commits with an engine-computed identity status in DerivedState is what makes requires_identity actionable rather than a dead-end refusal: the consequence names the missing piece and the exposed action that supplies it. The catalog's single identify_customer row survives as the verification commit; field collection was never going to be 'auth handoff' anyway.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, tool-mapping, phase-model

#### T4.D4 — Cross-conversation continuity: how does a returning customer's history (conversations, applications, DNT, open payments) link up?

- **cookie-only-continuity**: Status quo formalized: same-browser cookie is the only continuity; a new device or cleared cookie means a fresh anonymous Customer with no path back.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No merge logic and no takeover surface via claiming. But it makes the feature spec's core re-engagement journeys (abandoned payment resumed days later, get_open_items for a returning user) structurally impossible cross-device, strands paying customers from their own policies, and proliferates orphan Customer rows that poison the customer-scoped SSOT direction — personal data accumulates on shells nobody can ever claim, which is itself a GDPR data-minimization problem.
- **claim-by-declaration**: When a declared email/phone/CNP matches an existing Customer, silently link or merge the current conversation onto that record.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Seamless continuity with zero extra interaction. But it is a textbook account-takeover and PII-disclosure vector: typing victim@example.com would attach the impostor's session to the victim's applications, policies and payment items — indefensible under GDPR; also technically unsound for CNP since cnpEncrypted (random-IV AES-GCM) cannot be equality-searched.
- **✅ Recommended — verified-claim-and-merge**: Customer remains the join point. When a declared contact matches an existing Customer, the engine does NOT disclose the match; it exposes identify_customer against the claimed channel. On successful verification the engine executes a deterministic merge/re-bind: the current conversation (and its anonymous Customer shell's data) is attached to the verified Customer under explicit conflict rules (open application/DNT collisions resolved per dnt-sessions and application-lifecycle policies); only then do get_open_items / get_application_list / resume_* expose history. The dashboard magic-link flow and chat verification consume the same challenge mechanism so chat identity and User/JWT identity finally reconcile.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Requires the engine to own merge semantics (two open applications, two DNT states, conflicting declared fields) and a non-disclosing match protocol (the challenge is sent without confirming the account exists — same anti-enumeration posture the magic-link endpoint already takes). In exchange it is the only option that simultaneously satisfies confidentiality (history shown only to a proven owner), the catalog's returning-user tools, and the CustomerProfile SSOT direction (one customer-scoped record that conversations attach to, instead of per-cookie shells).

**Rationale:** Customer is already the relational join point for conversations/applications/quotes/policies/payments — the missing piece is a safe way for a session to EARN attachment to an existing Customer. Verification-gated claiming is the only design where cross-device resume works without making 'knowing someone's email' equivalent to owning their insurance history. It also resolves three verified defects in one coherent mechanism: the email unique-constraint dead end in collect_customer_field, the unreconciled zeno_session/zeno_auth dual identity, and the broken post-payment re-entry link — all become instances of 'verify the channel, then bind the session to the verified Customer'. Prerequisites: a deterministic match key (email/phone direct; CNP only via a new blind-index/hash column since random-IV ciphertext is unsearchable) and explicit merge conflict rules owned by the engine, not the agent.

**Depends on / interacts with:** dnt-sessions, application-lifecycle, payments, policy-post-sale, legality-engine, product-data

#### T4.D5 — Transport identity: what does the engine trust as 'who is calling' before any tier logic applies?

- **client-asserted-customer-id**: Status quo: zeno_session cookie holds the raw Customer.id and /api/chat accepts any customerId in the body.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No session infrastructure beyond a cookie. But every identity tier, gate and consequence built above it is void: possession of a guessable/leaked cuid IS full identity, including PII reads via get_customer_profile and the ability to act on someone else's conversation — the legality engine would be enforcing rules about a subject it cannot authenticate. Indefensible for a system that stores CNP and health answers.
- **✅ Recommended — server-resolved-opaque-session**: An HttpOnly signed/opaque session token (server-side session or signed JWT) resolves to customerId on the server; chat APIs stop accepting customerId from the request body; verified-tier upgrades are recorded against the session, unifying with the existing zeno_auth JWT machinery.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Anonymous-first chat is preserved (a session can point at an anonymous Customer), the engine gets a trustworthy subject for every commit, and identity-tier upgrades (magic link/OTP completion) have a server-side object to attach to. Costs a session issuance/validation layer at the API boundary — which is also the correct enforcement point for the swap test, since GUI and agent clients authenticate identically.
- **mandatory-login**: Require account creation/login (User + JWT) before chatting.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Strongest authentication and a single identity system. But it destroys the anonymous-first discovery funnel the whole catalog is designed around (discovery, DNT preview, pricing examples all work pre-identity) and adds an account where the domain only needs a verifiable contact channel at specific commits.

**Rationale:** Identity tiers are an engine-enforced legality property, and legality enforcement is only as strong as the engine's knowledge of who is acting. With client-asserted customerIds, requires_identity gates would be decorative — an attacker bypasses them by asserting a different id. An opaque server-resolved session keeps the anonymous-first funnel intact while giving every commit an authenticated subject, and it is the natural place where magic-link/OTP completion upgrades the SAME identity the chat is using, eliminating the current zeno_session/zeno_auth split at its root. This decision is a prerequisite for the other four: tiers, gates, identify_customer and claim-and-merge all assume the engine knows who is calling.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope

### Risks

- Verification introduces an asynchronous wait state (challenge sent, awaiting click/OTP) between quote and acceptance; if the legality engine does not model 'verification_pending' as an explicit state with an exposed resume path, the agent will deadlock or loop — the same failure mode previously shipped and fixed in the advance-flow work (a prompt-driven sequence whose required action was not exposed).
- Existing data is misclassified under a tier model: rows with isAnonymous=false were set by post-payment (lib/payments/post-payment.ts:96) or field-completion without channel proof, and some may lack CNP entirely; reclassifying them (declared vs verified vs neither) is a data-correctness migration with compliance implications for already-submitted policies.
- Merge semantics are genuinely hard: an anonymous shell and the claimed Customer can each hold an open application, divergent DNT state, or conflicting declared fields; without deterministic engine-owned conflict rules (coordinated with dnt-sessions and application-lifecycle), merge becomes an LLM judgment call — exactly what the architecture forbids.
- CNP as a match/dedup key is currently impossible (random-IV AES-GCM ciphertext is unsearchable) and adding a blind index creates a new sensitive artifact; getting the hashing scheme wrong either re-identifies CNPs or silently breaks duplicate detection.
- Two verification flows could diverge: the dashboard magic-link path (User/JWT) already exists and post-payment mints links against it; if chat verification is built as a separate mechanism instead of retargeting the same challenge lifecycle, the current dual-identity split is reproduced one layer up.
- Tightening transport identity (rejecting body-supplied customerId) breaks any existing client, script, or e2e flow that passes customerId explicitly (e.g. app/chat/page.tsx bootstrap, scripts/verify-*.ts sims); the cutover needs the session layer in place first or the funnel goes dark.
- Gating accept_quote on VERIFIED while quotes expire creates a race: a customer who delays the email click can hold an expired quote; quote-lifecycle validity rules must define whether verification pauses, extends, or invalidates the quote window, or customers will hit rejected(quote_expired) through no fault of the flow.
- GDPR erasure (app/api/gdpr/delete-data/route.ts) anonymizes Customer PII while retaining policies/payments; the tier model must define post-erasure identity (verified status revoked, channels cleared) or an erased customer could still 'claim' retained records via a stale verified session.
- Strict identity gates at set_application raise the abandonment cliff exactly where the funnel converts; if the declared-tier field collection is not driven deterministically (today the agent cannot even call collect_customer_field due to the dead save_customer_field grants), conversations will stall at the gate with the engine demanding fields the agent has no exposed action to collect.

---

## T5. Application lifecycle: set_application freeze, DNT ordering, multi-app, resume/prefill + tier/level selection placement

> Topic key: `application-lifecycle`

### Current state (code-grounded)

APPLICATION CREATION & DNT ORDERING — lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts: startApplication (line 29) hard-gates on Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil (lines 35-40) — DNT must be signed BEFORE the application exists, the inverse of the catalog (application first, DNT gates the questionnaire inside @application). No identity check exists anywhere in startApplication — anonymous customers can start applications. Product resolves from context.product ?? Conversation.productId ?? candidateProductId (line 47); creating the app also commits the candidate to Conversation.productId (lines 97-99). Optional tierCode/levelCode/includesAddon args resolve to Application.tierId/levelId/includesAddon (lines 50-75) AND are dual-written as Answer rows for PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST so getNextQuestion skips them (lines 83-95).

SCOPING — prisma/schema.prisma: Application (lines 490-512) has conversationId @unique (exactly one application per conversation), customerId, nullable tierId/levelId, includesAddon, ApplicationStatus enum = OPEN/PAUSED/COMPLETED only (lines 21-25) — no CANCELLED, no QUOTED. cancelApplication (application-handlers.ts lines 496-528) sets status COMPLETED, making cancelled and successfully-completed applications indistinguishable in data. Answer rows are conversation-scoped: @@unique([questionId, conversationId]) (schema line 483) — answers cannot follow a customer across conversations and two applications in one conversation would collide. Quote.applicationId is @unique (line 516) — one quote row per application; generate_quote (quote-handlers.ts line 189) always does prisma.quote.create with no existing-quote check.

SELECTION (tier/level/addon) lives in FOUR places today: (1) start_application args (above); (2) engine questions — prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts lines 577-657 seed PACKAGE_CHOICE, PREMIUM_LEVEL, BD_ADDON_INTEREST, PAYMENT_FREQUENCY plus HEALTH_DECLARATION_CONFIRM into the 'application' QuestionGroup (phase='application'), with side-effect mapping in saveApplicationAnswer (application-handlers.ts lines 279-301) and the generic set_answer (set-answer-handlers.ts lines 51-81; PREMIUM_LEVEL silently no-ops when tierId is null, line 68); (3) change_selection (change-selection-handlers.ts) — in-place tier/level/addon mutation any time pre-acceptance, expires DRAFT quote, re-upserts the Answer rows (lines 92-109); (4) UI buttons — lib/chat/action-adapter.ts lines 34-52 map select_tier/select_level to save_application_answer with field=PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL. set_candidate_product (candidate-handlers.ts lines 71-78) carries ONLY productId + confidence — no tier/level/addons, so nothing exists to freeze. switch_product (product-switch-handler.ts) re-points Conversation.productId and nulls the application's tier/level/addon (lines 54-68) but does NOT update Application.productId — Application.productId diverges from Conversation.productId; deriveState computes missing[] from Application.productId (lib/chat/derive-state.ts line 156) while handlers use the conversation product via resolveActiveProductId (lib/engines/question-groups.ts lines 30-40).

NO FREEZE ANYWHERE — modify_quote (quote-handlers.ts lines 449-527) expires the quote, REOPENS the completed application (status OPEN, completedAt null, tier/level nulled) and deletes the selection answers — the direct opposite of the catalog's 'quote completes the application, immutable thereafter; post-quote change = cancel + new application'.

RESUME/PREFILL — resumeApplication (application-handlers.ts lines 432-490) only flips PAUSED→OPEN for the SAME conversation's application; it is an unpause tool, not the catalog's cross-session position read. get_last_application_info, get_open_items, get_application_list, identify_customer do not exist anywhere in lib/ (verified by grep). No prefill mechanism exists. DNT is conversation-scoped (sign_dnt writes Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil +365d, dnt-handlers.ts lines 295-301) so the 1-year validity is never honored for a returning customer in a new conversation. Identity: collect_customer_field (data-handlers.ts) flips Customer.isAnonymous=false only after ALL of name/cnp/dateOfBirth/email/phone are collected (lines 241-245); generate_quote falls back to age 30 when dateOfBirth is missing (quote-handlers.ts line 63).

PHASE MODEL — derive-state.ts determinePhase (lines 34-49) encodes the current ordering: product set → CONSENT (gdpr+DNT) → SELECTION → start_application → QUESTIONNAIRE → QUOTE → CLOSING; nextBestAction for SELECTION says 'record via change_selection (or pass tier/level/addon to start_application)' (line 56).

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** change_selection (change-selection-handlers.ts) — in-place tier/level/addon mutation any time pre-acceptance
  **Correction:** The handler has no pre-acceptance boundary of any kind. changeSelection never checks quote status before mutating: it looks up the application (lines 20-25), computes changes, and only expires a quote when `existingQuote.status === 'DRAFT'` (lines 86-90). If the quote is already ACCEPTED, the ACCEPTED quote is left intact while Application.tierId/levelId/includesAddon and the Answer rows are still mutated (lines 92-109). The tool is also in DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS (lib/chat/default-tools.ts line 17), which the orchestrator merges in as an always-available baseline (lib/chat/orchestrator.ts line 414), so it remains callable after accept_quote. The accurate statement is: change_selection is available at ANY time once an application exists — including post-acceptance, where it silently desynchronizes the accepted quote from the application's selection. _(lib/tools/handlers/change-selection-handlers.ts:16-25 (only guards: at-least-one-arg + application exists), :86-90 (expiry conditional on status === 'DRAFT' only; ACCEPTED untouched), :92-109 (mutations proceed regardless); lib/chat/default-tools.ts:17; lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:414)_

### Gaps

- No identity gate on application creation: startApplication (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts lines 29-48) never checks Customer.isAnonymous; identify_customer does not exist; catalog requires set_application -> requires_identity.
- DNT ordering inverted vs catalog: DNT signature is a precondition of start_application (application-handlers.ts lines 35-40) instead of the first gate inside @application; deriveState's CONSENT-before-SELECTION phase rule (derive-state.ts lines 44-47) bakes the inverted ordering into the phase model.
- DNT is conversation-scoped (Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil) — a returning customer with a valid 1-year DNT must re-sign in every new conversation; the catalog's 'valid DNT skips straight to questionnaire' is impossible today. No products_covered/product-type coverage model exists.
- No frozen snapshot exists: the candidate carries no tier/level/addons (candidate-handlers.ts), switch_product mutates the application in place, and modify_quote (quote-handlers.ts lines 449-527) reopens a COMPLETED application and deletes answers — violating 'one application -> one quote, immutable after quote'.
- No catalog tool has tier/level selection (set_application takes product_id + addon_ids only) while Zeno's entire pricing model is PricingTier/PricingLevel — the selection gap; today selection is split across four divergence-prone paths (start_application args, PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST engine questions, change_selection, UI action-adapter), each dual-writing Answer rows + Application columns.
- Application is conversation-scoped (Application.conversationId @unique) and Answer is conversation-scoped (@@unique([questionId, conversationId])) — multi-application-per-customer, cross-conversation resume, get_open_items, and get_application_list are structurally impossible.
- resume_application only unpauses a PAUSED app in the same conversation (application-handlers.ts lines 432-449); the catalog's resume_application is a READ returning current position for any incomplete application.
- get_last_application_info, get_open_items, get_application_list do not exist (grep over lib/ confirms); no prefill mechanism of any kind exists.
- ApplicationStatus has no CANCELLED or REFERRED value; cancel_application records COMPLETED (application-handlers.ts lines 511-514), corrupting any future get_open_items/get_application_list semantics.
- Latent defect: Quote.applicationId is @unique and generate_quote always quote.create (quote-handlers.ts line 189) with no existing-quote handling — after change_selection expires a DRAFT quote, the promised re-quote will throw a unique-constraint violation.
- Live divergence: switch_product updates Conversation.productId but not Application.productId (product-switch-handler.ts lines 35-68), so deriveState (keyed on Application.productId, derive-state.ts line 156) and the question handlers (keyed on the conversation product) compute question sets for different products.
- PAYMENT_FREQUENCY is an underwriting-questionnaire question (seed-questions.ts lines 640-653) but the catalog places payment options in get_quote_info / accept_quote(payment_option).
- PREMIUM_LEVEL set via set_answer silently no-ops when no tier is set (set-answer-handlers.ts line 68) — an invalid state (level answered, levelId null) is recorded without error.
- generate_quote prices with a fabricated fallback age of 30 when dateOfBirth is missing (quote-handlers.ts lines 62-75) — a direct consequence of the missing identity gate.

### Decision points

#### T5.D1 — Ordering: should the DNT remain a precondition of creating the application (current), or should the application be created first with the (customer-scoped) DNT as the first gate inside @application blocking the underwriting questionnaire (catalog)?

- **dnt-first (status quo)**: Keep startApplication's gate (application-handlers.ts lines 35-40): DNT signed on the Conversation before any application exists; deriveState keeps CONSENT before SELECTION.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simple legality rule, but architecturally wrong on three counts: (1) the DNT is a needs analysis about the customer with 1-year validity, yet conversation scoping forces re-signing every conversation, making validity semantics a fiction; (2) until consent completes there is no application entity, so an interrupted pre-DNT funnel has no engine-visible artifact for get_open_items/resume to anchor on; (3) the catalog's returning-customer skip (valid DNT -> straight to questionnaire) is unimplementable.
- **✅ Recommended — application-first, customer-scoped DNT (catalog)**: set_application creates the application immediately when intent is committed (requires identity). DNT becomes a customer-scoped record (signedAt/validUntil/product-types-covered on Customer or a Dnt entity). The legality engine exposes the underwriting questionnaire only when a valid DNT covers the application's product type; otherwise blocked with requires_consent and the DNT sub-flow is offered inside @application.
  _Tradeoffs:_ The application becomes the stable aggregate root from the moment of intent — DNT-session state, questionnaire progress, flags, and resume semantics all hang off one entity, and the gate becomes a declarative exposure rule ('get_next_question exposed iff dnt.valid_for(product.type)') instead of an imperative precondition scattered in a handler. Returning customers with valid DNT skip correctly. Requires the legality engine to actually enforce the questionnaire block, or underwriting data could be collected before the needs analysis — a compliance inversion that the current hard gate cannot produce.
- **hybrid: DNT-first but customer-scoped**: Keep the current ordering (DNT before application) but move DNT storage to the customer so returning customers skip it.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Fixes the re-signing absurdity but keeps the structural problem: pre-application funnel state still has no anchor entity, the phase model still needs a synthetic CONSENT phase outside the application, and the DNT gate stays an imperative check inside start_application rather than an engine-computed exposure rule — exactly the kind of handler-resident business rule the target architecture removes.

**Rationale:** The application is the natural aggregate root for everything that follows intent — DNT session, questionnaire, flags, quote. Creating it first makes every gate (DNT, identity, disclosures) an engine-computed exposure condition on a single entity rather than imperative preconditions strung across handlers, which is precisely the 'engine decides legality' invariant. Customer scoping is forced by the DNT's own semantics (1-year validity, product-type coverage): a document that outlives the conversation cannot live on the conversation. The compliance ordering (needs analysis before underwriting) is preserved — it moves from a creation-time gate to a questionnaire-exposure gate, which is strictly more faithful to IDD intent since the application record itself contains no risk data yet.

**Depends on / interacts with:** dnt-sessions, identity, legality-engine, phase-model

#### T5.D2 — Where does tier/level/addon selection live (the selection gap), and what happens to change_selection and switch_product mid-application?

- **selection on the candidate, frozen at set_application**: Extend the candidate to (productId, addonIds, tierCode, levelCode); set_candidate_product carries all of it; set_application freezes the full selection; any change afterwards = cancel + new application.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Maximally faithful to 'frozen snapshot of candidate', and a single owner pre-application. But tier/level is a pricing decision customers legitimately revisit after seeing coverage detail and the DNT-informed recommendation — freezing it at creation makes the single most common change-of-mind (tier upgrade, level downgrade) a destructive cancel+recreate, and it inverts demands-and-needs ordering: the customer commits a coverage level before the needs analysis that is supposed to inform it.
- **selection as engine questions (status quo, formalized)**: Keep PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST as questions in the underwriting questionnaire (seed-questions.ts lines 601-639), answered via write_question_answer, edited via modify_answer while incomplete; retire change_selection as redundant.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One uniform answer pipeline and free resume/prefill (selections are just answers). But tier/level are commercial choices, not underwriting facts: encoding them as questions conflates risk data with pricing selection, perpetuates today's dual-write (Answer row + Application.tierId synced in three handlers — application-handlers.ts 279-301, set-answer-handlers.ts 51-81, change-selection-handlers.ts 92-109, with the silent PREMIUM_LEVEL no-op), and corrupts the consequence taxonomy — changing tier is re_rating, not cascade_invalidate, so modify_answer would need question-specific consequence carve-outs.
- **✅ Recommended — dedicated selection commit inside @application (select_coverage)**: One first-class commit — select_coverage(application_id, tier, level, addon_ids) — legal between set_application and generate_quote (DNT not required to select, only to answer underwriting questions). Application.tierId/levelId/addons become the single store; PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST leave the question group; the engine blocks generate_quote until selection is complete (replacing quote-handlers.ts lines 46-51's error with a blocked_actions reason). change_selection's behavior becomes this tool's re-invocation: consequence re_rating, plus cascade_expand/questions_removed when the addon toggles the bd_medical group. switch_product mid-application becomes illegal (product is frozen) — engine returns rejected; the correct path is cancel_application + set_candidate_product + set_application, prefilled.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Single writer, no dual store, no Answer/column sync; the consequence vocabulary fits exactly (re_rating for tier/level, cascade_expand/questions_removed for addons); GUI tier buttons and the agent call the identical commit (swap test). It adds one tool beyond the catalog's surface — a deliberate, documented extension since the catalog simply has no slot for tier/level — and the DNT-informed recommendation can precede selection because selection sits after application creation, alongside (not inside) the questionnaire.

**Rationale:** Tier/level/addon selection is a commercial pricing decision with its own consequence semantics (re_rating, addon-driven question-set changes) — it is neither part of the application's identity (which is the underwriting subject: product + customer) nor an underwriting fact (a question answer). Giving it its own commit makes it a single-writer store, lets the legality engine express 'generate_quote blocked: selection incomplete' as a computed reason, and resolves the catalog's gap without contorting either the candidate (premature freeze) or the questionnaire (taxonomy corruption). Retiring switch_product-mid-application also eliminates the live Application.productId/Conversation.productId divergence by construction.

**Depends on / interacts with:** questionnaire-consequences, quote-lifecycle, tool-mapping, product-data, legality-engine

#### T5.D3 — What does 'frozen snapshot' mean concretely — which fields freeze at set_application and what stays editable until the quote?

- **✅ Recommended — freeze product only**: set_application freezes Application.productId (copied from the candidate). Addons, tier, and level live in the mutable selection (select_coverage) until generate_quote; quote issuance freezes the entire application.
  _Tradeoffs:_ The frozen identity is exactly the underwriting subject: the product determines the question-set skeleton and the DNT product-type requirement, so freezing it keeps every downstream computation stable, while addon/tier/level changes remain expressible through the consequence taxonomy (re_rating, cascade_expand for bd_medical when the addon is added, questions_removed when dropped). Diverges from the catalog's literal set_application(product_id, addon_ids[]) signature — addons passed at creation become initial selection values rather than frozen fields.
- **freeze product + addons (catalog literal)**: set_application(product_id, addon_ids[]) freezes both; only tier/level remain editable pre-quote.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches the catalog signature, but addon membership changes the question set (bd_medical) and the premium — the two things the consequence taxonomy exists to govern in-flight. Freezing addons turns 'actually, add the treatment-abroad cover' — a routine mid-funnel pivot the engine could handle as cascade_expand — into a destructive cancel+recreate, and contradicts the catalog's own 'in-place edits only while incomplete' assumption.
- **freeze product + addons + tier/level (full snapshot)**: Everything commercial freezes at creation; any change is cancel + new application pre-filled.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Strongest immutability and the simplest audit story (the application is a pure snapshot), but it pushes every change-of-mind through application churn, multiplying cancelled-app noise in get_application_list and making the consequence taxonomy's re_rating/cascade values nearly unreachable — a model where the engine's most expressive machinery is unused is a design smell.

**Rationale:** Freeze what defines the underwriting subject; keep mutable what the consequence engine is built to govern. The product is the only field whose change invalidates the application's reason for existing (different question groups, different DNT coverage, different pricing universe) — hence frozen, with product change = cancel + new application. Addon/tier/level changes are exactly re_rating/cascade_expand/questions_removed events, and routing them through in-place commits preserves data integrity (one application history shows the customer's real path) while the post-quote boundary ('quote completes the application, immutable thereafter') supplies the hard freeze where it matters for one-app-one-quote. The catalog is a conceptual target; its set_application signature predates the tier/level reality.

**Depends on / interacts with:** questionnaire-consequences, quote-lifecycle, commit-envelope, legality-engine

#### T5.D4 — Application scoping and multiplicity: conversation-scoped (today) vs customer-scoped, how many open applications, and how resume works across conversations?

- **conversation-scoped (status quo)**: Keep Application.conversationId @unique; one application per conversation; resume only within the conversation.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches every existing query path, but structurally forbids the catalog's returning-customer flows: get_open_items, get_application_list, resume days later in a new conversation, and post-quote re-application all require the customer to own applications. It also entrenches conversation-scoped Answers, which block multi-app and prefill permanently.
- **customer-scoped, unlimited open applications**: Applications belong to the customer; any number may be open; conversations point at the one in focus.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Maximally flexible, but several open applications for the same product create genuine ambiguity (which one is 'the' funnel? which does get_dnt_state/resume target?) and a duplicate-policy risk the backlog explicitly flags — ambiguity the legality engine would have to resolve with arbitrary rules.
- **✅ Recommended — customer-scoped, at most one open per product**: Application.customerId becomes the owning scope with a partial-unique constraint (customerId, productId, status=OPEN/PAUSED); Conversation gets an activeApplicationId pointer (the channel). Underwriting answers re-key from (questionId, conversationId) to (questionId, applicationId); customer-stable facts move to the CustomerProfile SSOT. get_open_items lists the customer's open apps/quotes/payments; resume_application(application_id) becomes a read returning current position, callable from any conversation.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches the catalog's identity-keyed reads exactly, permits parallel interest across product types (forward-looking home/car/life) while making 'which application?' always answerable per product, and the answer re-keying is what makes resume and prefill carry actual data. Requires identity at set_application — an anonymous browser cannot own a durable application — so this option is inseparable from the identity gate.
- **customer-scoped, one open total**: A single open application per customer across all products.
