  _Tradeoffs:_ Simplest open-items semantics, but blocks the legitimate multi-product case the catalog anticipates (get_dnt_state's products_covered by type only matters if a customer can pursue more than one product), trading future flexibility for a constraint with no integrity benefit over per-product uniqueness.

**Rationale:** The catalog's read surface (get_application_list, get_open_items, get_last_application_info — all keyed by identity) is only satisfiable if the customer owns applications; the conversation is a channel, consistent with the CustomerProfile SSOT direction. Per-product uniqueness gives determinism (every product-scoped action has exactly one possible target) without forbidding multi-product journeys, and it is the natural guard against duplicate coverage. Re-keying underwriting answers to the application is the load-bearing move: it simultaneously fixes multi-app collisions, cross-conversation resume, and gives prefill a well-defined source. With today's single 'protect' product this behaves identically to one-open-total, so nothing is lost in the present.

**Depends on / interacts with:** identity, dnt-sessions, legality-engine, quote-lifecycle, product-data

#### T5.D5 — Prefill for post-quote re-application (get_last_application_info): what is the data source and how are the Gherkin's 're-confirm every answer' rules enforced?

- **silent copy**: On set_application after a prior completed app, copy the prior application's answer rows into the new one; the questionnaire engine skips them as already answered.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Fastest user path, but underwriting answers (including the health declaration, seed-questions.ts lines 588-599) get committed without fresh customer attestation — a misrepresentation exposure on a regulated document — and the data cannot distinguish 'confirmed now' from 'confirmed months ago', defeating the backlog's answer-freshness concern. Directly violates the Gherkin ('re-confirms every answer including the one being changed', zeno_workflow.feature lines 362-366).
- **✅ Recommended — prefill as per-question proposals**: get_last_application_info is a pure read over the prior application's answers (catalog marks it R). The new application starts with zero answers; get_next_question returns each question with a suggested_answer from the prior app; the agent (or GUI) presents it for one-tap confirmation and each confirmation is a real write_question_answer commit, timestamped now.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Every answer in the new application is a first-class commit made in that application — uniform audit trail, correct freshness, and the changed answer flows through the identical cascade machinery as any other answer (if the new value branches differently, cascade_expand fires naturally). Schema drift is handled for free: a question added since the old app simply has no suggestion. The conversational cost (one confirmation per question) is a UX property, not an architectural one — and it is exactly what the Gherkin mandates.
- **copy-then-bulk-ratify**: Copy prior answers flagged unconfirmed; a single confirm_prefill commit ratifies all at once; individual edits before ratification go through modify_answer.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Fewer round-trips than per-question confirmation while keeping an attestation step, but the attestation is not per-question (weaker audit value on health declarations), it introduces a third answer state (unconfirmed) that every read path and the legality engine must handle, and it is undefined what happens when a copied answer is now invalid against a changed question schema — the bulk ratify would commit data no single write_question_answer would accept.

**Rationale:** Correctness and compliance both demand that every answer in the new application be an attestation made in that application: the per-question proposal model achieves this with zero new states, zero special validation paths, and full reuse of the existing answer/cascade machinery — the changed answer that motivated the re-application is just another confirmed write with its normal consequence. It also keeps get_last_application_info a side-effect-free read, matching its R classification, and composes with the CustomerProfile SSOT: stable customer facts (DOB, occupation) come from the profile, while only true underwriting answers go through the confirm loop.

**Depends on / interacts with:** questionnaire-consequences, quote-lifecycle, identity, commit-envelope

#### T5.D6 — Application status model: what terminal and intermediate states does the lifecycle need (today: OPEN/PAUSED/COMPLETED, with cancel writing COMPLETED)?

- **keep three statuses, encode intent in metadata**: Keep OPEN/PAUSED/COMPLETED and record cancellation/referral reasons in flagsForReview JSON.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No enum migration, but the primary lifecycle fact lives in untyped JSON: get_open_items and get_application_list cannot distinguish a quoted application from an abandoned one without parsing metadata, and the one-quote-per-application invariant ('completed = quoted = immutable') is unenforceable when COMPLETED also means cancelled (application-handlers.ts lines 511-514).
- **✅ Recommended — explicit lifecycle enum**: ApplicationStatus = OPEN, PAUSED (flag escalation, resumable), REFERRED (manual underwriting, per generate_quote's referred consequence), COMPLETED (quote issued — the only path in, set by generate_quote, immutable thereafter), CANCELLED (terminal via cancel_application's requires_confirmation -> terminal). resume_application legal only for OPEN/PAUSED; get_open_items lists OPEN/PAUSED/REFERRED; get_last_application_info reads the latest COMPLETED.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Every catalog read and exposure rule becomes a direct status predicate — the legality engine's 'exposed when' conditions compile to enum checks, the immutability boundary is the COMPLETED transition itself, and cancelled apps stop polluting completion semantics. The status machine is engine-owned: handlers can no longer improvise transitions (modify_quote's reopen becomes structurally impossible because no transition COMPLETED->OPEN exists).
- **status enum + separate terminal flag**: Small enum (OPEN/CLOSED) plus closedReason and isTerminal columns.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Avoids enum growth but splits one fact across columns; invariants like 'no writes after quote' need compound predicates instead of a single state check, and nothing in the domain calls for distinguishing closure mechanics from state — the lifecycle genuinely has five distinct, behaviorally different states.

**Rationale:** The legality engine's whole premise is that exposure and consequence rules are computed from state — that requires state to be honest. Five behaviorally distinct situations (answering, paused-for-flag, referred-to-human, quoted-immutable, cancelled-terminal) deserve five values; the moment COMPLETED stops meaning two contradictory things, one-application-one-quote becomes a database-level truth (COMPLETED iff quote exists), get_open_items becomes a trivial correct query, and the catalog's terminal consequence maps to exactly one transition. This decision is upstream of resume, prefill, and open-items semantics — all three consume these statuses.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, quote-lifecycle, commit-envelope, tool-mapping

### Risks

- Compliance inversion if the ordering flip ships without engine enforcement: once the application exists before the DNT, the ONLY thing preventing underwriting-data collection before the needs analysis is the legality engine's questionnaire block — today that gate is an imperative check inside start_application (application-handlers.ts lines 35-40) and deriveState's CONSENT phase (derive-state.ts lines 44-47), both of which encode the OLD ordering and must be rewritten in the same change, not after.
- Answer re-keying must move atomically with application re-scoping: deriveState progress (derive-state.ts lines 158-173), getNextQuestion, calculateProgress, and generate_quote's PAYMENT_FREQUENCY lookup (quote-handlers.ts lines 144-152) all key answers by conversationId; customer-scoped applications with conversation-scoped answers would silently compute 0% progress or read another conversation's answers.
- Latent P2002 defect in the current re-quote path: Quote.applicationId is @unique and generate_quote always prisma.quote.create (quote-handlers.ts line 189) — change_selection promises 'a new quote on your next request' after expiring the DRAFT (change-selection-handlers.ts lines 86-90) but the create will violate the unique constraint; any redesign keeping expire-then-regenerate must change quote cardinality (one-to-many with single-DRAFT invariant) or it inherits this failure.
- Live product-divergence bug until switch_product is retired: Application.productId is never updated by switch_product, so question sets, deriveState.missing[], and addon pricing (generate_quote uses application.productId, quote-handlers.ts line 113 area) can disagree about which product is being sold — quotes can mix one product's questions with another's pricing.
- Funnel deadlock if identity gating lands before identify_customer exists: set_application -> requires_identity with no exposed identity action reproduces the historical advance-flow deadlock pattern (prompt/engine demanding a tool that does not exist); collect_customer_field's all-five-fields threshold (data-handlers.ts lines 241-245) is too heavy to serve as the identity commit.
- Removing PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST/PAYMENT_FREQUENCY from the question group breaks the GUI swap-path: action-adapter select_tier/select_level map to save_application_answer with those field codes (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts lines 34-52), and modify_quote's answer-deletion (quote-handlers.ts lines 484-497), seeds, e2e change-of-mind scenario, and personas all reference them — GUI and agent must converge on the new select_coverage commit or the swap test fails.
- modify_quote retirement is a behavioral break: today's UI 'modify_quote' button reopens a completed application; under the target model that flow becomes cancel + new application with prefill — if the old tool survives in any pack/UI path it will violate the immutability invariant the whole quote lifecycle depends on.
- Prefill-as-proposals needs engine support for suggested_answer in get_next_question; without it the agent will be tempted to batch-fabricate confirmations from prior answers, which is indistinguishable from silent copy and defeats the attestation requirement.
- DNT product-type coverage (products_covered) has no data model and only one product type exists in the catalog ('protect', LIFE) — coverage-matching logic will ship untested against real multi-product data, so its rules must be property-tested synthetically or the returning-customer skip may misfire when home/car products land.
- generate_quote's silent age-30 fallback (quote-handlers.ts lines 62-75) means quotes can be priced on fabricated data today; under application-first ordering, identity (hence DOB) arrives at set_application, but only if the identity gate is enforced — otherwise the fallback becomes more reachable, not less.

---

## T6. Questionnaire consequence engine: answer dependency schema + modify_answer cascades

> Topic key: `questionnaire-consequences`

### Current state (code-grounded)

All paths relative to C:/GitHub/Zeno/.claude/worktrees/unruffled-pike-1535df.

DATA MODEL (prisma/schema.prisma): Question (lines 448-471) carries the only dependency mechanism today: `parentQuestionId` (self-FK, relation "questionBranching") + `showWhenValue` (string: exact match, comma-list, or "true"/"false"). A question can have AT MOST ONE parent (scalar FK) — no multi-parent, no AND-conditions, no dependency kind. Answer (lines 473-484) is conversation-scoped (@@unique([questionId, conversationId])) with only `value` + `answeredAt` — no invalidatedAt, no history, no causality; every write is a destructive upsert. QuestionGroup (433-446) has `phase` ('dnt'|'application') and optional productId. Application (490-512) has status OPEN|PAUSED|COMPLETED (enum at line 21), tierId/levelId/includesAddon, flagsForReview Json, totalQuestions snapshot. There is NO QuestionDependency table, NO consequence engine, NO answer-revision table.

ENGINE (lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.ts): shouldShowQuestion (lines 68-104) is pure visibility evaluation: no parent → visible; parent unanswered → hidden; showWhenValue match (comma-list, boolean-normalized, or exact). getNextQuestion (389-480) loads all questions for group codes, applies shouldShowQuestion, returns first visible-unanswered + progress over the VISIBLE set. validateAnswer (111-239) handles type/range/options; checkForFlags (247-291) reads validationRules.flagAnswers ({value, action: flag|escalate|reject, reason}). calculateProgress (485-534) also visibility-filtered. Group codes come from lib/engines/question-groups.ts resolveGroupCodes(productId, phase).

REAL QUESTION GRAPH (prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts): 8 groups, 37 questions. Application-phase questions: group 'application' = HEALTH_DECLARATION_CONFIRM (flagAnswers: value 'false' → escalate, line 598), PACKAGE_CHOICE (standard|optim), PREMIUM_LEVEL (level_1..3), BD_ADDON_INTEREST (boolean), PAYMENT_FREQUENCY; group 'bd_medical' = BD_CANCER_HISTORY, BD_CARDIOVASCULAR, BD_NEUROLOGICAL, BD_TRANSPLANT, BD_CHRONIC_CONDITIONS, BD_HOSPITALIZATION_RECENT (all boolean, riskWeight 10). DNT questions include DNT_CNP, DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE, DNT_LIFE_FAMILY_INCOME, DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_IMPORTANCE etc. Exactly ONE dependency edge exists in the entire seed: DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_PREFERENCE → parent DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_IMPORTANCE, showWhenValue 'somewhat,quite_important,very_important' (lines 564-565). The group descriptions CLAIM conditionality ("shown when DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE = financial_and_investment", lines 325, 479, 536) but no edges implement it. bd_medical is NOT gated on BD_ADDON_INTEREST — its 6 questions are unconditionally part of the application flow (resolveGroupCodes returns both groups for phase 'application'). The seed helper cannot even express cross-group parents: questionIdMap is per-group (seed-questions.ts:59-67).

ANSWER WRITE PATHS — five independent writers, none with cascade logic: (1) lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts saveApplicationAnswer (127-386): validates, checks flags (escalate → status PAUSED + flagsForReview append), upserts, hardcoded side-effects for PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST (tierId/levelId/includesAddon), marks COMPLETED when getNextQuestion returns null (328-334). (2) lib/tools/handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts setAnswer (18-119): "answer any question by code, supports editing" — upserts with NO application-status guard (works even on COMPLETED apps post-quote), same tier/level/addon side-effects, no cascade, no flag re-check. (3) lib/tools/handlers/change-selection-handlers.ts changeSelection: updates tier/level/addon + mirrors answers, expires DRAFT quote; if tier changes WITHOUT level, application.levelId keeps pointing at the OLD tier's level row (lines 53-69 only touch level when levelArg passed) — a live validity-cascade hole. (4) lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts modifyQuote (449-530): the ONLY cascade-like code in the repo — hard-deletes 4 hardcoded answer codes (PACKAGE_CHOICE, PREMIUM_LEVEL, BD_ADDON_INTEREST, PAYMENT_FREQUENCY), reverts status COMPLETED→OPEN, nulls tierId/levelId but NOT includesAddon (473-482), expires the quote. (5) dnt-handlers.ts:177 (DNT upsert path). Catalog tools modify_answer / write_question_answer / get_next_question do not exist as tools (registry names verified in lib/tools/registry.ts: set_answer, save_application_answer, change_selection, modify_quote, check_bd_eligibility...).

PROGRESS DIVERGENCE: lib/chat/derive-state.ts (154-173) computes application.required/answered/missing over ALL questions in the application groups with NO shouldShowQuestion filtering — it disagrees with questionnaire-engine progress the moment branching exists, lists invisible questions as 'missing', and counts zombie answers of removed questions as answered.

ELIGIBILITY TODAY: Product.eligibility Json exists (schema.prisma:111; seeded minAge 18 / maxAge 64, prisma/seeds/seed-product.ts:146-152) but generate_quote (quote-handlers.ts:19-200) never enforces it — age (fallback hardcoded 30 when no dateOfBirth, line 63) is used only to filter coverage rows and match addon pricing rules. BD eligibility is a separate agent-invoked tool check_bd_eligibility (lib/tools/handlers/bd-handlers.ts) that requires all 6 BD answers, and on any 'true' SILENTLY sets application.includesAddon=false (lines 58-65) — an engine decision living behind agent discretion.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** "ANSWER WRITE PATHS — five independent writers, none with cascade logic: (1) saveApplicationAnswer, (2) setAnswer, (3) changeSelection, (4) modifyQuote, (5) dnt-handlers.ts:177" (repeated in risks: "five Answer write paths exist today (save_application_answer, set_answer, change_selection, modify_quote, dnt-handlers)")
  **Correction:** Undercount. There is a sixth handler-level Answer write path the enumeration omits: startApplication's recordSelection pre-fill, which upserts PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST Answer rows when an application is created with tier/level/addon args (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:83-95, prisma.answer.upsert at line 86). The report is internally inconsistent: its own DP6 'pure-planner' option lists 'application creation pre-fill' among the writers that must route through the planner. Additionally, app/api/gdpr/delete-data/route.ts:116 performs prisma.answer.deleteMany (GDPR erasure) — a further non-engine Answer mutation path relevant to the 'exactly one write path' risk, though arguably not a business 'writer'. All other characterizations of the listed five paths are accurate. _(lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:83-95 (recordSelection upsert at line 86, called at lines 92-95); app/api/gdpr/delete-data/route.ts:116; repo-wide grep for prisma.answer.(upsert|create|update|delete) returns write sites in application-handlers.ts (86, 189, 254), set-answer-handlers.ts:45, change-selection-handlers.ts:100, quote-handlers.ts:491, dnt-handlers.ts:177, and app/api/gdpr/delete-data/route.ts:116)_
- **Claim:** "generate_quote (quote-handlers.ts:19-200) never enforces it" — line range citation 19-200 for generateQuote
  **Correction:** Minor citation error: the generateQuote function spans lines 19-255 of lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts (quote creation at 189-214, return payload through 251, catch through 255). The behavioral claims attached to the citation are all correct: Product.eligibility is never read or enforced in generateQuote (product loaded at 162-164 only for quoteValidityDays at 183), the age-30 fallback is at line 63, and customerAge is used only to filter age-based coverage rows (84-93) and match addon pricing rules (122-124). _(lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:19 (function start) and :255 (function end); :63 (let customerAge = 30 // fallback); :162-183 (product used only for quoteValidityDays))_
- **Claim:** DP1 rationale: "PREMIUM_LEVEL→PACKAGE_CHOICE is a real validity dependency enforced ad hoc in three handlers"
  **Correction:** Minor undercount: four handlers contain the ad hoc tier-scoped level resolution, not three. startApplication also scopes the PricingLevel lookup by tierId and rejects levelCode without tierCode (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:57-63), in addition to saveApplicationAnswer (application-handlers.ts:288-297), setAnswer (set-answer-handlers.ts:68-73), and changeSelection (change-selection-handlers.ts:53-69). The substantive point (the dependency is enforced ad hoc per-handler and violated by change_selection's tier-without-level path) is verified correct. _(lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:57-63 (startApplication: 'levelCode requires tierCode' + findFirst({ where: { tierId, code: levelCode } })); application-handlers.ts:288-297; set-answer-handlers.ts:68-73; change-selection-handlers.ts:53-69)_

### Gaps

- No consequence engine exists: all five Answer write paths upsert destructively with zero cascade computation; the only cascade-like behavior is the hardcoded 4-question delete in modifyQuote (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:484-497).
- The dependency graph is essentially empty where the domain requires it: exactly one parentQuestionId edge exists (DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_PREFERENCE); the DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE gating of dnt_life_financial/investment/sustainability groups is documented in seed descriptions but unimplemented; bd_medical's 6 questions are asked unconditionally even when BD_ADDON_INTEREST=false.
- Validity dependencies are expressed nowhere: PREMIUM_LEVEL's meaning depends on PACKAGE_CHOICE (level codes repeat across tiers; levelId is tier-scoped) yet no mechanism invalidates the level when the tier changes — change_selection can leave application.levelId pointing at the old tier's level, and generate_quote prices from that stale pricingLevel.
- Answer model has no audit/causality fields (no invalidatedAt, no superseded history, no 'cleared because X changed'); modifying an underwriting declaration overwrites the prior value irrecoverably — an IDD/audit problem for an insurance flow.
- deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:154-173) and questionnaire-engine compute progress differently (unfiltered vs visibility-filtered); there is no single canonical 'visible question set' computation, which a cascade engine requires.
- No application-incomplete-only guard on answer modification: set_answer edits answers on COMPLETED applications with an issued quote, violating the catalog's 'modify_answer exposed when application incomplete only' and 'quote completes the application (immutable thereafter)'.
- No requires_confirmation mechanism for sensitive fields; the closest machinery is validationRules.flagAnswers (escalate pauses the application) — and modifying a flagged answer never recomputes flagsForReview, so corrected answers leave stale escalation flags and a PAUSED status.
- Eligibility is not engine-owned: check_bd_eligibility must be remembered by the agent and silently mutates includesAddon; Product.eligibility bounds (minAge/maxAge) are enforced nowhere; generate_quote silently assumes age 30 when dateOfBirth is missing (quote-handlers.ts:63).
- shouldShowQuestion supports only single-parent, equality/in-list predicates — no multi-parent AND conditions, no cross-question validity predicates; the seed helper cannot create cross-group parent links at all (questionIdMap is per-group, prisma/seeds/seed-questions.ts:59-67).
- Catalog tools get_next_question (with branching_metadata), write_question_answer, modify_answer do not exist; current next-question payloads (application-handlers.ts:351-382) carry no provenance for why a question appeared.
- cancel_application sets status COMPLETED (application-handlers.ts:511-514), conflating cancellation with completion — any cascade/status-recompute logic keyed on COMPLETED would misfire on cancelled applications (owned by application-lifecycle, but blocks clean status semantics here).

### Decision points

#### T6.D1 — How should answer dependencies be represented so the engine can compute invalidation (validity), not just visibility?

- **derive-from-visibility**: Keep parentQuestionId/showWhenValue as the only edges; treat 'child becomes invisible or its gate value changed' as the invalidation signal. No schema change.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Conflates two distinct semantics: a question can stay VISIBLE while its answer becomes INVALID (PREMIUM_LEVEL stays on screen when PACKAGE_CHOICE changes, but the stored level is now scoped to the wrong tier — this dependency exists in business logic today and is invisible to the parentQuestionId graph). Single scalar parent forbids multi-parent conditions (e.g. bd_medical gated on BD_ADDON_INTEREST=true AND addon product active). Cannot type edges, so eligibility participation (which answers feed eligibility rules) has no home. Visibility-only graphs make questions_removed derivable but cascade_invalidate inexpressible without hiding questions.
- **✅ Recommended — explicit-dependency-edges**: New QuestionDependency table: {questionId, dependsOnQuestionId, kind: VISIBILITY|VALIDITY|ELIGIBILITY, predicate: {op: equals|not_equals|in|is_true|is_false|any_answered, value?}}. Migrate the existing parentQuestionId/showWhenValue pair into VISIBILITY edges (then retire those columns) so there is one graph. Engine walks typed edges to compute show-set, invalidation-set, and eligibility-recheck-set from any answer change.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One declarative, queryable source of truth the engine, deriveState, a GUI, and tests all read; multi-parent and cross-group edges become first-class (fixes bd_medical gating and the tier→level validity hole); edge kinds map 1:1 onto the consequence taxonomy (VISIBILITY edges produce cascade_expand/questions_removed, VALIDITY edges produce cascade_invalidate, ELIGIBILITY edges produce eligibility_recheck), making consequences derivable rather than hand-coded. Cost: the predicate DSL is deliberately bounded — conditions beyond equals/in (computed values, arithmetic) need an escape hatch; if parentQuestionId is kept alongside instead of migrated, two sources of truth will drift.
- **rules-as-code**: Per-product TypeScript rule modules (e.g. protectQuestionnaireRules.ts) exporting predicate functions: visibility(question, answers), invalidates(changedQuestion, answers), eligibility(answers).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Unlimited expressiveness (arbitrary boolean logic, computed conditions) and unit-testable as pure functions. But the question catalog stops being data: every new product or rule tweak is a code deploy; the graph is opaque to deriveState/GUI/admin tooling (cannot answer 'what depends on X' without executing code); and it weakens the swap-test property — a non-AI client can read a dependency table but cannot introspect closures. Drifts toward business rules scattered per product, the exact pathology the deterministic-engine direction is meant to kill.

**Rationale:** The decisive test is the question the topic poses: can the representation say 'this answer's VALIDITY depends on that answer' without hiding the question? Only explicit typed edges can. The codebase already contains the counterexample that sinks option (a): PREMIUM_LEVEL→PACKAGE_CHOICE is a real validity dependency enforced ad hoc in three handlers and violated by change_selection (stale levelId under a new tier), while bd_medical→BD_ADDON_INTEREST is a real visibility dependency that simply doesn't exist, because one scalar parent column was never enough. Typed edges additionally make the consequence taxonomy DERIVED rather than asserted: the engine computes cascade_invalidate from VALIDITY edges, cascade_expand/questions_removed from VISIBILITY edges, eligibility_recheck from ELIGIBILITY edges — the same walk powers a dry-run preview for requires_confirmation. Rules-as-code buys expressiveness nothing in the current catalog needs (every seeded condition is an equality/in-list) at the cost of data-driven products and graph introspectability; if a future predicate exceeds the DSL, add a named-predicate registry (edge references a registered pure function) rather than moving the whole graph into code. Migrating parentQuestionId/showWhenValue INTO the table (not alongside it) is mandatory — two dependency stores would reintroduce the deriveState-vs-engine divergence this design must end.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, product-data, tool-mapping, dnt-sessions

#### T6.D2 — When a gating answer changes, what happens to dependent Answer rows, and can Application status revert (COMPLETED→OPEN) before a quote exists?

- **hard-delete-dependents**: Cascade deletes dependent Answer rows (the modifyQuote pattern generalized); progress and status recomputed from the surviving set.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simplest read model (an Answer row = a live answer) and no schema change. But it destroys the underwriting declaration trail: in an insurance flow, 'customer declared having cancer history, then changed it' is exactly the record compliance needs; deletion also erases WHY an answer vanished (user modification vs cascade), making consequence payloads unverifiable after the fact and bugs in cascade scope unrecoverable.
- **mark-stale**: Add invalidatedAt + invalidatedBy (reason enum: USER_MODIFIED|CASCADE|REMOVED_BY_BRANCH, plus the triggering question code/commit id) to Answer. Engine treats invalidated rows as unanswered; re-answering reactivates (clears invalidation, overwrites value).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Preserves the LAST invalidated value and its cause with one migration; queries stay one-row-per-question. But re-answering still overwrites: a value modified twice loses the intermediate state, so the audit trail is partial — you know an answer was invalidated, not the full sequence of declarations. Causality lives on the corpse row only; reconstructing 'what did the application look like when the quote was generated' is impossible.
- **✅ Recommended — append-only-revisions**: Answer becomes append-only: each write creates a revision {value, source: USER_ANSWER|PREFILL|SELECTION_MIRROR, status: ACTIVE|SUPERSEDED|INVALIDATED, causedByQuestionId/commitId, createdAt}; the active answer is the latest ACTIVE revision; cascade_invalidate flips dependents' active revision to INVALIDATED with causality. (Either revision rows in the Answer table with an active flag, or Answer + AnswerRevision pair.)
  _Tradeoffs:_ Complete declaration history: every value ever asserted, when, by what, and what invalidated it — the consequence payload returned to the agent is literally a query over revisions, so cascades are auditable, replayable, and testable against recorded sessions. Supports the catalog's pre-fill flows (get_last_application_info) with provenance. Cost: reads need an 'active' filter (a partial unique index on (questionId, conversationId) WHERE active keeps the current uniqueness guarantee); all five writer paths must go through one engine API or history integrity is fiction.

**Rationale:** This is an underwriting questionnaire: answers are regulated declarations, and the consequence engine's whole value proposition is that every commit's effects are deterministic AND verifiable. Hard-delete makes the engine's own consequence reports unfalsifiable after the fact; mark-stale keeps only the last corpse. Append-only revisions make the cascade itself data — 'cascade_invalidate cleared BD_CANCER_HISTORY because BD_ADDON_INTEREST changed to false at commit N' is a row, not a log line — which is what testing-bdd needs to assert the Gherkin consequence table and what compliance needs for IDD. It also subsumes the flagsForReview staleness problem: flags become derivable from active revisions instead of an append-only Json blob that survives corrections. On status: status must be DERIVED, not a ratchet — answered(visible required set) ⊂ active revisions determines completeness; a cascade that clears answers on a not-yet-quoted application reverts COMPLETED→OPEN deterministically (and the consequence payload says so). The one-way ratchet is quote issuance, not questionnaire completion: once a quote exists, modify_answer is not exposed at all (catalog: 'application incomplete only'; post-quote change = cancel + new application). This requires application-lifecycle to fix cancel_application's status=COMPLETED conflation and ideally introduce a READY_FOR_QUOTE distinction; the cascade engine must run plan+apply+status-recompute in ONE transaction with the triggering write.

**Depends on / interacts with:** application-lifecycle, quote-lifecycle, commit-envelope, testing-bdd, identity

#### T6.D3 — Which field classes trigger requires_confirmation on modification, and where does the sensitivity flag live?

- **validation-rules-json**: Add {sensitive: true} (or confirmationPolicy) inside the existing Question.validationRules Json, alongside flagAnswers/riskWeight.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Consistent with where flagAnswers already lives and needs no migration. But validationRules is already an untyped grab-bag (riskWeight, flags, placeholder, inputType, pattern all coexist); the engine's legality decisions would hinge on an unvalidated Json key — unqueryable ('list all sensitive questions' becomes a scan+parse), typo-silent, and invisible to schema-level review. Configuration that gates commits deserves the same rigor as the commit itself.
- **✅ Recommended — typed-sensitivity-column**: New typed column Question.sensitivity (enum NONE|CONFIRM_ON_MODIFY|CONFIRM_ALWAYS) read by the engine. Seed it for: HEALTH_DECLARATION_CONFIRM, all six BD_* medical questions, DNT_CNP (the CNP encodes sex and full date of birth, so it IS the age/identity field), and future DOB/smoker fields.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Sensitivity becomes part of the schema contract: queryable, type-checked, migration-reviewed, and uniform across products; the engine's exposure logic (does this commit need a confirm leg?) reads a typed field, which keeps the legality surface deterministic and introspectable for GUI clients (render a confirm dialog) exactly as for the agent. Cost: one migration and a second place to look beside validationRules — mitigated by treating validationRules as VALUE validation only and the column as COMMIT policy.
- **code-level-field-class-registry**: A registry in code mapping question codes/insightKeys to classes (medical, identity, financial) with per-class confirmation policy.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Centralizes policy by class rather than per-question and avoids touching seed data. But splits question metadata across code and DB (the question catalog no longer self-describes), couples policy to string codes that products can change, and per-product question sets would need per-product registries — the rules-as-code drift again.

**Rationale:** requires_confirmation is a LEGALITY behavior — it changes whether a commit applies — so its configuration belongs in the typed schema the engine treats as the source of truth, not in a presentation-flavored Json blob or in code. The classification follows from data already in the repo: HEALTH_DECLARATION_CONFIRM carries an escalate flag (a wrong modification can un-pause or pause an application), BD_* answers individually determine addon eligibility (riskWeight 10, any-yes-rejects per bd-handlers), and DNT_CNP is the identity/age root (and under the CustomerProfile SSOT direction, the DOB derived from it feeds pricing and eligibility). Equally important is the MECHANISM: confirmation must be stateless and two-phase — modify_answer on a sensitive field returns requires_confirmation carrying a dry-run consequence preview (computed by the same cascade planner: 'changing this clears these 3 answers and re-opens the application') plus a confirmation token; nothing is written until modify_answer is re-invoked with confirm=true+token. No pending rows in the DB, idempotent on double-submit, and the preview the user confirms is exactly the plan that will be applied. CONFIRM_ALWAYS (vs ON_MODIFY) covers fields where even first-write needs explicit affirmation — the bd_medical CONTEXT-HIT explicit-affirmation rule in lib/chat/context-loaders.ts:596-603 is prompt-enforced today and would become engine-enforced.

**Depends on / interacts with:** commit-envelope, legality-engine, identity, tool-mapping

#### T6.D4 — What should get_next_question return as branching_metadata so the agent can explain WHY a question appeared?

- **minimal-parent-ref**: Return {parentQuestionCode, matchedValue} when the current question has a visibility gate; nothing else.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Trivially derivable from the dependency graph and enough for the basic Gherkin line. But it cannot distinguish 'always existed' from 'just appeared because of your last answer' (the agent's most useful framing), gives no text for the gating question (agent must re-fetch or guess), and collapses with multi-parent edges or eligibility-driven additions.
- **✅ Recommended — structured-provenance**: Return branching_metadata: {triggeredBy: [{questionCode, questionText: {en,ro}, answerValue, kind: VISIBILITY|ELIGIBILITY, predicate}], addedByLastCommit: boolean, groupCode, groupName}. Plus the standard answered_count/total_count over the engine's canonical visible set. The cascade_expand consequence on the preceding write carries the matching questions_added list, so the two surfaces cross-reference.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pure data, fully deterministic, swap-testable: the agent phrases 'this follows from your earlier answer X' in conversation while a GUI renders a breadcrumb from the same payload; the Gherkin scenario ('A branching question explains why it appears') asserts on structure, not prose. Localized question texts ride along so the agent never re-queries to explain. Slightly larger payload and requires the engine to track which questions became visible in the last commit (cheap: diff of visible sets, already computed by the cascade planner).
- **engine-generated-narrative**: Engine returns a ready-made explanation string ('This question appears because you answered yes to the addon').
  _Tradeoffs:_ Zero agent work, but pushes localization, tone, and phrasing into the engine — the one component that must stay free of conversational concerns; breaks the agent/GUI symmetry (a GUI wants structure, not prose); and couples spec tests to wording.

**Rationale:** The architecture contract says the agent renders injected state and owns no business rule — the symmetric statement is that the engine owns no PHRASING. Structured provenance is the only option that satisfies both: the engine emits facts (which edge fired, on which answer, just now or earlier) and each client renders them natively. The addedByLastCommit flag is what makes the flagship UX moment work ('because you just said yes to Treatment Abroad, I need to ask 6 medical questions') and it falls out of the cascade planner for free, since cascade_expand already computed the visible-set diff. Including the gating question's localized text is a correctness measure, not a convenience: it stops the agent from paraphrasing a regulated question from memory. This decision also forces the prerequisite fix that deriveState and get_next_question must share ONE visible-set computation — branching_metadata over one graph while deriveState.missing reports another (today's unfiltered count at lib/chat/derive-state.ts:158-173) would have the agent explaining questions the state says don't exist.

**Depends on / interacts with:** tool-mapping, phase-model, commit-envelope, testing-bdd

#### T6.D5 — Should answer writes/modifications trigger a deterministic eligibility pre-check (eligibility_recheck consequence), and how does it bind to product eligibility data?

- **single-checkpoint-at-quote**: No per-answer hook; generate_quote is the only eligibility evaluation point (status quo, minus the agent-invoked check_bd_eligibility).
  _Tradeoffs:_ One authoritative evaluation, no duplicated rule surface. But it directly violates the catalog's early-signal requirement ('does not send the customer through a questionnaire that will reject them') and the eligibility_recheck consequence in the taxonomy; a customer answers 6 medical questions, then 5 application questions, and only at quote time learns the addon died at question one. Also leaves check_bd_eligibility's current silent includesAddon mutation with no principled home.
- **✅ Recommended — synchronous-edge-scoped-recheck**: ELIGIBILITY edges (from DP1) mark which answers participate in which eligibility rule (rules live in product data: Product.eligibility bounds, addon any-yes-rejects rule, age windows from PricingRule). Any write/modify touching such an answer synchronously evaluates the affected rule(s) via a pure function and returns eligibility_recheck {subject: product|addon, outcome: eligible|conditional|ineligible, reason} on the same commit. Engine applies deterministic effects (e.g. addon ineligible → includesAddon=false + questions_removed for remaining bd_medical questions) and REPORTS them in the same consequence payload; generate_quote re-evaluates everything as the final authority.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Early signal exactly where the catalog demands it; eligibility becomes engine-owned instead of agent-remembered (check_bd_eligibility is eliminated as a tool — its rule moves into product data, satisfying 'compliance/eligibility live in the engine, never the LLM'); edge-scoping makes it cheap and deterministic (only answers on eligibility edges trigger evaluation). Defense-in-depth duplication with generate_quote is intentional, but BOTH must call the same pure rule evaluator or they will drift. Auto-applying ineligibility (vs asking) is correct because eligibility is not a user choice — but the consequence must say what changed, never silently mutate (fixing bd-handlers.ts:58-65).
- **deferred-batch-recheck**: Evaluate all eligibility rules once, as a pre-flight gate when the questionnaire reaches 100% (between last answer and generate_quote exposure).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Single evaluation point earlier than the quote, fewer recomputations than per-answer. But the early-signal scenarios still fail (the BD any-yes rule is decidable at the FIRST yes — five further medical questions asked pointlessly is both UX waste and needless collection of sensitive medical data, a data-minimization concern); and it creates a third checkpoint that is neither per-commit nor the final quote authority.

**Rationale:** The taxonomy already commits to eligibility_recheck as a per-commit consequence, and the BD addon is the proof case in production data: the rule is monotone (any yes → ineligible), so the engine can and should decide at the first qualifying answer, remove the remaining bd_medical questions via the same cascade machinery (questions_removed), and report both consequences on one commit — strictly better on correctness, data minimization (don't collect five more medical declarations you no longer need), and agent reliability (no remembering to call check_bd_eligibility). Binding the trigger to ELIGIBILITY edges keeps it deterministic and auditable: 'which answers can change eligibility' is a graph query, not a code path. The rule CONTENT must live with product data (Product.eligibility bounds, addon rules — owned by the product-data topic) and be evaluated by one shared pure function so the per-answer hook and generate_quote cannot diverge. Two adjacent holes must close for this to be sound: generate_quote's silent age-30 fallback (quote-handlers.ts:63) becomes a rejected/blocked outcome (age unknown → eligibility indeterminate → requires_identity per the catalog), and the age source must be the CustomerProfile SSOT derivation (DOB/declaredAge), not a snapshot.

**Depends on / interacts with:** product-data, legality-engine, identity, quote-lifecycle, tool-mapping

#### T6.D6 — Where does cascade computation live: how do write_question_answer/modify_answer produce their consequences?

- **inline-in-handlers**: Extend the existing tool handlers (saveApplicationAnswer, setAnswer) with cascade logic where the upserts happen today.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Follows the current code shape, but the current shape is the problem: five writer paths means five places to keep cascade behavior identical, and history shows they diverge (modifyQuote forgot includesAddon; change_selection forgot level re-validation; setAnswer forgot status guards and flag re-checks). Consequences computed imperatively per-handler are untestable except through tool plumbing, and a GUI client calling a future API would bypass them entirely.
- **✅ Recommended — pure-planner-plus-transactional-applier**: One engine module: computeCascadePlan(graph, activeAnswers, proposedChange) → CascadePlan {writes, invalidations (with causes), questionsAdded, questionsRemoved, eligibilityOutcomes, statusTransition, consequences[]} as a pure function over pre-fetched data (the questionnaire-engine.ts pure-function pattern, extended); plus applyPlan(plan) executing in a single prisma transaction. modify_answer with a sensitive target runs ONLY the planner and returns the plan as the requires_confirmation preview; confirm=true re-plans and applies. ALL writers (write_question_answer, modify_answer, change_selection, application creation pre-fill) route through this one path.
  _Tradeoffs:_ The consequence payload IS the plan — preview (dry-run) and execution are the same computation, so what the user confirms is what happens. Pure planner is directly unit/property-testable (Gherkin's consequence table maps to planner assertions with zero DB) and exhaustively checkable (e.g. 'no plan ever leaves a visible required question both unanswered and counted as answered'). Single transaction kills partial-cascade states. Cost: requires disciplined refactor of every existing writer onto the path, and the planner needs the full answer/graph snapshot loaded up front (fine at 37-question scale; pageable later).
- **database-triggers**: Implement cascades as Postgres triggers/functions on Answer writes.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Impossible to bypass even by rogue code paths, and transactional by construction. But the business semantics (consequence taxonomy, confirmation previews, branching metadata) live in the application layer — triggers cannot RETURN a consequence payload to the caller, so the engine would re-derive what the trigger did; rules in SQL are the least testable and least reviewable home for regulated logic; and it splits the deterministic engine across two runtimes.

**Rationale:** This decision is what makes the other five real. The catalog's contract — every commit returns a consequence; a GUI calling the same operation gets the same transition — requires that consequence computation be a single, deterministic, client-agnostic artifact: a pure plan. The repo's own history is the argument against inline handlers — three independent partial implementations of 'what happens when a selection changes' already disagree (change_selection, modifyQuote, setAnswer), and each new writer multiplies the divergence. The planner/applier split also resolves requires_confirmation elegantly (the preview problem disappears when planning is side-effect-free), gives testing-bdd a pure target for the scenario-outline consequence table, and preserves the existing architectural seam in questionnaire-engine.ts (pure functions + thin DB wrappers) rather than fighting it. The transactional applier closes today's partial-write windows (answer upserted, then application.update fails → state skew). Legality (is modify_answer exposed at all for this application?) stays in the legality-engine; the planner assumes a legal commit and computes only its consequences — clean layering between 'may you' and 'what happens'.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, testing-bdd, application-lifecycle

### Risks

- Bypassable cascades: five Answer write paths exist today (save_application_answer, set_answer, change_selection, modify_quote, dnt-handlers) — if even one keeps writing outside the planner/applier path, cascade integrity, revision history, and consequence reporting are all fiction. The refactor must end with exactly one write path and a test that greps/asserts no direct prisma.answer writes outside the engine.
- Progress-divergence regressions: deriveState's unfiltered required/missing (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:154-173) vs the engine's visibility-filtered set will produce contradictory states the moment real branching edges are seeded (bd_medical gating). Both must consume one canonical visible-set function before any new edges land, or phase computation (QUESTIONNAIRE vs QUOTE) flips incorrectly.
- Live data-integrity bug as migration hazard: change_selection can already leave application.levelId pointing at a level row of the previous tier, and generate_quote prices from it (lib/tools/handlers/change-selection-handlers.ts:53-69, quote-handlers.ts:54-60). Existing conversations may carry inconsistent tier/level pairs that a VALIDITY-edge backfill must detect and repair, not assume away.
- Stale escalation flags: Application.flagsForReview is append-only and never recomputed on answer modification — a corrected HEALTH_DECLARATION_CONFIRM leaves the application PAUSED with a live escalate flag. If the consequence engine doesn't take ownership of flag recomputation (derive flags from active answer revisions), modify_answer's cascade_invalidate will resurrect this class of zombie state.
- DNT scope leakage: the target spec declares DNT flat (modify_dnt_answer → applied, no consequences), but the only existing dependency edge in the seed is a DNT question (DNT_SUSTAINABILITY_PREFERENCE), and the documented DNT_LIFE_SUBTYPE group-gating is unimplemented. Either the DNT spec assumption is wrong (DNT has branching and needs the same engine) or that edge must move/die — the cascade engine must be explicitly phase-scoped either way, and this conflict needs resolving with the dnt-sessions topic before edges are seeded.
- Confirmation race/idempotency: the stateless two-phase modify_answer (preview token → confirm) must bind the token to the planned state snapshot; if answers change between preview and confirm (GUI and agent acting concurrently is an explicit catalog scenario), a confirm against a stale plan must be rejected and re-planned, or the user confirms consequences that no longer match reality.
- Conversation-scoped Answer vs customer-scoped SSOT: the entire engine keys on (questionId, conversationId) while the strategic CustomerProfile SSOT direction moves customer facts to customer scope. Building the planner against a thin answer-store interface (rather than prisma.answer directly) is the hedge; otherwise the re-keying migration re-touches every cascade rule.
- Sensitive-data minimization: until bd_medical is gated and eligibility short-circuits, the system collects six medical declarations from customers who declined the addon or are already ineligible — a GDPR data-minimization exposure that grows with every conversation shipped before the edges land.
- Append-only revision growth and uniqueness: replacing the @@unique([questionId, conversationId]) upsert with revisions requires a partial-unique active-row constraint; getting this wrong silently permits two active answers for one question, which corrupts every downstream computation (visibility, progress, eligibility) at once.

---

## T7. Quote lifecycle: one-app-one-quote, immutability, IDD/IPID disclosures, accept with payment option

> Topic key: `quote-lifecycle`

### Current state (code-grounded)

DATA MODEL (prisma/schema.prisma): Quote (lines 514-536) has applicationId String @unique — one-app-one-quote is already DB-enforced as 1:1 — plus premiumAnnual/premiumMonthly/premiumSemiAnnual/premiumQuarterly, paymentFrequency String?, coverages Json, addonsSelected Json, status QuoteStatus, validUntil, and a Policy? relation. QuoteStatus (lines 27-31) = DRAFT | ACCEPTED | EXPIRED — no CANCELLED, no REJECTED/REFERRED, no issued-vs-presented distinction. ApplicationStatus (lines 21-25) = OPEN | PAUSED | COMPLETED — no CANCELLED. Product has quoteValidityDays Int @default(30) (line 125) and paymentFrequencyOptions Json? (line 123, unused in the quote path) and eligibility Json (line 111, only echoed to the agent via lib/tools/shape-product-info.ts:228, never enforced).

GENERATE_QUOTE (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:19-255): gates on verifyConsents(conversationId) (lib/compliance/consent-check.ts — checks 3 answer codes DNT_CONSULTATION_CONSENT / DNT_ELECTRONIC_COMMUNICATION / DNT_MARKETING_CONSENT plus Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil) and Application.status === 'COMPLETED' with tierId+levelId. Application flips to COMPLETED when the last questionnaire answer is saved (lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:330-333) — i.e. immutability-relevant completion happens at all-answers-complete, BEFORE generate_quote, contradicting the catalog's "issuing a quote completes the application". Customer age is computed from Customer.dateOfBirth with a SILENT FALLBACK of 30 when DOB is missing (quote-handlers.ts:63). calculateQuote (lib/engines/quote-engine.ts:77-101) is pure arithmetic (base + addon premium, frequency splits, validUntil = now + quoteValidityDays) with ZERO eligibility logic; there is no rejected(reason)/referred outcome anywhere — failures are generic success:false strings. paymentFrequency is read from a PAYMENT_FREQUENCY questionnaire answer (quote-handlers.ts:140-159; union 'annual'|'semi_annual'|'quarterly' — note 'monthly' is not a legal value even though premiumMonthly is computed and displayed). The handler does prisma.quote.create (line 189) with status DRAFT. CRITICAL LATENT BUG: nothing in lib/ ever deletes a Quote row (grep: only quote.update calls exist), so after modify_quote/change_selection EXPIRE a quote, a second generate_quote for the same application throws Prisma P2002 on the applicationId unique constraint — the advertised "regenerate" path is structurally broken; no test covers it (only mention: __tests__/lib/debug/conversation-export.test.ts:64, unrelated).

GET_QUOTE_DETAILS (quote-handlers.ts:261-310): returns premiums/status/validUntil/coverages. Does NOT lazily expire past-validUntil quotes, does NOT bundle payment_options, has no disclosures_required concept. No get_quote_info per catalog.

ACCEPT_QUOTE (quote-handlers.ts:316-443; registry lib/tools/registry.ts:871-888): requires confirmAcceptance:true (requires_confirmation analogue); schema accepts quoteId but the handler IGNORES it (resolves via conversation→application). Requires status DRAFT; lazily expires when validUntil passed (lines 344-349). On success: Quote→ACCEPTED, creates Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION) BEFORE any payment (lines 359-371) WITHOUT setting Policy.paymentFrequency, then marks the Conversation COMPLETED (lines 376-382). Because Policy.paymentFrequency stays null, initiate_payment (lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts:80-87) branches annual-vs-default-MONTHLY — a quarterly/semi-annual quote silently bills the monthly amount. No disclosure gate exists. Not idempotent: a second accept returns an error ("not in DRAFT") rather than an idempotent success. accept_quote does not re-verify consents.

MODIFY_QUOTE (quote-handlers.ts:449-530; registry 906-918): expires the quote, resets the Application (tierId/levelId null, status OPEN, completedAt null), deletes PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST/PAYMENT_FREQUENCY answers — directly contradicts one-app-one-quote immutability, and its end state is unreachable anyway due to the P2002 collision above. CHANGE_SELECTION (lib/tools/handlers/change-selection-handlers.ts): mutates tier/level/addon with NO application-status check and NO ACCEPTED-quote check (it expires only DRAFT quotes, lines 86-89) — it can mutate an application whose quote was already ACCEPTED with a Policy created, diverging the frozen artifacts; it is ALWAYS exposed via DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS (lib/chat/default-tools.ts:17). switch_product (lib/tools/handlers/product-switch-handler.ts:74-83) also expires DRAFT quotes. The frontend has accept_quote/modify_quote buttons wired through lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:66-78, and seed workflow step 'present_quote' grants ['get_quote_details','accept_quote','modify_quote'] (prisma/seeds/seed-workflows.ts:401).

DISCLOSURES: No IDD/IPID acknowledgment storage exists anywhere. Precedents: Customer.gdprConsentAt/gdprConsentScope/aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt (migration prisma/migrations/20260520000000_add-customer-consent-tracking) with acknowledge_ai_disclosure stamping Customer (lib/tools/registry.ts:1067-1122); lib/compliance/dnt-report.ts generates an IDD suitability report PDF post-policy and stores Policy.suitabilityReportPath (lines 453-458). No Document/ProductDocument model, no IPID file storage or serving route, no acknowledge_disclosures tool, no requires_disclosures gate.

EXPIRY: only the lazy check inside accept_quote. deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:176-196) treats a time-expired DRAFT as a live quote; no cron/job infrastructure exists. PHASE MODEL: deriveState maps application COMPLETED→'QUOTE' phase and ACCEPTED quote→'CLOSING' (derive-state.ts:41-48); nextBestAction QUOTE='call generate_quote', CLOSING='present the quote and proceed to accept_quote' (lines 61-64); phase sections in lib/chat/phase-sections-map.ts. Side note feeding risks: cancel_application sets status COMPLETED (application-handlers.ts:511-514, no CANCELLED status exists), so a cancelled application derives as QUOTE phase with nextBestAction generate_quote.

REJECTED/REFERRED PRECEDENTS: Application.flagsForReview Json accumulates escalate/flag outcomes from answer validation (application-handlers.ts:184-251; escalate sets status PAUSED); check_bd_eligibility (lib/tools/handlers/bd-handlers.ts) is the one deterministic eligibility check (any 'true' medical answer strips the addon); escalate_to_human (lib/tools/handlers/utility-handlers.ts:14-46) only sets Conversation IDLE and console.logs — no operator queue record.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** seed workflow step 'present_quote' grants ['get_quote_details','accept_quote','modify_quote'] (prisma/seeds/seed-workflows.ts:401) — repeated in risks as "seed workflow step 'present_quote' grants modify_quote"
  **Correction:** The step code is 'quote_review' (name: 'Review Quote'), not 'present_quote'. No step named 'present_quote' exists in the seed file (grep for 'present_quote' returns nothing). The cited line number and the allowedTools array are otherwise correct: line 401 is exactly allowedTools: ['get_quote_details', 'accept_quote', 'modify_quote'], belonging to the quote_review step. _(prisma/seeds/seed-workflows.ts:396 (code: 'quote_review'), :397 (name: 'Review Quote'), :401 (allowedTools: ['get_quote_details', 'accept_quote', 'modify_quote']); grep 'present_quote' across the file matches only the transition target 'quote_review' context — zero 'present_quote' hits)_
- **Claim:** no test covers it (only mention: __tests__/lib/debug/conversation-export.test.ts:64, unrelated)
  **Correction:** The parenthetical is inaccurate in both possible readings. If 'only mention' refers to modify_quote: modify_quote appears in ZERO files under __tests__ (conversation-export.test.ts:64 mentions 'generate_quote' and 'change_selection', not modify_quote). If it refers to generate_quote: the string appears in SIX test files, not one (main-chat-constraints.test.ts:72-75, advance-flow-tools.test.ts:18, navigation.test.ts:81, state-rows.test.ts:70, derive-state.test.ts:177, conversation-export.test.ts:49 and :64). The substantive claim is nonetheless TRUE and verified: none of those tests exercise the generateQuote handler or the expire-then-regenerate path (they only reference the tool name in prompt assertions, derived-state fixtures, and export summaries), so the P2002 regeneration break is indeed untested. _(__tests__/lib/debug/conversation-export.test.ts:64 (expect(out.summary.toolsUsed).toEqual(['change_selection', 'generate_quote', 'set_candidate_product'])); grep 'modify_quote|modifyQuote' in __tests__/ → no matches; grep 'generate_quote|generateQuote' in __tests__/ → 6 files)_

### Gaps

- No get_quote_info: get_quote_details (quote-handlers.ts:261-310) returns premiums/status/coverages but bundles neither payment_options nor disclosures_required.
- No disclosure machinery at all: no acknowledge_disclosures tool, no acknowledgment storage (DisclosureAck or otherwise), no IPID/IDD document model or serving path, no requires_disclosures block on accept_quote. The only IDD artifact (lib/compliance/dnt-report.ts suitability PDF) is generated post-policy, after the moment the catalog requires disclosure.
- No cancel_quote tool and no CANCELLED value in QuoteStatus; the only terminal-ish path is modify_quote's EXPIRED-plus-reopen, which the catalog eliminates.
- generate_quote has no rejected(reason)/referred(manual underwriting) outcomes: quote-engine.ts has zero eligibility logic, Product.eligibility Json is never enforced, missing DOB silently defaults age to 30 (quote-handlers.ts:63), and an unmatched addon age rule silently prices the addon at 0 instead of rejecting/referring.
- Quote regeneration is structurally broken: Quote.applicationId is @unique (schema.prisma:516), only prisma.quote.create exists (quote-handlers.ts:189), and no code path deletes a Quote — any expire-then-regenerate flow (modify_quote, change_selection, switch_product) hits P2002 on the next generate_quote. No test covers this.
- accept_quote ignores its quoteId argument, has no payment_option parameter, and never writes Policy.paymentFrequency — initiate_payment (payment-handlers.ts:80-87) then defaults to monthly billing even for quarterly/semi-annual quotes.
- accept_quote is not idempotent per the catalog: a double-submit returns an error instead of replaying the success consequence; there is no CAS-style guard (contrast lib/payments/post-payment.ts:28-31 which does it correctly for payments).
- Quote expiry is enforced only inside accept_quote; deriveState (derive-state.ts:176-196), get_quote_details and any future available_actions computation treat a time-expired DRAFT as live.
- Application immutability is undefined: status flips COMPLETED at last answer (application-handlers.ts:330-333), but change_selection mutates tier/level/addon at any status with no ACCEPTED-quote check and is always exposed (default-tools.ts:17).
- The expired/cancelled-quote -> new-application-prefilled flow does not exist (no get_last_application_info; the catalog's post-quote change path has no implementation).

### Decision points

#### T7.D1 — How do we resolve modify_quote / post-quote change_selection against one-app-one-quote, and exactly when does the application become immutable?

- **✅ Recommended — Catalog-literal: immutable at generate_quote success; eliminate modify_quote and post-quote change_selection; post-quote change = cancel_quote + new application pre-filled**: Keep Quote.applicationId @unique as the structural invariant. generate_quote success atomically freezes the application (a frozen marker set in the same transaction as quote creation). modify_quote is deleted; change_selection becomes illegal once the application is frozen (engine-gated, not just prompt-gated) and also while a quote exists in any state. Any change after a quote exists = cancel_quote (terminal) then a new application pre-filled from the old via get_last_application_info, with every answer re-confirmed. Answers and selection remain mutable (with cascade consequences) right up to the generate_quote commit, including the window after the last answer — completion-at-last-answer stops being the lock point.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Strongest audit/compliance property: every priced offer maps 1:1 to an immutable answer set, which is exactly the evidence IDD suitability disputes need. Idempotency and legality checks become trivial (quote exists => application frozen). Passes the swap test cleanly: a GUI edit button maps to cancel+re-apply. Cost: a customer wanting a tier tweak after seeing the price goes through a re-confirmation loop — correct but more ceremonial; the pre-fill flow must exist or UX collapses into full re-entry.
- **Bounded regenerate-while-DRAFT: application stays mutable until accept_quote; DRAFT quotes are superseded**: Interpret one-app-one-quote as one ACTIVE quote: change_selection/modify_answer remain legal until acceptance, each change expires the DRAFT and the next generate_quote supersedes it (requires dropping @unique to 1:N with a latest-active discipline). Immutability begins at ACCEPTED.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches what change_selection already tries to do and gives a fluid price-shopping UX. But it directly contradicts the catalog and the Gherkin regression guard ('One application yields one quote'), weakens the audit chain (which answer set produced the offer the customer saw?), reintroduces cascade logic at the priced-artifact stage, and the 1:N latest-active discipline is a standing source of divergence bugs (deriveState, get_open_items, policy joins all must agree on 'latest').
- **Immutable at all-answers-complete (formalize current code): lock at Application COMPLETED, generate_quote is a pure read-and-issue**: Keep the existing COMPLETED-at-last-answer flip as the freeze point; block modify_answer/change_selection from that moment; generate_quote merely prices the frozen set.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simplest invariant to state, but it creates a dead zone with no compliance rationale: between the last answer and generate_quote no priced artifact exists, yet a customer who spots a typo in their final answer is forced into cancel+re-apply. It also conflates 'questionnaire finished' with 'offer issued', which breaks the rejected/referred design (a rejected application would be immutable for no reason).

**Rationale:** A quote is a binding offer derived from a declared fact set; the integrity property that matters is that the fact set cannot drift after pricing. Freezing at generate_quote success (not at last-answer) puts the lock exactly where the legal artifact is created, keeps pre-quote corrections cheap and cascade-governed, and makes the legality engine's rules decidable from one bit of state. The DB already enforces the 1:1; the design should embrace it rather than fight it (today's expire-and-reuse approach is provably broken via P2002). The Gherkin spec pins this interpretation twice ('A successful quote completes the application', 'One application yields one quote').

**Depends on / interacts with:** application-lifecycle, questionnaire-consequences, legality-engine, tool-mapping, testing-bdd

#### T7.D2 — Where and how are IDD/IPID disclosure acknowledgments stored, how are the documents served, and how does the requires_disclosures gate work?

- **✅ Recommended — New DisclosureAck model bound to the quote + versioned ProductDocument registry; acknowledge_disclosures(quote_id) commit; engine gate on accept_quote**: ProductDocument(productId, type: IPID|IDD_INFO|TERMS, version, locale, storageRef, effectiveFrom) is the registry of servable documents (served via an authenticated route, same storage style as the dnt-report PDF). DisclosureAck(quoteId, customerId, documentType, documentVersion, locale, acknowledgedAt, channel) records one row per acknowledged document. get_quote_info computes disclosures_required = current ProductDocument versions minus existing acks for this quote. acknowledge_disclosures(quote_id) writes the missing rows. accept_quote's exposure/legality check: all required docs acked for THIS quote at CURRENT versions, else blocked with requires_disclosures.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Compliance evidence is exactly what regulators ask for: which document version was presented for which offer, to which identified customer, when. Quote-scoped acks correctly force re-acknowledgment on a new quote (a new offer is a new pre-contractual disclosure duty). Version binding makes 'document updated between view and accept' detectable deterministically. Costs: two new models and a serving route; the engine must treat ProductDocument as part of product data SSOT.
- **Timestamp fields on Quote (disclosuresAcknowledgedAt + Json detail)**: Add Quote.disclosuresAcknowledgedAt and a Json blob listing what was acked; gate accept_quote on the timestamp.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Keeps everything on the existing aggregate, and the gate is a null-check. But Json acks are unqueryable for audits, carry no enforced version linkage (false evidence risk if the IPID changes), cannot represent partial acknowledgment of multiple documents, and die with the quote row instead of forming a compliance ledger.
- **Customer-level fields per document type (extend the gdprConsentAt / aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt pattern)**: Add Customer.ipidAcknowledgedAt etc., mirroring migration 20260520000000.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Consistent with the existing consent pattern and naturally customer-scoped (aligned with the CustomerProfile SSOT direction). But it is the WRONG scope for IDD: an IPID is product- and version-specific and the acknowledgment is per offer; a customer-level stamp from a January quote would incorrectly satisfy the gate for a different June quote on a revised document. AI-disclosure/GDPR are relationship-level; IPID/IDD are transaction-level — they must not share a model.

**Rationale:** The acknowledgment's evidentiary value lives entirely in the binding (this customer, this offer, this document version, this instant). Only a first-class quote-scoped row with a versioned document reference provides that; both alternatives destroy at least one leg of the binding. It also makes the requires_disclosures consequence purely computable (set difference), which is what the legality engine needs to expose/block accept_quote deterministically, and the same ProductDocument registry later serves get_policy_documents in @policy.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, product-data, identity, policy-post-sale, testing-bdd

#### T7.D3 — What is payment_option in accept_quote(quote_id, payment_option), where does it come from, and where is the chosen value stored?

- **✅ Recommended — payment_option = payment frequency chosen at accept; sourced from Product.paymentFrequencyOptions intersected with the quote's premium variants; persisted on the acceptance (Quote.paymentFrequency + acceptedAt), removed from the questionnaire**: get_quote_info returns payment_options as [{option:'annual'|'semi_annual'|'quarterly'|'monthly', amount, currency}] derived from Product.paymentFrequencyOptions (schema line 123, currently unused) and the quote's stored premium variants. accept_quote(quote_id, payment_option) validates membership and persists the choice as part of the acceptance record (Quote.paymentFrequency becomes 'chosen at accept', null until accepted, alongside acceptedAt). PAYMENT_FREQUENCY leaves the underwriting questionnaire (it is not an underwriting fact). change_payment_option in @payment re-rates and rewrites the same single field pre-capture.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Single source of truth for the billing term, chosen at the moment it becomes contractually meaningful; kills today's three-way divergence (questionnaire answer vs Quote.paymentFrequency vs Policy.paymentFrequency-null-defaults-to-monthly) by construction; change_payment_option has exactly one cell to mutate. Requires deciding the legal frequency set explicitly (today 'monthly' is computed and billed but not a legal quote-engine value — that contradiction must be resolved, not inherited).
- **Keep PAYMENT_FREQUENCY as a questionnaire answer; accept_quote reads it (formalize current flow)**: Frequency stays an Answer row captured during the questionnaire; accept_quote copies it forward to the policy/payment layer.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No tool-signature change and the quote can display the 'chosen' frequency early. But it couples a payment-contract term into the frozen underwriting fact set: under DP1 immutability, change_payment_option would have to mutate an answer on an immutable application — a direct contradiction; and the duplicate stores (Answer + Quote + Policy) are exactly the divergence class the SSOT direction is eliminating.
- **payment_option as a richer object (frequency + method/mandate)**: Accept {frequency, method: card|transfer|mandate} so the payment module gets a complete instruction.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Future-proof for multi-rail payments, but method selection is Stripe's domain in the stated architecture ('Stripe owns card entry'); modeling it in the quote phase couples Zeno to payment-provider concerns and widens the accept commit beyond what any current flow consumes. Frequency is the only term that re-rates the schedule, which is the engine's actual concern.

**Rationale:** Frequency is a term of the payment contract, not a risk fact, so it must not live inside the frozen application (DP1) and must not be guessable downstream (today's bug: Policy.paymentFrequency is never written at accept, so initiate_payment bills monthly regardless of the quote — verified at quote-handlers.ts:359-371 vs payment-handlers.ts:80-87). Binding the choice to the acceptance record gives the payment phase one authoritative input and gives change_payment_option a single, auditable mutation point. Whether the persisted home is Quote fields or a dedicated acceptance/order entity should follow the payments-topic decision on when Policy is created; the invariant to fix here is 'chosen at accept, stored once'.

**Depends on / interacts with:** payments, commit-envelope, application-lifecycle, product-data, policy-post-sale

#### T7.D4 — What deterministic rejected(reason)/referred outcomes should generate_quote return in v1, and what does 'referred' do operationally?

- **✅ Recommended — Typed decision inside the generate_quote commit: {issued | rejected(reason) | referred(reason)}, with v1 reasons ineligible_age, missing_identity_data, compliance_block, manual_underwriting; referred = Application REFERRED + operator work item; decision persisted on the Application**: An eligibility module runs inside generate_quote before pricing: (1) age vs Product.eligibility bounds and the pricing/addon age windows — currently silently degraded (fallback age 30 at quote-handlers.ts:63; unmatched addon rule prices to 0) becomes rejected(ineligible_age) or rejected(missing_identity_data) when DOB is absent; (2) consent/DNT validity (today a generic error from verifyConsents) becomes rejected(compliance_block); (3) accumulated flagsForReview escalate-class flags (application-handlers.ts:184-251) become referred(manual_underwriting). rejected/referred create NO Quote row; the decision {outcome, reason, decidedAt} is persisted on the Application for audit; referred additionally sets an Application REFERRED state and creates a real operator work item (replacing escalate_to_human's console.log).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Puts compliance/eligibility exactly where the spec demands ('Compliance/eligibility live here, never in the LLM') and makes every outcome replayable from persisted state. Reason taxonomy is extensible without schema churn (reason is data). Requires the application-lifecycle topic to add a REFERRED-capable state and an operator surface; until that exists referred degrades to PAUSED + escalation, which is acceptable but weaker.
- **Pre-gate eligibility in exposure: the engine blocks generate_quote (blocked_actions with reason) until eligibility passes**: Eligibility evaluated as part of available_actions computation; generate_quote is only exposed when the customer would pass, so the commit itself can only issue.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Aligns with the early-eligibility-signal philosophy and avoids walking a doomed customer to the final step. But final underwriting needs the complete answer set and identity, which is only certainly present at the commit; encoding it as exposure makes blocked_actions carry underwriting verdicts (a category error — blocks are about legality, not adjudication), and 'referred' has no natural expression as a block. Early signals belong in discovery (eligibility_bounds); the verdict belongs in the commit.
- **Status-quo plus: keep generic errors, add reasons to the error strings**: Keep success:false string returns but standardize the wording so the agent can relay reasons.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No schema or engine change, but reasons-as-prose are not machine-checkable, cannot drive the consequence taxonomy (rejected vs referred are different downstream flows), leave no audit record of the underwriting decision, and keep the silent age-30/addon-0 holes that actively misprice today.

**Rationale:** The catalog defines generate_quote as THE deterministic underwriting decision point, and the current code's failure mode is not missing checks but silent mis-decisions (guessed age, zero-priced addon) — only a typed, persisted decision fixes both the determinism and the auditability. Keeping rejected/referred off the Quote table preserves the invariant 'a Quote row exists iff an offer was issued', which DP1 and DP5 both lean on. Exposure-gating stays for what it is good at (identity present, questionnaire complete, consents valid as requires_consent blocks) while adjudication lives in the commit.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, identity, application-lifecycle, product-data, phase-model

#### T7.D5 — Who expires quotes (lazy vs job), and what is the expired-quote flow?

- **✅ Recommended — Lazy, engine-computed expiry: one isExpired predicate (validUntil < now) used by every read and legality check; persisted EXPIRED status written opportunistically on commit attempts; expired => offer new pre-filled application**: Truth is validUntil; a single shared predicate feeds deriveState/available_actions, get_quote_info (which returns an expired status even if the row still says DRAFT/ISSUED), and accept_quote/cancel_quote legality. Commits against an expired quote persist EXPIRED and return rejected(quote_expired). Since the application is immutable (DP1), the recovery path is never regenerate-on-same-application: Zeno offers a new application pre-filled via get_last_application_info.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Deterministic at the moment of every decision — no staleness window, no race between a sweeper and an in-flight accept, no clock-skew double-source. The status column becomes a materialization of derived truth, so every consumer MUST go through the predicate (a direct quote.status read is a latent bug; deriveState already makes this mistake today). Re-engagement messaging ('your quote expired yesterday') has no push trigger.
- **Background sweep job: periodic transition of past-validUntil quotes to EXPIRED, optionally firing re-engagement**: A scheduled job updates statuses and can enqueue notifications; reads trust the status column.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Status column is consistent for ad-hoc queries (get_open_items, operator dashboards) and enables proactive re-engagement. But between runs the column lies, so every legality check still needs the lazy predicate — the job can only ever be additive, never the source of truth for legality; treating it as such reintroduces the time-of-check/time-of-use race the catalog's idempotency rules exist to prevent. There is also no job infrastructure in the codebase today (verified: none found).
- **Database-enforced expiry (generated column / view computing effective status)**: Push the validUntil comparison into the database so every query sees the effective status.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Eliminates the must-use-the-predicate discipline problem at the data layer, but couples lifecycle semantics to DB engine features, splits the legality logic across two languages (TS engine + SQL), and makes the consequence taxonomy (rejected(quote_expired) with persisted transition) harder to express as a single engine concern.

**Rationale:** The architecture's load-bearing promise is that available_actions/blocked_actions are computed fresh every turn — expiry is just one more input to that computation, and a sweeper cannot be trusted for legality anyway (the lazy check is mandatory regardless, as accept_quote already demonstrates at quote-handlers.ts:344-349).
