Centralizing the predicate fixes the verified inconsistency where deriveState counts a time-expired quote as live while accept_quote rejects it. A re-engagement job can be layered on later for notification purposes without ever owning state transitions.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, phase-model, application-lifecycle, testing-bdd

#### T7.D6 — What exactly does the accept_quote commit do (idempotency, Policy creation timing, conversation closure), and what is the quote status model?

- **✅ Recommended — Narrow accept: CAS transition ISSUED->ACCEPTED (idempotent replay on repeat), persist payment_option + acceptedAt, return advance_phase->@payment; NO Policy creation, NO Conversation COMPLETED; QuoteStatus extended to ISSUED/ACCEPTED/EXPIRED/CANCELLED**: Rename DRAFT to ISSUED (under one-app-one-quote there is no draft state — generation IS issuance) and add CANCELLED for the new cancel_quote terminal commit (requires_confirmation, then CAS ISSUED->CANCELLED). accept_quote does a compare-and-swap updateMany where status=ISSUED (the proven pattern at lib/payments/post-payment.ts:28-31); a repeat call against an already-ACCEPTED quote with the same payment_option returns the SAME success consequence (idempotent replay) instead of an error. Policy creation moves out of accept entirely — per catalog, issue_policy is a system effect of the payment module on first successful payment — and the conversation stays open through @payment.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches the catalog's phase machine exactly and fixes three verified defects at once: premature Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION)+issuedAt before any money moves, Conversation COMPLETED before payment (which strands resume/retry flows on a 'completed' conversation), and error-on-double-submit. Idempotent replay needs the persisted payment_option to disambiguate a repeat from a conflicting accept (different option => rejected). Downstream, initiate_payment must learn to hang payments off the accepted Quote instead of a Policy — a payments-topic dependency that must land together.
- **Keep Policy-at-accept (current code) but set paymentFrequency and add idempotency**: Retain Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION) creation inside accept_quote, fix the missing paymentFrequency propagation, make the double-submit path return idempotent success.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Smallest semantic delta from current behavior and Payment keeps its existing Policy FK. But it bakes in a policy record (with issuedAt!) for a contract that may never be paid — a data-integrity falsehood that policy-post-sale then has to special-case (PENDING_SUBMISSION as 'not really a policy'), and it contradicts the catalog's explicit 'issue_policy is fired by the payment module'. The phase model also stays distorted: deriveState's CLOSING conflates accepted-awaiting-payment with done.
- **Introduce a dedicated Acceptance/Order entity between Quote and Policy**: accept_quote creates an Order(quoteId, paymentOption, acceptedAt, status) that the payment module consumes; Policy references the Order.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Cleanest separation of offer/acceptance/contract and a natural anchor for payment schedules and change_payment_option; scales to multi-installment payment plans. But it adds an aggregate whose v1 content is two fields already expressible on Quote, and every consumer (payments, policy, open-items) gains a join; justified the moment payment schedules become first-class, premature while Payment is single-transaction.

**Rationale:** Acceptance is consent to an offer, not contract issuance — the current code's Policy-with-issuedAt-before-payment is the single largest semantic falsehood in the funnel and it propagates (initiate_payment trusts a Policy that represents no paid contract; suitability reporting hangs off it). The CAS pattern is already proven in this codebase for exactly this idempotency class. Status renames make the state machine honest: ISSUED (offer stands), ACCEPTED (consented, paying), EXPIRED (time), CANCELLED (customer terminal) — each with exactly one entering commit, which is what makes the BDD scenarios mechanically checkable. The Acceptance-entity option is the right evolution if/when payments become schedule-based; that trigger belongs to the payments topic.

**Depends on / interacts with:** payments, policy-post-sale, commit-envelope, phase-model, legality-engine, tool-mapping

### Risks

- Latent production break verified in code: any expire-then-regenerate flow (modify_quote quote-handlers.ts:467, change_selection change-selection-handlers.ts:89, switch_product product-switch-handler.ts:79) leaves the EXPIRED Quote row holding the unique applicationId, so the next generate_quote throws P2002 and the funnel dead-ends with a raw Prisma error surfaced to the agent. No test exercises this path.
- Verified billing mismatch shipping today: accept_quote never writes Policy.paymentFrequency (quote-handlers.ts:359-371), so initiate_payment's annual-else-monthly branch (payment-handlers.ts:80-87) bills the monthly amount for quarterly/semi-annual quotes; additionally 'monthly' is not even a legal value in the quote-engine frequency union while premiumMonthly is displayed everywhere — the legal frequency set must be decided explicitly during DP3.
- Compliance exposure: verifyConsents (lib/compliance/consent-check.ts:10-14) hard-requires DNT_MARKETING_CONSENT to generate a quote — conditioning service on marketing consent violates GDPR freely-given consent; this gate will be inherited by the new compliance_block reason unless deliberately split.
- Premature contract artifacts: Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION, issuedAt=now) is created and the Conversation is marked COMPLETED at acceptance, before any payment — the @payment re-engagement flows the catalog mandates (resume/retry days later) would operate on a conversation the system considers finished; any analytics or operator view counting Policies overcounts unsold contracts.
- Silent underwriting holes until DP4 lands: missing DOB prices a quote at age 30 (quote-handlers.ts:63) and an unmatched addon age rule includes the addon at premium 0 — both produce legally presented offers from invented facts; these must be treated as rejected/referred from day one of the new generate_quote, not deferred.
- change_selection is in the always-exposed DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS (default-tools.ts:17) and checks neither application status nor ACCEPTED-quote existence — until the legality engine gates it, it can mutate an application whose quote is already ACCEPTED with a Policy created, diverging the frozen snapshot from the sold artifact.
- Phase-model integrity: cancel_application sets ApplicationStatus COMPLETED (application-handlers.ts:511-514; no CANCELLED value exists), so deriveState classifies a cancelled application as QUOTE phase with nextBestAction 'call generate_quote' — the one-app-one-quote redesign must not inherit COMPLETED as an overloaded terminal; coordinate with application-lifecycle on a CANCELLED/REFERRED-capable status enum.
- Frontend coupling: the UI action adapter maps accept_quote/modify_quote buttons (lib/chat/action-adapter.ts:66-78) and seed workflow step 'present_quote' grants modify_quote (prisma/seeds/seed-workflows.ts:401) — eliminating modify_quote without migrating these surfaces leaves dead buttons that fail the swap test (GUI and agent must call the same operations).
- Disclosure-evidence trap: if acknowledge_disclosures ships before the versioned ProductDocument registry, acks will be recorded against unversioned documents, producing compliance 'evidence' that cannot prove what the customer actually saw — the version linkage is the point, not the timestamp.
- deriveState treats a time-expired DRAFT quote as live (derive-state.ts:176-196) while accept_quote rejects it — until the shared isExpired predicate exists, the injected situational briefing can instruct the agent toward an accept that the commit will refuse, recreating the narrated-progress pathology the transformation is meant to eliminate.

---

## T8. Payment flows & entities: schedule model, status/resume/retry/change-option, policy auto-issuance

> Topic key: `payments`

### Current state (code-grounded)

TOOLS — Only `initiate_payment` exists (registered lib/tools/registry.ts:940-952, zero-arg schema lib/tools/validation.ts:194, handler lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts; granted via SkillPack allowedTools, prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts:166). Verified by repo-wide grep: `get_payment_status`, `resume_payment`, `retry_payment`, `change_payment_option`, `get_open_items`, and `get_customer_info` do NOT exist anywhere in lib/ — only in the target docs.

initiate_payment (lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts): resolves Policy via context.policy or DB chain conversation→application→quote→policy (lines 29-65); hard-gates on Policy.status === 'PENDING_SUBMISSION' (line 68); amount = premiumAnnual*100 if paymentFrequency==='annual' else premiumMonthly*100 (lines 80-87); creates a provider PaymentIntent and a NEW Payment row (status PENDING) on EVERY call — no reuse of an existing open attempt (lines 92-115); returns uiAction `show_payment` with clientSecret/redirectUrl so card entry happens in the UI (Stripe Elements / PayU hosted redirect) — the agent never touches card data. LOAD-BEARING BUG: Policy.paymentFrequency is never written anywhere — accept_quote (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:359-371) does not copy quote.paymentFrequency into the Policy — so the annual branch is dead code and every customer is charged exactly one month's premium regardless of quoted frequency.

PROVIDERS (lib/payments/): types.ts defines PaymentProvider {createPaymentIntent, getPaymentStatus, handleWebhook}; WebhookEvent carries only event ('payment_succeeded'|'payment_failed') + providerPaymentId — NO provider event id, so event-level dedup is impossible at the interface. index.ts: env-selected singleton (stripe/payu/mock). providers/stripe.ts: PaymentIntents + signature-verified webhooks; unknown event types are returned AS payment_succeeded with metadata.originalEventType (lines 118-126) and filtered in the route. providers/payu.ts: redirect-based order flow; handleWebhook SKIPS signature validation entirely when the header lacks a `signature=` part (line 186 `if (expectedHash)`), and uses HMAC-MD5. providers/mock.ts: always succeeds.

WEBHOOKS — app/api/webhooks/stripe/route.ts and app/api/webhooks/payu/route.ts both: verify signature via provider; look up Payment by findFirst on providerPaymentId (schema.prisma:581 — @@index only, NOT @unique, nullable); on succeeded → runPostPaymentFlow(payment.id); on failed → Payment.status=FAILED + failureReason; return 200 even on internal processing errors (stripe route lines 103-111, payu lines 87-94) so a crashed handler permanently drops the settlement event (provider will not retry). No webhook-event persistence/dedup table exists (verified model list in prisma/schema.prisma).

IDEMPOTENCY — lib/payments/post-payment.ts: atomic CAS `updateMany({id, status:'PENDING'} → COMPLETED)` (lines 28-31); first caller wins; then Policy→SUBMITTED (line 66-69), DNT report PDF, magic-link generation, confirmation email. This protects one Payment ROW against double processing (confirm API + webhook race), but NOT against two distinct PENDING rows created by calling initiate_payment twice — each has its own providerPaymentId and both can be captured. app/api/payments/confirm/route.ts: POST verifies status with the provider before settling (does not trust the client); GET is the PayU redirect return; both call the idempotent runPostPaymentFlow.

MODELS (prisma/schema.prisma) — Payment (563-582): strictly single-transaction (policyId FK, amount Float in bani, provider, providerPaymentId String? indexed, status PENDING/COMPLETED/FAILED/REFUNDED — no ABANDONED, no CANCELED — paidAt, failureReason, metadata Json). No PaymentSchedule, Installment, or WebhookEvent models exist. Policy (538-561): PENDING_SUBMISSION/SUBMITTED/ACTIVE/CANCELLED/EXPIRED; paymentFrequency String? (never written); created by accept_quote BEFORE payment with issuedAt stamped at acceptance time (quote-handlers.ts:369) and the uiAction is literally `show_policy_issued` (line 429). SUBMITTED→ACTIVE is a manual admin transition (app/api/admin/policies/[id]/status/route.ts, sets allianzPolicyNumber). Quote (514-536): premiumAnnual/Monthly/SemiAnnual/Quarterly all stored; paymentFrequency set at generate_quote from the PAYMENT_FREQUENCY questionnaire answer (quote-handlers.ts:140-159), domain 'annual'|'semi_annual'|'quarterly' (lib/engines/quote-engine.ts:19 — no 'monthly', yet payment defaults to monthly). accept_quote (quote-handlers.ts:316-439) takes only confirmAcceptance — no payment_option input — sets Quote→ACCEPTED, creates Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION), and marks the Conversation COMPLETED (lines 376-382).

PHASE/CONTEXT — lib/chat/derive-state.ts: 6 phases ending at CLOSING (acceptedQuote → CLOSING, line 41); there is NO PAYMENT or POLICY phase; deriveState reads no Payment or Policy data; CLOSING's nextBestAction is "present the quote and proceed to accept_quote" (line 64) — stale once the quote is already accepted. lib/chat/context-builder.ts:43-51,110-119 injects policy id/status/premiums/paymentFrequency into ToolContext; no payment attempts injected.

TESTS — zero test coverage of payment paths: grep over __tests__/ for post-payment/initiatePayment/webhook finds nothing; no __tests__/**/payment* files exist.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** accept_quote (quote-handlers.ts:316-439) takes only confirmAcceptance — no payment_option input
  **Correction:** The tool's input schema also accepts an optional quoteId parameter in addition to confirmAcceptance — both in the zod schema and the registry JSON schema. The handler ignores quoteId (it resolves the quote via the conversation's application), so the behavioral point stands, and 'no payment_option input' is correct. But 'takes only confirmAcceptance' is wrong at the schema level. _(lib/tools/validation.ts:107-112 (acceptQuoteSchema = z.object({ quoteId: z.string().optional(), confirmAcceptance: z.literal(true) }).strict()); lib/tools/registry.ts:876-879 (properties include quoteId, required: ['confirmAcceptance']); lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:317 (handler reads only args.confirmAcceptance))_
- **Claim:** WebhookEvent carries only event ('payment_succeeded'|'payment_failed') + providerPaymentId — NO provider event id, so event-level dedup is impossible at the interface
  **Correction:** WebhookEvent also carries an optional untyped metadata field (metadata?: Record<string, unknown>), which both providers populate (Stripe passes paymentIntent.metadata / originalEventType; PayU passes extOrderId/status). The conclusion is still correct — no typed provider event id field exists and neither provider puts the event id in metadata (Stripe discards event.id) — but 'carries only event + providerPaymentId' is incomplete, and dedup is unimplemented rather than strictly 'impossible' at the interface (metadata could carry an event id without an interface change). _(lib/payments/types.ts:21-25 (WebhookEvent { event, providerPaymentId, metadata?: Record<string, unknown> }); lib/payments/providers/stripe.ts:103-126 (passes paymentIntent.metadata, never event.id); lib/payments/providers/payu.ts:214-226 (metadata: { extOrderId, status }))_
- **Claim:** app/api/payments/confirm/route.ts: POST verifies status with the provider before settling (does not trust the client)
  **Correction:** Provider verification in the POST handler is conditional on payment.providerPaymentId being non-null: the entire getPaymentStatus check is wrapped in `if (payment.providerPaymentId)`, and when it is null the handler falls through and calls runPostPaymentFlow(paymentId) with NO provider verification, settling purely on the client's say-so. In practice every provider's createPaymentIntent returns an id so the field is populated for rows created by initiate_payment, but the unconditional phrasing overstates the guarantee — the trust boundary is the nullable providerPaymentId column, not the route. _(app/api/payments/confirm/route.ts:55-88 (`if (payment.providerPaymentId) { ...getPaymentStatus... }` then unconditional `await runPostPaymentFlow(paymentId)` at line 88); prisma/schema.prisma:570 (providerPaymentId String? — nullable))_

### Gaps

- None of the five catalog payment-phase tools exist (get_payment_status, resume_payment, retry_payment, change_payment_option) nor the cross-cutting get_open_items / get_customer_info reads; the only payment tool is initiate_payment.
- No schedule/installment data model: Payment is a single transaction; semi_annual/quarterly premiums are quoted and stored on Quote (quote-handlers.ts:196-198) but only one capture ever occurs; no next_due, no per-installment status, no recurrence mechanism.
- Policy.paymentFrequency is never populated (accept_quote omits it), so initiate_payment always charges one month's premium — annual-frequency customers are under-charged and the policy still advances to SUBMITTED after a single monthly payment.
- Policy is created and issuedAt-stamped at accept_quote, BEFORE any payment (quote-handlers.ts:358-371), and the UI announces 'show_policy_issued' — directly contradicting the catalog target where issue_policy is a system effect of the payment module on first successful payment.
- No webhook idempotency beyond per-row CAS: providerPaymentId is indexed but not unique, no provider event id is captured (lib/payments/types.ts WebhookEvent), no event-dedup/inbox table exists; two initiate_payment calls create two capturable intents → policy-level double charge is possible.
- Webhook routes return 200 on internal processing errors (both app/api/webhooks/*/route.ts), so a transient DB failure permanently loses the settlement event; no retry signal, no dead-letter.
- PayU webhook processes unsigned payloads when the OpenPayU-Signature header lacks a 'signature=' segment (providers/payu.ts:186) — forgeable settlement notification.
- No abandonment concept: PaymentStatus has no ABANDONED value, nothing detects stale PENDING intents, and orphan PENDING Payment rows accumulate on every re-initiation.
- No payment-phase representation in deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts ends at CLOSING) and accept_quote marks the Conversation COMPLETED — a returning customer in a new conversation has no engine path to their pending payment (no get_open_items, customer-scoped).
- accept_quote takes no payment_option even though the catalog specifies accept_quote(quote_id, payment_option) and bundles payment_options in get_quote_info; the binding frequency choice instead leaks in via a questionnaire answer consumed at generate_quote.
- Frequency domains are inconsistent: quote engine supports annual/semi_annual/quarterly (no monthly), payment handler supports annual/monthly (default monthly), Quote stores all four premium figures; premiumSemiAnnual/premiumQuarterly are never used by payment.
- Zero automated tests for initiate_payment, post-payment flow, confirm route, or either webhook route — the @payment Gherkin scenarios (no card data, retry, resume, no double charge, re-rating, auto-issuance) have no executable counterpart.

### Decision points

#### T8.D1 — Schedule data model: how should recurring premium collection (monthly/quarterly/semi-annual/annual) be represented, given Payment is single-transaction today?

- **✅ Recommended — engine-owned-schedule**: New PaymentSchedule entity (frequency, installmentAmount, totalInstallments, nextDueAt, status: pending_first_capture/active/abandoned/completed) plus Installment rows (sequence, dueAt, status), each Installment owning 0..n Payment attempt rows. The existing Payment model becomes the attempt/transaction record; the PaymentProvider interface stays at 'create/verify one charge'. The schedule is created at accept_quote from the chosen payment_option, priced from the Quote's stored per-frequency premiums.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + The engine remains the single source of truth: get_payment_status answers schedule/next_due/failures from engine state, which is the architecture's core invariant ('the engine decides legality and consequences'). + Provider-uniform: Stripe and PayU (redirect-based, no subscription parity) both already support exactly what this needs — one-off captures. + Insurance rules (grace, lapse, dunning, free-look refund, mid-schedule re-rating) are domain rules and get a domain home instead of being encoded as provider subscription mutations. + Fully testable with the Mock provider; the GUI swap-test client reads the same schedule. − The engine must own recurrence: off-session collection needs saved payment methods (Stripe SetupIntent) and a clock/dunning process; PayU may only support customer-initiated installments (re-engagement instead of auto-charge), which the schedule must model per provider capability.
- **provider-managed-subscriptions**: Use Stripe Billing subscriptions (price = installment, interval = frequency); the engine mirrors subscription state from webhooks; change_payment_option mutates the subscription.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Provider handles retries, dunning, and mandate storage natively. − The provider becomes the source of truth for schedule/next_due and the engine degrades to a cache of someone else's state — get_payment_status can no longer answer truthfully from engine state during webhook gaps. − Not provider-uniform: PayU has no Stripe-Billing equivalent, so the abstraction forks into two incompatible recurrence models. − Domain rules (lapse per insurance regulation, free-look interaction, re-rating semantics) get expressed in Stripe's vocabulary, coupling compliance behaviour to one vendor. − Untestable offline except by faking the vendor's subscription lifecycle.
- **single-payment-v1**: Keep Payment single-transaction; restrict the sellable frequency to annual (one capture covers the term); defer all schedule entities until installments are actually offered.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Smallest correct surface; one capture genuinely settles an annual policy. − Contradicts existing data and UX: the quote engine already prices semi_annual/quarterly, the PAYMENT_FREQUENCY question exists, and Quote stores all four figures — shipping a payment phase that ignores the chosen frequency either mis-sells (charge annual when quarterly was chosen) or silently narrows the product. − get_payment_status's contract (schedule, next_due) and change_payment_option become vacuous, so the catalog's payment phase cannot be implemented against it. − The monthly-undercharge bug would be 'fixed' by deleting the feature rather than modelling it.

**Rationale:** The whole transformation rests on the engine being the sole legitimate source of truth that the agent (or a GUI) merely renders. A schedule the engine cannot read locally breaks get_payment_status, breaks the swap test, and pushes insurance-domain rules (grace/lapse/re-rating/free-look) into a vendor's subscription model that only one of the two integrated providers even has. Engine-owned PaymentSchedule + Installment keeps the PaymentProvider abstraction at the one capability both providers actually share (single capture), makes every Gherkin @payment scenario expressible as engine state transitions testable with the Mock provider, and gives the re_rating consequence a concrete artifact (old schedule vs new schedule). The off-session-collection burden is real but is an insurance-domain obligation (dunning and lapse are regulated behaviours) that must live in the engine regardless of who fires the charge.

**Depends on / interacts with:** quote-lifecycle, application-lifecycle, policy-post-sale, commit-envelope, product-data, legality-engine

#### T8.D2 — Policy issuance timing: keep policy-before-payment, or invert so the payment module issues the policy on first successful payment?

- **✅ Recommended — payment-issues-policy**: accept_quote creates NO Policy — it binds the payment_option, creates the PaymentSchedule (pending_first_capture), and advances to @payment. The first successful capture, inside the same idempotent settlement transaction, creates the Policy as a system effect. Policy state machine: ISSUED (or PENDING_SUBMISSION if the manual Allianz submission step remains) → ACTIVE (insurer/admin confirms, sets allianzPolicyNumber) → LAPSED (missed installments after grace) / CANCELLED (free-look or post-sale rule) / EXPIRED (term end). Transition owners: payment module creates; admin/insurer integration activates; policy-post-sale rules lapse/cancel. The agent has zero transitions — exactly as the catalog states ('issue_policy is a system effect... not an agent tool').
  _Tradeoffs:_ + The data model stops lying: before money moves there is no policy in any legal sense — what exists is an accepted quote awaiting consideration, which Quote(ACCEPTED)+PaymentSchedule encode precisely. + 'Policy exists' becomes a trustworthy invariant, so the catalog's exposure conditions for @policy tools (get_policy_status/get_policy_documents 'a policy exists') work without status-filtering caveats. + Kills today's contradictions: issuedAt stamped at acceptance, show_policy_issued shown pre-payment, admin stats counting phantom policies. + Free-look and refund logic anchor to a real issuance timestamp. − Payment must re-anchor: Payment/Installment reference the schedule (and through it the quote), not policyId; every consumer that assumes policy-exists-pre-payment (initiate_payment's gate, confirm GET's redirect chain, dnt-report, context-builder) must re-anchor to the schedule — a coherence requirement, not an effort argument.
- **pending-payment-policy**: accept_quote creates Policy(PENDING_PAYMENT); the first successful capture transitions it to ISSUED/ACTIVE. Payment keeps its policyId FK.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Single stable anchor for the whole payment phase; minimal FK reshaping. − Reintroduces the phantom-entity problem in softer form: every consumer of Policy must know that PENDING_PAYMENT policies are not policies (documents must not be issuable, status reads must caveat, counts must filter), i.e. an invariant enforced by convention at every call site instead of by existence. − The @policy phase exposure condition 'a policy exists' becomes wrong and needs a parallel 'a real policy exists' predicate. − Cancellation semantics blur: cancelling pre-payment is really abandoning a payment, but it would surface as a Policy transition, conflating two different lifecycle stages.
- **keep-current**: Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION) at accept_quote, SUBMITTED on payment, ACTIVE manually — as implemented today.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Already wired end-to-end. − Directly contradicts the catalog and the Gherkin scenario 'First successful payment issues the policy automatically'. − issuedAt at acceptance is factually wrong and feeds the suitability/DNT report. − PENDING_SUBMISSION conflates 'awaiting payment' with 'awaiting insurer submission' — two unrelated gates in one status — which is why the paymentFrequency bug could ship invisibly: the status machine cannot express 'partially paid'.

**Rationale:** The catalog is explicit that policy issuance is a payment-module system effect, and the architectural argument stands on its own: an entity that exists before its legal predicate (paid consideration) forces every consumer to re-derive the truth from a status field, which is exactly the class of divergence this transformation is meant to eliminate. With an engine-owned schedule (DP1), the payment phase has a natural anchor — the accepted Quote and its PaymentSchedule — so the Policy row regains a crisp meaning: coverage issued. The settlement transaction (webhook/confirm → installment paid → first capture? → create Policy) is also the only place issuance can be made idempotent together with payment dedup, which option (a) gets for free by construction.

**Depends on / interacts with:** quote-lifecycle, policy-post-sale, phase-model, commit-envelope, legality-engine

#### T8.D3 — Webhook reconciliation & idempotency: how do provider events settle payments exactly once, and how does get_payment_status read truthfully during the pending→paid gap?

- **✅ Recommended — transactional-inbox**: (1) providerPaymentId becomes @unique on Payment. (2) New PaymentEvent table with @@unique([provider, providerEventId]); the PaymentProvider.WebhookEvent type gains eventId (Stripe event.id; PayU a derived orderId+status key); processing = insert-event-or-ignore + payment CAS + installment/schedule advance + (first capture) policy issuance, all in ONE transaction. (3) Invariant: at most one open (PENDING) Payment attempt per installment — re-initiation supersedes (provider-cancels) the prior intent instead of stacking a second capturable one. (4) On internal processing failure return 5xx so the provider retries (replacing today's 200-swallow); 200 only for verified-but-irrelevant events. (5) One shared reconcile(paymentId) function — provider.getPaymentStatus → same idempotent settlement path — used by the webhook, the confirm route, and get_payment_status when a PENDING attempt looks stale; the agent reports 'processing' until the engine says paid.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Exactly-once settlement holds across BOTH duplicate events (event unique key) and duplicate intents (single-open-attempt invariant) — today's CAS only covers the former within one row. + An auditable event log is a compliance asset for premium collection. + get_payment_status never has to guess: engine state, lazily reconciled, is the single answer — satisfying the Gherkin 'treats the payment as paid once'. − Synchronous settlement inside the webhook request: a slow downstream (PDF, email) must be moved out of the transaction (it already is best-effort in post-payment.ts) to keep the handler fast.
- **hardened-cas-only**: Keep the current per-row CAS, add @unique on providerPaymentId, fix the PayU unsigned-payload skip, and stop returning 200 on errors — but persist no events.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Touches nothing structural. − Cannot distinguish a replayed event from new money once schedules have many installments: CAS-per-row is only sufficient when the row set is fixed at exactly one, which DP1 abolishes. − No audit trail of provider notifications (reconciliation disputes become he-said-she-said with the provider). − Does nothing about the two-capturable-intents double charge, which is the actual live risk.
- **async-outbox-queue**: Webhook handler only persists the raw event (inbox) and acks; a queue/worker settles asynchronously with retries and dead-lettering.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Maximal delivery robustness and handler latency isolation. − Introduces eventual consistency between event receipt and settlement that get_payment_status must then reason about ('received but not yet applied' becomes a fourth truth-state the agent has to narrate). − Adds an availability dependency (worker/queue) to the correctness story without changing it — the dedup keys and transactional settlement are identical to the inbox design, just deferred. − The deterministic-engine property is easier to test when settlement is synchronous with receipt.

**Rationale:** Correctness here has two independent halves and the current code covers neither fully: event-level dedup (needs a persisted unique event identity — impossible today because the provider interface discards the event id) and intent-level dedup (needs the one-open-attempt-per-installment invariant — violated today because initiate_payment unconditionally creates). The transactional inbox closes both while keeping settlement synchronous, which is the property that lets get_payment_status be truthful from engine state alone. The async queue is a deployment evolution of the same design, not a competing model, and it weakens the truth-during-gap story; the CAS-only option is structurally incapable of supporting installments. Independently mandatory fixes that belong to this decision: PayU must hard-reject unsigned payloads (providers/payu.ts:186), the HMAC-MD5 scheme must be verified against the OpenPayU IPN spec, and Stripe's 'unknown event mapped to payment_succeeded' (providers/stripe.ts:118-126) must become an explicit ignored variant.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, testing-bdd, policy-post-sale

#### T8.D4 — Recovery tools: are resume_payment and retry_payment distinct commits from initiate_payment, or one operation with engine-determined mode — and how do returning customers find their pending payment?

- **three-distinct-tools**: Catalog-literal: initiate_payment (first attempt), resume_payment (abandoned/incomplete), retry_payment (last attempt failed). The engine exposes exactly one at a time via available_actions; each returns a payment session/link handoff.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Self-describing action surface: available_actions alone tells a UI whether to label the button Pay/Resume/Retry, and the agent's narration maps 1:1 to tool names. − The three tools have identical inputs, identical outputs (session/link), identical consequence (applied), and mutually exclusive exposure conditions — they are one operation wearing three names, which triples the schema surface the LLM can mis-pick (calling retry when state says abandoned → avoidable rejected noise) while encoding zero decisions the engine doesn't already make in its exposure logic.
- **✅ Recommended — single-ensure-payment-session**: One commit — ensure_payment_session(application_id) — whose engine-side semantics are 'return the canonical open payment session for the currently due installment, creating, reusing, or superseding the provider intent as state requires'. The response carries mode: started|resumed|retried for narration; get_payment_status (read) carries the status that motivates the call. The catalog framing explicitly permits eliminating tools where the flow simplifies.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + It IS the single-open-attempt invariant from DP3 expressed as a tool: one code path, one test surface, impossible to stack capturable intents by picking the wrong verb. + Passes the swap test cleanly — a GUI 'Pay now' button calls the same operation in all three states. + The agent cannot commit an illegal mode because mode is not an input. − The action surface is less self-labelling; the UI/agent must read get_payment_status (or the returned mode) to phrase the button/narration — information the read tool provides anyway.
- **recall-initiate**: Keep only today's initiate_payment and let the agent re-call it after failures/abandonment (the current de facto behaviour).
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Nothing new. − Today's implementation creates a fresh provider intent and Payment row per call — this is the double-charge surface, not a recovery mechanism. − Gates on Policy PENDING_SUBMISSION, which evaporates under DP2's issuance inversion. − No engine state distinguishes failed from abandoned, so the Gherkin retry/resume scenarios are unimplementable.

**Rationale:** The engine already decides which recovery mode is legal — that is precisely what 'exposed when' means — so encoding the mode in three tool names duplicates engine knowledge into the agent's action-selection problem and creates a new failure class (wrong-verb commits) without adding any expressiveness. A single ensure-session commit makes the DP3 invariant (at most one capturable intent) structural rather than disciplinary, and the returned mode preserves every bit of narration the three-name version offered. Alongside it: get_payment_status (read: schedule, per-installment status, next_due, failure reasons, derived 'abandoned' for stale PENDING attempts — derivable at read time without a cron until dunning/lapse needs a clock) and a NEW cross-cutting get_open_items read that is CUSTOMER-scoped, not conversation-scoped — mandatory because accept_quote marks the Conversation COMPLETED, so a customer returning days later arrives in a fresh conversation and the pending schedule must be reachable through identity (aligning with the CustomerProfile SSOT direction of customer-scoped state). get_open_items exposure requires an identified customer, which couples it to the identity topic.

**Depends on / interacts with:** identity, legality-engine, application-lifecycle, phase-model, commit-envelope

#### T8.D5 — change_payment_option pre-capture: does re-rating mutate the accepted Quote or produce a derived schedule record?

- **mutate-accepted-quote**: Update Quote.paymentFrequency (and the operative premium figure) in place on the ACCEPTED quote; the payment phase re-reads the quote.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + One record to read for 'what the customer pays'. − Destroys the audit trail of what was accepted: the quote is the priced offer the customer expressly consented to at accept_quote (requires_confirmation), and compliance requires that artifact to remain inspectable as-consented. − Violates the catalog's immutability rule ('Issuing a quote completes the application (immutable thereafter)') and the one-application-one-quote invariant the regression scenarios guard.
- **✅ Recommended — derived-schedule-record**: Quote stays immutable (it already stores premiumAnnual/SemiAnnual/Quarterly — all options priced at generation, bundled into get_quote_info as payment_options). The chosen option lives on the PaymentSchedule created at accept_quote(payment_option). change_payment_option, legal only while capturedCount == 0 (engine exposure condition 'payment not yet captured'), recomputes the installment plan from the quote's stored figures (or via calculateQuote if per-frequency loadings appear later) and supersedes the schedule — old schedule retained/marked superseded for audit. Returns re_rating with old-vs-new schedule; requires_confirmation gates application; the open provider intent is cancelled and re-created at the new amount (DP4's ensure-session does this naturally).
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Quote remains the immutable consented artifact; the schedule is the mutable execution plan — clean separation of offer vs collection. + The re_rating consequence has a concrete diffable payload (two schedules). + The superseded-schedule trail satisfies premium-collection auditability. − Two records describe price (quote = offered options, schedule = elected plan); readers must know the schedule is operative — mitigated by get_payment_status being the only payment-phase read.
- **cancel-and-reapply**: Treat a frequency change like any post-quote change: cancel_quote + new application pre-filled from the old.
  _Tradeoffs:_ + Maximal uniformity with the post-quote-change rule. − Wrong classification: the catalog deliberately places payment_option selection in the quote/payment phases (accept_quote(payment_option), change_payment_option with re_rating) precisely because frequency is not underwriting input — no risk answer changes, so forcing a re-application re-runs eligibility for nothing and contradicts the catalog's own tool.

**Rationale:** Frequency selection is choosing among price points the quote already contains — the quote engine computes all four figures at generation (lib/engines/quote-engine.ts:82-84) and Quote persists them — so re-rating is not a re-quote and must not touch the consented artifact. The schedule is the natural owner of frequency, installment amount, and next_due, and superseding it (rather than editing in place) gives the re_rating consequence its payload and compliance its trail. Corollary that resolves a current incoherence: the PAYMENT_FREQUENCY questionnaire answer (consumed at generate_quote, quote-handlers.ts:140-159) stops being the binding choice — it can seed a default, but the binding election happens at accept_quote(payment_option), which today takes no such argument. A rounding rule must be defined with the schedule: N installments of round(annual/N) do not sum to premiumAnnual, so the schedule must carry an explicit remainder policy (e.g., last installment absorbs the delta).

**Depends on / interacts with:** quote-lifecycle, questionnaire-consequences, commit-envelope, product-data

### Risks

- LIVE double-charge surface: every initiate_payment call creates a fresh provider intent + Payment row; the post-payment CAS is per-row, so two intents paid by the customer both settle. Must be closed by the single-open-attempt invariant before any recovery tool re-calls initiation.
- LIVE under-collection bug: Policy.paymentFrequency is never set (accept_quote omits it), so the annual branch in payment-handlers.ts:80 never fires — every sale captures one month's premium and the policy advances to SUBMITTED with no mechanism for the remaining installments.
- Webhook 200-on-internal-error (both webhook routes) permanently drops settlement events — payments stuck PENDING forever with no provider retry and no dead-letter; flipping to 5xx-on-failure must accompany idempotent processing or retries will partially re-execute today's non-transactional handler.
- PayU webhook accepts unsigned payloads when the signature header segment is absent (providers/payu.ts:186), making settlement forgeable; the HMAC-MD5 verification scheme also needs validation against the actual OpenPayU IPN spec before production.
- Issuance inversion (DP2) re-anchors Payment from policyId to schedule/quote; consumers assuming policy-before-payment (initiate_payment gate, confirm GET redirect chain, generateDntReport(policy.id), context-builder policy injection, show_policy_issued UI) would silently break if migrated partially — the inversion must land as one coherent change with the schedule model.
- Off-session recurring collection is provider-asymmetric: Stripe supports saved-mandate auto-charge (SetupIntent), PayU's redirect flow may only support customer-initiated installments — the schedule must model per-provider capability (auto-charge vs dunning-by-re-engagement) or monthly schedules on PayU will silently never collect.
- Phase-model gap: deriveState has no PAYMENT/POLICY phase and accept_quote marks the Conversation COMPLETED — until the phase-model topic adds payment-phase derivation (anchored on accepted quote + schedule, customer-scoped), the new tools have no exposure context and re-engagement scenarios cannot bind.
- Zero existing tests on payment paths means the refactor has no regression net; per the project's TDD rules, the @payment Gherkin scenarios (no card data, retry, resume, no-double-charge reconciliation, re-rating, auto-issuance) should be written as failing tests before implementation.
- Money as Float: Payment.amount (bani) and all premium fields are Float; installment math compounds rounding (12×round(annual/12) ≠ annual) — the schedule needs integer minor-units and an explicit remainder rule, else collected totals drift from quoted premiums.
- PayU lacks a native unique event id, so its dedup key must be derived (orderId+status); if PayU legitimately replays distinct transitions with the same tuple, a derived key could mask a real event — the dedup design needs a provider-specific key strategy documented per provider.
- Stripe provider maps unknown webhook event types to payment_succeeded with only metadata flagging them (providers/stripe.ts:118-126); any future route that forgets the metadata filter would settle payments on unrelated events — the interface should make 'ignored' a first-class event variant.

---

## T9. Policy & post-sale: status/documents/cancellation, free-look window, Allianz submission

> Topic key: `policy-post-sale`

### Current state (code-grounded)

DATA MODEL (prisma/schema.prisma): Policy (lines 538-561) has quoteId (1:1 Quote), customerId, productId, allianzPolicyNumber (String?), status PolicyStatus @default(PENDING_SUBMISSION), effectiveFrom/effectiveUntil (DateTime? — NEVER written by any code; only read in app/dashboard/(protected)/page.tsx:104-105 and components/dashboard/policy-hero-card.tsx), premium fields, coverageSummary Json, suitabilityReportPath (String? — raw filesystem path), issuedAt. PolicyStatus enum (lines 33-39): PENDING_SUBMISSION, SUBMITTED, ACTIVE, CANCELLED, EXPIRED — no LAPSED. PaymentStatus has REFUNDED (line 45) but no code path ever writes it (verified by grep over lib/app/prisma). Product (lines 104-141) has gracePeriod and contractTerm as free-text strings ('60 days for premium payment' in prisma/seeds/seed-product.ts:452) and quoteValidityDays Int — no free-look/cooling-off field anywhere.

LIFECYCLE WRITES: accept_quote (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:316-443) creates Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION) BEFORE payment, sets issuedAt=now() at acceptance (line 369), sets Conversation status=COMPLETED (lines 376-382), and returns uiAction 'show_policy_issued' with message 'Your policy has been created...' (lines 426-438) — issuance narrated before payment, underwriting review, or Allianz confirmation. initiate_payment (lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts) requires status PENDING_SUBMISSION (line 68). lib/payments/post-payment.ts:66-69 auto-sets Policy → SUBMITTED on first successful payment — directly conflicting with docs/allianz-submission-sop.md, where SUBMITTED means 'operator emailed Allianz' (SOP §6) and PENDING_SUBMISSION is the operator's work queue (§2). Admin route app/api/admin/policies/[id]/status/route.ts allows ADMIN/OPERATOR to set ANY of the 5 statuses with no transition validation, optionally writes allianzPolicyNumber, overwrites issuedAt when status=ACTIVE (line 59), and the SOP-promised customer activation email is a console.log stub (lines 75-81). Admin UI: app/admin/(protected)/applications/[id]/client.tsx (mark SUBMITTED line 263; activate with Allianz number when SUBMITTED line 271), app/admin/(protected)/policies/page.tsx (list, filters by all 5 statuses), dashboard counts PENDING_SUBMISSION+SUBMITTED together as 'new' (app/admin/(protected)/page.tsx:19).

DOCUMENTS: One real document exists — the DNT suitability report, generated by lib/compliance/dnt-report.ts (jsPDF, IDD-framed) during post-payment (lib/payments/post-payment.ts:71-84), written to REPORTS_PATH (default './tmp/reports' — ephemeral) and the path stored in Policy.suitabilityReportPath (dnt-report.ts:443-459). Served with role-checked auth by app/api/documents/dnt-report/[policyId]/route.ts. Customer dashboard (components/dashboard/document-list.tsx, app/dashboard/(protected)/documents/page.tsx) hardcodes 3 documents — policy PDF, DNT report, payment receipt — but only DNT is real; the other two are alert() placeholders. No IPID and no terms/conditions document exists anywhere in code (searched lib/, app/, prisma/); IPID appears only in the target catalog/Gherkin docs. No Document table exists.

TOOLS & EXPOSURE: lib/tools/registry.ts registers 33 tools — ZERO policy tools. get_policy_status / get_policy_documents / request_cancellation / get_policy_details do not exist. prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts post-sale packs (post-sale-onboarding line 241, post-sale-support 285, post-sale-claims 329, post-sale-renewal 372) all list phantom 'get_policy_details' in allowedTools (lines 277, 322, 364, 406); post-sale-renewal also lists phantom 'get_quote' (line 409; registry has only get_quote_details/generate_quote). These packs are additionally DORMANT: lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:597 hardcodes recommendedSlugs=[] — no skill pack is ever activated. The workflow seed (prisma/seeds/seed-workflows.ts) ends at step 'completed' with allowedTools: [] (lines 438-443) — no post-sale step. lib/chat/derive-state.ts has 6 phases ending at CLOSING (quote ACCEPTED, line 41) with no POLICY phase; CLOSING's nextBestAction ('present the quote and proceed to accept_quote', line 64) is stale once the quote is already accepted.

ALLIANZ SOP (docs/allianz-submission-sop.md): fully manual back-office process — operator reviews PENDING_SUBMISSION applications (2h SLA), generates a pre-filled email in admin, sends via own mail client with the DNT report attached, marks SUBMITTED, then on Allianz confirmation enters the Allianz policy number and activates → ACTIVE (24h SLA; customer email claimed automatic but is the console.log stub above). Allianz rejection → operator marks CANCELLED and contacts the customer (§10).

TESTS: e2e (e2e/lib/db-verifier.ts:180-198) verifies Policy exists with status PENDING_SUBMISSION|SUBMITTED after payment; all e2e scenarios (e2e/scenarios/*.test.ts) stop at show_payment_success/show_policy_issued. No post-sale, cancellation, or free-look coverage anywhere. v2-build-plan.md:452 is the only free-look mention in the repo ('30-day cooling-off period communicated').

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** Admin dashboard "counts PENDING_SUBMISSION+SUBMITTED together as 'new'" (app/admin/(protected)/page.tsx:19)
  **Correction:** The combined count at line 18-20 exists, but it is the `pendingPolicies` metric rendered as the card 'Polite in asteptare' (pending policies), not 'new'. The dashboard's 'new' card ('Aplicatii noi') is a different metric: it counts Applications with status 'OPEN' (line 17), not policies. So PENDING_SUBMISSION+SUBMITTED are counted together as 'pending', and 'new' refers to open applications. _(app/admin/(protected)/page.tsx:15-20 (`openApplications` = prisma.application.count({where:{status:'OPEN'}}) at line 17; `pendingPolicies` = prisma.policy.count({where:{status:{in:['PENDING_SUBMISSION','SUBMITTED']}}}) at lines 18-20) and lines 33-35 (cards: {label:'Aplicatii noi', value: openApplications} vs {label:'Polite in asteptare', value: pendingPolicies}))_

### Gaps

- No policy-phase tools exist at all: lib/tools/registry.ts has no get_policy_status/get_policy_documents/request_cancellation; the catalog's entire @policy section is unimplemented.
- Phantom tool references: seed-skill-packs.ts post-sale packs grant 'get_policy_details' (4 packs) and 'get_quote' (renewal pack) — neither is registered; and orchestrator.ts:597 hardcodes recommendedSlugs=[] so no pack (post-sale or otherwise) is ever activated, making the entire POST_SALE pack layer dead config.
- SUBMITTED status has two contradictory meanings: lib/payments/post-payment.ts:66-69 auto-sets it on payment success, while the SOP and admin UI define it as 'operator emailed Allianz'. The state 'paid, awaiting back-office submission' is unrepresentable, and the audit trail cannot distinguish paid-only from actually-submitted policies.
- accept_quote over-narrates: 'show_policy_issued' uiAction + 'Your policy has been created' message fire at quote acceptance, before payment, submission, or Allianz confirmation — violating the spec invariant that the agent never narrates a transition the engine did not perform.
- Policy.effectiveFrom/effectiveUntil are never written; issuedAt is written twice with different meanings (at accept_quote, then overwritten on activation). There is no reliable anchor date for a free-look window or for EXPIRED detection.
- No free-look/cooling-off logic anywhere: no window-length config, no request_cancellation, no refund path (PaymentStatus.REFUNDED is a dead enum value). Customers cannot cancel a policy through any channel except calling a human.
- No LAPSED status and no way to detect installment failure: Payment is a single-transaction model with no schedule; the catalog's 'lapsed' status is unreachable until the payments topic delivers recurring schedules.
- No Document model: the only stored document is a raw filesystem path (suitabilityReportPath) defaulting to ephemeral ./tmp/reports; policy schedule PDF, IPID, terms, and payment receipt shown in the customer dashboard are placeholders that do not exist.
- Admin status route (app/api/admin/policies/[id]/status/route.ts) performs no transition validation — any status can jump to any other, including un-cancelling, and activation without an allianzPolicyNumber is accepted.
- No post-sale conversational surface: Conversation is set COMPLETED at accept_quote, deriveState has no POLICY phase, the workflow's terminal step exposes no tools — a returning policyholder has no modeled state from which policy tools could be exposed.
- The SOP-promised automatic customer activation email is a console.log stub in the admin status route.
- Zero test coverage past payment: no e2e/BDD scenario exercises policy status, documents, or cancellation (inside or outside the free-look window).

### Decision points

#### T9.D1 — Where do policy documents (policy schedule, suitability report, IPID, terms, receipt) live — path fields on Policy, a Document table, or on-demand regeneration?

- **More path columns on Policy**: Extend the current pattern: add policyDocPath, ipidPath, termsPath, receiptPath alongside suitabilityReportPath; each generator writes a file and stores the path.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Keeps a flat model, but cannot represent versions, product-level shared docs (one IPID per product version would be duplicated per policy), or acknowledgement events; auth and serving logic gets re-implemented per route; raw FS paths in the DB couple storage layout to the schema and break on storage migration.
- **✅ Recommended — Document table with kind/version/storage provider**: New Document model: id, customerId, policyId?, productId?, kind enum (SUITABILITY_REPORT, POLICY_SCHEDULE, IPID, TERMS, PAYMENT_RECEIPT), version, storageKey (behind a storage-provider interface: FS now, object storage later), contentHash, generatedAt, source (GENERATED | STATIC_PER_PRODUCT_VERSION). Customer-generated docs (suitability report, policy schedule, receipt) are immutable per-policy rows; IPID/terms are static per product version, attached by reference. get_policy_documents/get_policy_info reads this table; one auth-checked download route serves all kinds; suitabilityReportPath migrates in and is retired.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Introduces one new aggregate, but gives immutable compliance snapshots (the doc the customer saw at sale is provably the doc on file via contentHash), uniform authorization, versioning when product terms change, and a single deterministic read for the tool. Customer-scoped rows align with the CustomerProfile SSOT direction (documents outlive the conversation).
- **Generate on demand, store nothing**: Regenerate every document from DB state at request time; no stored artifacts.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No storage to manage, but fails compliance: regenerating after any data change (price re-rating, question edits, product reseed) silently produces a document different from what the customer was shown at sale; no audit trail of what was actually delivered; IPID/terms aren't derivable from DB state at all.

**Rationale:** Compliance documents are evidence — they must be immutable snapshots tied to the moment of sale, individually authorizable, and queryable as a set ('give me everything for policy X'). Only a first-class Document aggregate provides that: path columns can't model product-level static docs or versions, and on-demand regeneration breaks the snapshot guarantee outright. The storage-provider indirection decouples the schema from the current ephemeral ./tmp/reports filesystem, which is itself a data-loss bug. Static IPID/terms per product version slot naturally into product-data versioning rather than per-policy copies.

**Depends on / interacts with:** product-data, quote-lifecycle, tool-mapping, testing-bdd

#### T9.D2 — Free-look (cooling-off): where does the window length live, how does the deterministic request_cancellation rule engine work, and how does it interact with refunds?

- **Statutory constant in the handler**: Hardcode 30 days in the request_cancellation handler; window = activatedAt + 30d; inside → cancel+refund, outside → rejected.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simplest rule, but legally wrong as a constant: in Romania the withdrawal right is channel-dependent (30 calendar days for DISTANCE-sold life insurance under OG 85/2004 transposing Directive 2002/65/EC — which matches v2-build-plan.md's '30-day cooling-off'; 20 days for face-to-face life insurance under the Solvency II art. 186 transposition). A hardcoded constant also changes retroactively for in-flight policies if the law or product changes.
- **Product-config field read at cancellation time**: Add freeLookDays (and the anchor rule) to Product config; request_cancellation computes window = anchorDate + product.freeLookDays at call time.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Configurable per product/channel, but the rule's outcome for an existing policy changes whenever someone edits product config — the same cancellation request can be legal on Monday and illegal on Tuesday without anything about the policy changing. Violates data integrity for in-flight contracts and makes outcomes non-reproducible in audits.
- **✅ Recommended — Per-policy snapshot: freeLookEndsAt frozen at activation**: Product config (freeLookDays, default 30 for the distance channel) is the SOURCE, but at the moment the policy becomes ACTIVE the engine computes and stores freeLookEndsAt on the Policy (anchored to activation/customer-notification — the legally relevant 'informed the contract is concluded' event). request_cancellation is then a pure deterministic comparison: now <= freeLookEndsAt → requires_confirmation, and on confirmation Policy → CANCELLED (terminal) + refund command to the payments module (full premium refund; Payment → REFUNDED); now > freeLookEndsAt → rejected with reason (term-life 'protect' has no surrender value) with escalate_to_human as the referral path. get_policy_status surfaces freeLookEndsAt so the agent can state the deadline from injected state.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One extra column and a write at activation, but the legality decision becomes a frozen, audit-reproducible timestamp comparison — immune to later config edits, trivially unit-testable at the boundary (T-1s/T+1s), and visible to the customer before they ask. Couples cancellation to the refund primitive the payments topic must provide.

**Rationale:** The free-look deadline is a property of the individual contract at the moment it was concluded, not of today's product configuration — freezing it at activation is the only option where the engine's answer is reproducible, auditable, and immune to config drift. The product config still owns the number for NEW policies (and must stay channel-aware: 30d distance vs 20d face-to-face in RO — needs legal sign-off, do not bake either constant into code). The refund is part of the same commit consequence chain (requires_confirmation → terminal + refund), which finally gives PaymentStatus.REFUNDED a live write path; the refund execution primitive belongs to the payments topic. Note: today nothing writes effectiveFrom or a clean activation timestamp (issuedAt is double-written), so an explicit activatedAt is a prerequisite.

**Depends on / interacts with:** payments, legality-engine, commit-envelope, product-data, testing-bdd

#### T9.D3 — What is the policy status machine (including lapse), and who owns each transition?

- **Keep current 5 statuses with free-form admin updates**: Status quo: PENDING_SUBMISSION/SUBMITTED/ACTIVE/CANCELLED/EXPIRED, any actor with the admin route can set anything; lapse not modeled.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No migration, but the machine is already broken: SUBMITTED is double-owned (payment webhook AND operator button) with contradictory meanings, illegal jumps (CANCELLED→ACTIVE) are accepted, and the catalog's 'lapsed' answer is impossible. Any get_policy_status tool built on this surfaces ambiguous states to customers.
- **✅ Recommended — Explicit transition table with per-transition owners, LAPSED added**: Statuses: PENDING_SUBMISSION (payment captured, awaiting back-office — post-payment.ts STOPS auto-setting SUBMITTED) → SUBMITTED (operator emailed Allianz) → ACTIVE (operator confirms with mandatory allianzPolicyNumber; activatedAt + effectiveFrom/effectiveUntil + freeLookEndsAt written here) → terminal CANCELLED / EXPIRED, plus LAPSED reachable only from ACTIVE and reversible to ACTIVE on reinstatement. Owners are exclusive per transition: payment module owns policy entry into PENDING_SUBMISSION; back-office owns PENDING_SUBMISSION→SUBMITTED→ACTIVE and Allianz-rejection→CANCELLED; the legality engine owns free-look ACTIVE→CANCELLED via request_cancellation; a scheduled job owns ACTIVE→LAPSED (driven by installment-failure events from the payments topic) and ACTIVE→EXPIRED (effectiveUntil passed); the agent owns NOTHING — read-only. One transition-validation service enforces the table for every writer including the admin route.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Requires fixing the post-payment SUBMITTED write and adding enum value + validation service, but restores single-writer semantics per transition, makes the SOP's audit trail truthful (paid ≠ submitted), gives the catalog's active/lapsed/cancelled answer a real source, and makes illegal admin jumps impossible. LAPSED stays structurally dormant until payments delivers schedules — acceptable because the transition owner (job) is defined now and activated later.
- **Minimal stored pipeline + derived liveness**: Store only the submission pipeline (PENDING_SUBMISSION/SUBMITTED/ACTIVE/CANCELLED); compute lapsed/expired as derived predicates from dates and payment rows at read time, never stored.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No status-drift risk and no jobs, but lapse/expiry become opinions of whoever computes them: no record of WHEN a policy lapsed or what notice was sent, grace-period rules get re-evaluated differently by each reader, and regulatory/audit questions ('was this policy in force on date X?') require replaying payment history. Liveness of an insurance contract is a legal fact that deserves a recorded transition.

**Rationale:** An insurance policy's status is a contractual fact with legal consequences — every transition needs a recorded owner, timestamp, and reason, which only an explicit machine provides. The current code already demonstrates why free-form writes fail: the SUBMITTED double-write makes the audit trail unable to prove whether Allianz ever received a case. Derived liveness (option C) is elegant for display but unacceptable for the record of when cover lapsed. The agent-never-writes rule follows directly from the swap-test invariant: a GUI could render the same machine, and neither client may push it.

**Depends on / interacts with:** payments, legality-engine, phase-model, commit-envelope

#### T9.D4 — Where does the Allianz submission step (PENDING_SUBMISSION → SUBMITTED → ACTIVE) fit, and does the agent surface it or is it back-office only?

- **Back-office only, invisible to the agent**: The manual SOP remains the whole story; the agent's knowledge of the policy ends at payment success and it deflects 'where is my policy?' questions to human support.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Clean separation, but creates a guaranteed conversational dead zone: every customer who pays will ask about their policy within the 2h-24h SLA window, and an agent that cannot answer from state will either deflect (pathology already catalogued in this project) or hallucinate. It also leaves the existing over-narration at accept_quote as the only 'status' the customer ever hears.
- **✅ Recommended — Agent reads the pipeline, back-office owns the transitions**: get_policy_status/get_policy_info exposes the submission pipeline read-only, mapped to honest customer language ('payment received, your file is being prepared for Allianz-Tiriac', 'submitted to the insurer', 'active since X, policy number Y'). All transitions stay with operators (admin UI per the SOP) and the payment module; the agent never marks anything submitted or active. Companion fixes: accept_quote stops emitting 'show_policy_issued' (replaced with a 'policy created, pending payment' surface), and activation triggers the real customer email (currently a console.log stub).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Requires the status machine of the previous decision (so the read is truthful) and honest re-wording of the acceptance flow, but eliminates both failure modes: no dead zone (the agent answers from injected state) and no fabrication (it can only relay what the engine recorded). Manual SOP stays manual — automation of the email itself is an independent back-office concern that doesn't change the agent contract.
- **Agent-driven submission tooling**: Give the agent (or a system step it triggers) tools to mark policies submitted/active as part of the conversation flow.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Closes the loop fastest in demos, but the agent would own transitions whose ground truth lives outside the system (a human sent an email; Allianz confirmed) — the engine cannot validate them, so this re-introduces narration-as-state-change, the exact failure the transformation is designed to eliminate. Submission is back-office workflow, not conversation.

**Rationale:** The SOP is genuinely manual (operator email + Allianz confirmation), and the ground truth of submission/activation enters the system only through operators — so transition ownership must stay back-office. But read access is a customer-experience and honesty requirement: the catalog's own invariant says the agent surfaces engine state and never narrates beyond it, which is only possible if the pipeline state is injectable. This also forces the two truthfulness fixes the current code needs regardless (accept_quote's premature 'policy issued' UI, and the phantom activation email).

**Depends on / interacts with:** payments, quote-lifecycle, tool-mapping, phase-model

#### T9.D5 — Tool surface for @policy: the catalog's three tools (get_policy_status, get_policy_documents, request_cancellation) or a simplification — and what happens to the phantom get_policy_details in the post-sale skill packs?

- **Catalog-faithful three tools**: Implement get_policy_status (status + schedule + freeLookEndsAt), get_policy_documents (Document rows + download URLs), request_cancellation (commit), exactly as the catalog tables them.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Maximum catalog traceability and smallest per-tool payloads, but the two reads have identical exposure conditions ('a policy exists'), identical auth, and read the same Policy aggregate — splitting them invites torn reads (status from one call, documents from another, different snapshots) and doubles the name surface that prompts and packs can drift against (the codebase already grew one phantom alias, get_policy_details).
- **✅ Recommended — One read + one commit: get_policy_info and request_cancellation**: get_policy_info returns a single consistent snapshot: status, allianz policy number, effective dates, payment schedule summary, freeLookEndsAt, and the document list with download links. request_cancellation remains the only commit, with the consequence chain requires_confirmation → terminal (in window) / rejected or referred (outside). Replaces both catalog reads; the catalog is explicitly a conceptual target, and the engine's available_actions still distinguishes the read from the commit.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Slightly larger read payload, but one atomic snapshot (no cross-call inconsistency), one name for prompts/packs/UI to reference, and a clean R/C split that mirrors how the dashboard GUI would consume the same operation — the swap test holds trivially. If document payloads ever grow heavy, splitting later is a non-breaking addition; merging two shipped tools is not.
- **Adopt the packs' name: get_policy_details + request_cancellation**: Same shape as option B but named get_policy_details so seed-skill-packs.ts allowedTools become retroactively correct without edits.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Avoids touching four seed rows, but lets dead config dictate the public contract — the packs are dormant anyway (orchestrator.ts:597 never activates any pack), the renewal pack also references phantom get_quote so the seeds need editing regardless, and 'details' signals less than 'info' about including documents/schedule. Naming should follow the design, not the artifact.

**Rationale:** Status and documents are two views of one aggregate with one exposure condition; a single read gives the agent (and any GUI) an atomic, consistent snapshot and halves the surface where names can drift — drift this codebase has already demonstrated with get_policy_details. The commit stays separate because it carries consequences and confirmation semantics. Cleanup is part of this decision: rewrite seed-skill-packs.ts allowedTools (get_policy_details → get_policy_info in all four POST_SALE packs; phantom get_quote → get_quote_details in post-sale-renewal), and treat pack activation wiring (orchestrator recommendedSlugs is hardcoded empty) as a blocking dependency — otherwise the new tools exist but are never exposed to the LLM.

**Depends on / interacts with:** tool-mapping, phase-model, legality-engine, testing-bdd

#### T9.D6 — From what state does the @policy phase derive — given that accept_quote marks the Conversation COMPLETED and deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts) has no post-sale phase?

- **Conversation-scoped: extend deriveState's existing chain**: Add a POLICY phase after CLOSING, derived from the conversation's application→quote→policy chain within the same conversation; stop closing the conversation at accept_quote.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Smallest conceptual change, but post-sale is customer-scoped by nature: a policyholder returning months later (magic link, new device) starts a NEW conversation with no application chain, and the derivation finds nothing — exactly the class of divergence the CustomerProfile SSOT direction exists to kill. Also overloads one conversation record with both the sale and the service relationship.
- **✅ Recommended — Customer-scoped: POLICY phase derived from the customer's policies**: deriveState (or its successor in the legality engine) checks the identified customer's policies independently of the current conversation: any non-terminal policy ⇒ post-sale state is available, and the engine exposes get_policy_info/request_cancellation whenever 'customer identified AND a policy exists' — matching the catalog's exposure condition verbatim. The sale conversation can still close; a fresh conversation for a returning policyholder derives POLICY immediately. Phase precedence when a policyholder shops for a second product is owned by the phase-model topic.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Requires the phase derivation to read customer-scoped state (a deliberate step toward the SSOT direction) and a precedence rule for mixed contexts, but makes post-sale reachable from any conversation, matches the catalog's 'a policy exists' condition exactly, and survives the conversation lifecycle instead of fighting it.
- **No conversational post-sale: dashboard only**: Policy status/documents/cancellation live exclusively in the customer dashboard UI; the chat never enters a policy phase.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Avoids phase-model work, but contradicts the Gherkin @policy feature outright, strands the four seeded POST_SALE packs permanently, and pushes free-look cancellation — a legally deadline-bound right — behind a UI the customer may never open. The engine-centric architecture explicitly wants both clients (chat and GUI) calling the same operations; removing one client is not a simplification of the engine.

**Rationale:** The catalog's exposure condition for every @policy tool is 'a policy exists' — a fact about the customer, not about any conversation. Conversation-scoped derivation provably fails the primary post-sale scenario (returning policyholder, new conversation), and the project has already committed strategically to customer-scoped truth (CustomerProfile SSOT). This also resolves the COMPLETED-conversation contradiction without un-closing sale conversations: the sale ends, the customer relationship continues, and identity (magic link) is the gate — which is why this decision leans on the identity topic.

**Depends on / interacts with:** phase-model, identity, legality-engine, tool-mapping

### Risks

- SUBMITTED double-write is live today: lib/payments/post-payment.ts auto-sets SUBMITTED on payment while the SOP/admin treat it as 'emailed to Allianz' — any status-machine or get_policy_info work built before fixing this will surface false 'submitted to insurer' claims to customers, and historical rows are ambiguous (a data backfill question, not just a code fix).
- Free-look window length and anchor are legal parameters, not engineering choices: RO distance-sold life insurance is 30 calendar days (OG 85/2004 / Directive 2002/65/EC) but face-to-face life is 20 days (Solvency II art. 186 transposition), and the anchor ('informed that the contract is concluded') may legally precede system activation. Shipping a deterministic engine with the wrong constant converts a compliance gap into a confidently-enforced compliance violation — requires legal sign-off before the rule is frozen.
- No reliable activation timestamp exists: issuedAt is written at accept_quote and overwritten at admin activation, and effectiveFrom is never written. Any free-look or expiry logic anchored to current fields is wrong by construction; an explicit activatedAt must land with the status-machine change.
- suitabilityReportPath points at ephemeral ./tmp/reports by default — existing report files may already be unrecoverable in deployed environments; the Document-table migration must tolerate dangling paths and decide whether regeneration of a compliance snapshot is permissible (it changes the artifact's hash and date).
- LAPSED is structurally blocked on the payments topic: Payment is single-transaction with no schedule or failure events. Adding the enum value before the detection job has inputs creates a second dead status (REFUNDED already demonstrates the pattern of enum values nothing writes).
- Refund execution is undefined: request_cancellation's terminal consequence requires a refund primitive (provider API, partial vs full, who triggers) that does not exist; until the payments topic delivers it, in-window cancellation can only mark state, not move money — a worse customer outcome than not offering the tool.
- Skill-pack activation is globally disabled (orchestrator.ts:597 recommendedSlugs=[]): new policy tools added to POST_SALE packs will silently never reach the LLM; the exposure path (engine-computed available_actions or pack re-wiring) must ship in the same change or the @policy phase is dead on arrival.
- Admin status route accepts any→any transitions and activation without an Allianz policy number; once the agent reads policy state, every historical or future bad admin write becomes customer-visible misinformation. Transition validation must cover the admin route, not just the engine.
- Zero post-payment test coverage: e2e stops at show_payment_success/show_policy_issued, and the Gherkin @policy scenarios (free-look inside/outside window, status/documents) have no executable counterpart — boundary tests on freeLookEndsAt and transition-table negative tests are mandatory before any of this is claimed done.
- Conversation lifecycle conflict: accept_quote sets Conversation COMPLETED, and several subsystems key off conversation status; deriving a customer-scoped POLICY phase must not resurrect completed sale conversations or double-count them in analytics/self-improvement scoring (lib/self-improvement/scorer.ts reads activeSkillPacks per conversation).

---

## T10. Phase model rework: drop CONSENT, add PAYMENT/POLICY, application sub-stages

> Topic key: `phase-model`

### Current state (code-grounded)

TWO phase vocabularies coexist. (1) lib/chat/phase.ts defines a 3-value ConversationPhase ('presentation'|'application'|'post_sale') computed from Conversation.mode + Application.status; consumed by lib/chat/compliance-checker.ts (selects PRESENTATION_RULES vs APPLICATION_RULES) and lib/chat/debug.ts:282 (identity payload); tested in __tests__/lib/chat/phase.test.ts and __tests__/integration/phase-transition.test.ts (which tests ONLY this 3-value model, not the 6-value one). (2) lib/chat/derive-state.ts defines the 6-value Phase (DISCOVERY|SELECTION|CONSENT|QUESTIONNAIRE|QUOTE|CLOSING). determinePhase (derive-state.ts:34-49) is a pure precedence ladder re-computed every turn from DB facts — nothing is stored: ACCEPTED quote → CLOSING; Application.status=COMPLETED → QUOTE; application with missing answers → QUESTIONNAIRE; product set + (!gdpr || !dntSigned) → CONSENT; product set → SELECTION; else DISCOVERY. determineNextBestAction (lines 51-66) returns hardcoded per-phase guidance strings naming concrete tools. dnt.validUntil is loaded (line 110-113) but NEVER checked by determinePhase — an expired DNT still counts as signed. A DRAFT quote's existence is also ignored by determinePhase — after generate_quote succeeds, phase stays QUOTE with nextBestAction 'call generate_quote' (regenerate-loop hazard). CLOSING's nextBestAction says 'proceed to accept_quote' even though CLOSING is only reached AFTER the quote is ACCEPTED (lines 41, 63-64).

Propagation: lib/chat/phase-sections-map.ts — getRequiredSectionsForPhase returns 6 alwaysIncluded section keys + a Record<Phase,string[]> of per-phase extras (CONSENT adds only 'complianceGuidance'; QUESTIONNAIRE adds questionnaireContext+complianceGuidance; QUOTE/CLOSING add productContext/coaching/compliance; no payment or policy sections exist anywhere in prompt-builder.ts's SECTION_REGISTRY at lines 70-89). formatDerivedBriefing (phase-sections-map.ts:34-51) renders 'Phase: X / Next best action: …' plus product/selection/missing questions into the situationalBriefing section ('=== SITUATIONAL ANALYSIS ===', dynamic suffix). lib/chat/orchestrator.ts: deriveState runs as Step 3 (lines 426-450, span label still 'reasoning_gate'); section selection via getRequiredSectionsForPhase(derived.phase) (line 438); error fallback to DISCOVERY sections (line 443); briefing patched at line 592; compliance check triggered when derived.phase is in the UNTYPED string array ['CONSENT','QUESTIONNAIRE','QUOTE','CLOSING'] (line 638) but the checker itself receives the 3-value getConversationPhase (line 651) — trigger and rule-set keyed off different vocabularies. Phase strings persist into TurnTrace.phases JSON (reasoningGate.derivedPhase line 439; promptAssembly.derivedPhase line 1478) and into TurnDebug via the debug:gate event carrying the full DerivedState (lines 440, 586-589; persisted by persistTurnDebug line 1540). The full DerivedState including phase is also MODEL-VISIBLE through the get_current_state tool (lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.ts:14-26) and rendered in the debug drawer via lib/debug/state-rows.ts:22 + components/debug/sections/state-section.tsx (raw string, tolerant of unknown values).

Reachability blocker for PAYMENT/POLICY: accept_quote (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:352-382) sets Quote→ACCEPTED, creates Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION), then sets Conversation.status=COMPLETED; the orchestrator guard (orchestrator.ts:351-353) throws on any turn for a COMPLETED conversation. So CLOSING is unreachable on the next turn and no in-conversation payment phase can exist today. initiate_payment (lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts) exists and requires Policy PENDING_SUBMISSION; Payment rows hang off Policy (prisma/schema.prisma models Policy line 538, Payment line 563); deriveState performs zero Payment/Policy queries. Consent today is two standalone tools record_gdpr_consent / acknowledge_ai_disclosure (lib/tools/registry.ts:1091,1109) plus sign_dnt (line 702) — the catalog folds consent into sign_dnt.
