Tests pinning 6-value phase strings: __tests__/lib/chat/derive-state.test.ts, __tests__/lib/chat/phase-sections-map.test.ts, __tests__/lib/debug/state-rows.test.ts, __tests__/lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.test.ts, __tests__/lib/tools/handlers/set-answer.test.ts, __tests__/integration/navigation.test.ts (lines 80, 100).

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** "QUOTE/CLOSING add productContext/coaching/compliance" (current_state, describing phase-sections-map.ts per-phase extras) — implies CLOSING includes the coachingBriefing section.
  **Correction:** Only QUOTE includes coachingBriefing. CLOSING's phase-specific extras are exactly ['productContext', 'complianceGuidance'] — no coaching section. The compressed phrasing is wrong for CLOSING. _(lib/chat/phase-sections-map.ts:22-23 — QUOTE: ['productContext', 'coachingBriefing', 'complianceGuidance']; CLOSING: ['productContext', 'complianceGuidance']. Also pinned by __tests__/lib/chat/phase-sections-map.test.ts:31-40 (QUOTE test asserts coachingBriefing, CLOSING test does not).)_
- **Claim:** "the grep-verified consumer set is entirely in-repo: ... and seven test files" (decision point 5 rationale).
  **Correction:** Six test files pin the 6-value phase strings, not seven — exactly the six the report itself lists in current_state (__tests__/lib/chat/derive-state.test.ts, __tests__/lib/chat/phase-sections-map.test.ts, __tests__/lib/debug/state-rows.test.ts, __tests__/lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.test.ts, __tests__/lib/tools/handlers/set-answer.test.ts, __tests__/integration/navigation.test.ts). If the two 3-value-model tests retired by the same clean break are included (__tests__/lib/chat/phase.test.ts, __tests__/integration/phase-transition.test.ts) the count is eight. Neither tally is seven. _(Grep for 'DISCOVERY'|'SELECTION'|'CONSENT'|'QUESTIONNAIRE'|'CLOSING' across __tests__ matches exactly 6 files (18 occurrences); a follow-up grep for QUOTE-phase pins (phase: 'QUOTE' / toBe('QUOTE') / getRequiredSectionsForPhase('QUOTE')) surfaces no additional files beyond those 6.)_

### Gaps

- No PAYMENT or POLICY phase exists and none is derivable: deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts) never queries Payment or Policy, and accept_quote (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:375-382) marks the Conversation COMPLETED, which the orchestrator guard (lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:351-353) turns into a hard error on the next turn — every @payment Gherkin scenario (declined-payment retry, abandoned-payment re-engagement, change_payment_option) and every @policy scenario is unimplementable in-conversation today.
- CONSENT exists as a standalone phase (derive-state.ts:46) gated on customer.gdprConsentAt + conversation.dntSignedAt, contradicting the catalog target where consent is captured inside sign_dnt and DNT is the first gate of @application. Its prompt-section payload is only 'complianceGuidance' (phase-sections-map.ts:20).
- No quote-review phase: determinePhase ignores DRAFT quotes, so after generate_quote succeeds the phase remains QUOTE with nextBestAction 'call generate_quote' (derive-state.ts:42, 61-62) — the catalog's @quote phase (review/disclosures/accept) has no derived counterpart, and CLOSING's guidance text is stale (says 'proceed to accept_quote' when the quote is already ACCEPTED).
- No sub-stage concept: the catalog's application(dnt → questionnaire → quote-gen) progression is smeared across CONSENT/QUESTIONNAIRE/QUOTE; DerivedState has no subphase field and formatDerivedBriefing (phase-sections-map.ts:34-51) cannot express where inside the application the customer is (no DNT progress, no quote validity, no payment status).
- dnt.validUntil is derived but never used in phase determination (derive-state.ts:46 checks only dnt.signed) — an expired DNT does not push the conversation back to a DNT renewal stage, violating the catalog's 'DNT valid' gate for the underwriting questionnaire.
- No advance_phase concept: no commit returns a phase transition; the only transition machinery in the tool pipeline is the dead WorkflowSession transition block (orchestrator.ts:1280-1295), which is unrelated to the derived phase.
- Dual phase vocabulary feeding compliance inconsistently: the compliance check is TRIGGERED by the 6-value phase (orchestrator.ts:638, untyped string array) but the checker selects its rule set from the 3-value getConversationPhase (orchestrator.ts:651) — two derivations of 'where are we' that can disagree.
- No payment/policy prompt sections exist: SECTION_REGISTRY (lib/chat/prompt-builder.ts:70-89) has no paymentContext or policyContext key, so even if a PAYMENT phase were derived there is nothing for the sections map to select.
- __tests__/integration/phase-transition.test.ts tests only the legacy 3-value model; there is no integration test for 6-value phase transitions across commits (only two static deriveState snapshots in navigation.test.ts:66-103).

### Decision points

#### T10.D1 — Target phase enumeration: how do DISCOVERY/SELECTION/CONSENT/QUESTIONNAIRE/QUOTE/CLOSING map to discovery_consultancy → application(dnt → questionnaire → quote-gen) → quote → payment → policy, and are dnt/questionnaire/quote-gen sub-stages or flat phases?

- **✅ Recommended — Hierarchical phase + subphase**: Phase = DISCOVERY | APPLICATION | QUOTE | PAYMENT | POLICY. DerivedState gains subphase: 'dnt' | 'questionnaire' | 'quote_gen' | null, populated only when phase=APPLICATION. Mapping: DISCOVERY+SELECTION → DISCOVERY (candidate exploration and tier/level talk are consultancy; the selection is frozen as application data at the set_application commit); CONSENT → APPLICATION/dnt (consent is the sign_dnt outcome); QUESTIONNAIRE → APPLICATION/questionnaire; today's QUOTE (application complete, not yet generated) → APPLICATION/quote_gen; a new derived QUOTE phase = DRAFT quote issued and awaiting disclosures/acceptance; PAYMENT = quote ACCEPTED + policy PENDING_SUBMISSION; POLICY = policy ACTIVE (or first payment COMPLETED). CLOSING is deleted.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches the catalog's two gating dimensions exactly: tool families are exposed per phase (get_dnt_state, resume_application, cancel_application are 'in @application' regardless of sub-stage) while fine gates (DNT validity, questionnaire completeness) select the sub-stage — so legality rules are expressed once per scope instead of repeated across three flat values. The top-level enum can also subsume the legacy 3-value ConversationPhase (compliance rule selection keys off the same Phase), killing the dual vocabulary. Cost: every Record<Phase,…> consumer needs a second lookup level for APPLICATION, and exhaustiveness checking spans two enums.
- **Flat 7-phase enum**: DISCOVERY | APPLICATION_DNT | APPLICATION_QUESTIONNAIRE | APPLICATION_QUOTE_GEN | QUOTE | PAYMENT | POLICY as a single flat union; same semantic mapping as above but encoded in one dimension.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Single-level Record keeps section maps and switch statements one-dimensional and trivially exhaustive. But every @application-scoped rule (tool exposure, compliance triggering, briefing text about the application as a whole) must enumerate three values, and any future sub-stage addition (e.g. disclosures as a quote sub-step) ripples through every consumer — the encoding hides the scope structure the legality engine needs.
- **Keep current 6 values, append PAYMENT/POLICY**: Minimal delta: retain SELECTION and CONSENT, add PAYMENT and POLICY after CLOSING, leave the rest untouched.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Preserves all existing tests and prompt text, but entrenches exactly what the target removes: a standalone CONSENT phase contradicts consent-inside-sign_dnt, SELECTION contradicts candidate-exploration-as-discovery, and the QUOTE/CLOSING ambiguity (no issued-quote-awaiting-acceptance state, stale CLOSING guidance) is left unfixed. Fails the catalog on correctness, not just naming.

**Rationale:** The catalog is explicitly hierarchical — '@application' is one scope with an internal dnt → questionnaire → quote-gen progression, and several tools are exposed at the phase scope across all sub-stages. A hierarchical DerivedState lets the legality engine, the sections map, and the compliance checker each key at the altitude they actually operate at, and it lets the top-level Phase replace lib/chat/phase.ts's 3-value model (presentation≈DISCOVERY, application≈APPLICATION, post_sale≈POLICY) so one derivation feeds everything. Dropping SELECTION is correct on the catalog's own terms: candidate exploration is consultancy ('talk is free'), and tier/level/addon are application attributes frozen at the set_application commit, not a conversation phase. Dropping CONSENT is correct because consent is an outcome of the sign_dnt commit inside APPLICATION/dnt — the phase model should reflect what gate is open, not which consent rows exist.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, dnt-sessions, application-lifecycle, tool-mapping, quote-lifecycle

#### T10.D2 — Derived vs stored phase: keep per-turn derivation as the source of truth with advance_phase as a computed result, or store the phase and have commits transition it?

- **✅ Recommended — Derivation is truth; advance_phase is the pre/post-commit delta**: Keep deriveState as the only authority. The commit envelope derives the phase before and after applying a commit (inside the same transaction); if the values differ, the commit's returned consequence includes advance_phase {from, to}, and that consequence is persisted with the commit record. No phase column anywhere.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Crash-consistent by construction: there is no second write that can be lost between 'apply commit' and 'update phase', so a crash or double-submit can never strand the machine in a phase that contradicts the data (idempotent re-derivation always converges). Time-driven transitions (quote validUntil passing, dnt validUntil expiring) are handled naturally at read time — a stored machine would need cron jobs or lazy-repair writes for these, which is where stored state machines historically rot. Preserves the swap test exactly: a GUI calling the same commit observes the same derived state because there is no agent-private or pipeline-private phase. Cost: deriveState must stay cheap (it already runs every turn) and every commit handler pays two derivations; phase history is not a first-class table but must be reconstructed from persisted consequences.
- **Stored phase column transitioned by commits**: Add phase (and subphase) columns to Conversation or Application; each commit's handler writes the new phase; deriveState reads the column instead of deriving.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches the catalog's state-machine prose most literally and makes phase history queryable for free. But it creates a dual-write integrity problem (commit data and phase column can diverge on partial failure — the exact class of bug the dead WorkflowSession model already demonstrated in this codebase), requires explicit repair for time-driven transitions (expired quote/DNT leave the stored phase wrong until something notices), and breaks the swap test unless every client mutation path remembers to transition the column. The catalog's own invariant — 'never advances a phase by narration; only a commit's advance_phase does' — is about who may CAUSE transitions, not about storage; derivation satisfies it because only commits change the underlying facts.
- **Derivation + append-only phase-transition event log**: Derivation remains authoritative; additionally, whenever a commit's pre/post derivation differs, append a PhaseTransition row (from, to, commitId, timestamp) purely for audit/analytics.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Gives compliance-grade audit ('when did this customer enter payment?') without a second source of truth — the log is derived output, never read back for decisions. But it is redundant with persisting the commit consequence itself (the commit-envelope topic's commit log already carries advance_phase per option 1), and TurnTrace/TurnDebug already snapshot derivedPhase per turn; a third record of the same fact invites drift in what analytics trusts.

**Rationale:** The two catalog framings reconcile cleanly once advance_phase is read as a REPORT, not a mechanism: phases only ever change because a commit changed the facts (or time passed a validUntil), so deriving before/after each commit yields exactly the advance_phase consequence the catalog specifies, while keeping the properties that matter — crash consistency (no dual write), idempotency (re-derive after double-submit converges), correct time-driven transitions (expiry is a read-time predicate, impossible to model correctly with stored transitions alone), and the swap test (no client-invisible state). Audit needs are met by persisting the consequence on the commit record (commit-envelope topic) rather than a parallel phase store. This is also continuous with what shipped in Plan B — derivation already proved itself against the WorkflowSession stored-machine failure mode recorded in the advance-flow deadlock history.

**Depends on / interacts with:** commit-envelope, legality-engine, quote-lifecycle, dnt-sessions

#### T10.D3 — PAYMENT/POLICY derivation predicates and conversation terminality: what makes those phases derivable, given accept_quote currently sets Conversation.status=COMPLETED and the orchestrator rejects turns on COMPLETED conversations?

- **✅ Recommended — Conversation stays ACTIVE through payment; terminality decouples from phase**: Remove the Conversation.status=COMPLETED write from accept_quote (quote-handlers.ts:375-382). Derivation: PAYMENT when an ACCEPTED quote has a Policy in PENDING_SUBMISSION and no COMPLETED payment; POLICY when the policy is ACTIVE (issue_policy fired as a system effect of the first successful payment, per catalog) or any later policy status. Conversation completion becomes an independent lifecycle event (explicit close or idle timeout), not a phase side effect.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Makes every @payment scenario possible (failed-payment retry, abandoned-payment re-engagement after days, change_payment_option before capture) and gives POLICY a real in-conversation existence for post-sale servicing. Phase and conversation lifecycle become orthogonal concerns, which is correct: a phase describes the FUNNEL position of the customer's purchase, a conversation status describes a chat session. Requires deciding what get_open_items-style resumption looks like across conversations (identity topic), since the funnel state is application/policy-scoped while deriveState is currently conversation-scoped.
- **Keep closing the conversation at accept_quote; payment is out-of-conversation**: Payment happens in the Stripe handoff UI only; a returning customer starts a NEW conversation where deriveState detects the pending payment via customer-scoped queries and enters PAYMENT directly.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Honors 'Stripe owns card entry' maximally and keeps the sale conversation immutable as a record. But it contradicts the catalog's @payment phase being part of THE state machine (Zeno monitors and re-engages within the flow), makes the common same-session path (accept → pay now) impossible without an artificial conversation break, and forces deriveState to become customer-scoped before the identity/customer-SSOT work lands — sequencing the hardest dependency first for no correctness gain.
- **Phase derivation goes customer/policy-scoped now**: Rework deriveState to derive from the customer's open items (applications, quotes, policies, payments) rather than the conversation, so PAYMENT/POLICY are derivable in any conversation the identified customer opens.
  _Tradeoffs:_ This is the strategically correct end-state (aligned with the CustomerProfile SSOT direction and the catalog's returning-user scenarios) and eliminates the conversation-scoping of funnel state entirely. But it presupposes identify_customer and customer-scoped DNT/application resolution that do not exist yet, and it must answer 'which open item is in focus' when a customer has several — a question owned by the identity and application-lifecycle topics. As the phase-model decision it overreaches; as the direction the predicates should be written toward (behind a focus-resolution seam), it is right.

**Rationale:** PAYMENT and POLICY phases are dead values unless the conversation survives accept_quote — the current COMPLETED write plus the orchestrator guard makes the catalog's entire @payment feature unreachable, which is a correctness contradiction with the target, not a style choice. Decoupling phase from conversation terminality fixes it with correct semantics: the funnel position is a property of the purchase (application → quote → policy chain), and the chat session's lifecycle is a transport concern. The predicates should be written against the policy/payment chain (Conversation → Application → Quote → Policy → Payments, all already related in prisma/schema.prisma) so that when the identity/customer-SSOT work later re-scopes 'the chain in focus' from conversation to customer, only the chain-resolution seam changes, not the phase logic.

**Depends on / interacts with:** payments, policy-post-sale, application-lifecycle, identity, quote-lifecycle

#### T10.D4 — Sections map rework: what does each target phase (and APPLICATION sub-stage) inject, where does CONSENT's complianceGuidance eligibility move, and how does situationalBriefing become sub-stage aware?

- **✅ Recommended — Per-(phase, subphase) map + new payment/policy sections + state-fact briefing**: getRequiredSectionsForPhase(phase, subphase): DISCOVERY keeps capabilityManifest/customerContext/customerMemory/agentKnowledge + absorbs SELECTION's productContext+coachingBriefing (product talk is consultancy); APPLICATION/dnt → complianceGuidance + a new dntContext section (DNT validity, session progress, consent status — the heir of CONSENT's payload); APPLICATION/questionnaire → questionnaireContext + complianceGuidance; APPLICATION/quote_gen → productContext + complianceGuidance; QUOTE → productContext + complianceGuidance + disclosures state (acknowledged or not); PAYMENT → new paymentContext section (schedule, status, failure reason, recovery action — no coachingBriefing: the sale is closed, selling guidance is wrong here); POLICY → new policyContext section (policy status, documents, free-look window). formatDerivedBriefing renders phase + subphase plus per-stage facts (DNT remaining, questionnaire missing, quote validUntil, payment status) and drops free-text nextBestAction in favor of the engine's available/blocked actions once the legality engine lands.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Keeps section selection deterministic and testable (pure function of DerivedState), gives PAYMENT/POLICY real prompt support instead of inheriting sales-phase sections, and moves consent guidance to where the catalog says the consent decision lives (the DNT gate). Requires two new SECTION_REGISTRY entries plus loaders, and the compliance checker's eligibility set must be re-stated in target vocabulary (today's untyped list at orchestrator.ts:638 silently breaks on rename).
- **Flat per-phase map only, sub-stage expressed solely in the briefing text**: Keep getRequiredSectionsForPhase keyed by top-level phase only; all APPLICATION sub-stages share one section set (questionnaireContext + complianceGuidance + dntContext always); formatDerivedBriefing alone differentiates dnt/questionnaire/quote_gen.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simpler map and fewer test permutations, and section over-inclusion is mostly a token-cost issue rather than a correctness issue. But it injects questionnaire framing during the DNT gate and DNT framing during quote-gen — precisely the kind of mixed signal that produced the historical stall/loop pathologies; section selection exists to keep the model's working set phase-appropriate, and flattening it gives that up where the funnel is most delicate.
- **Engine-injected actions manifest replaces most per-phase sections**: Once the legality engine computes available_actions/blocked_actions per turn, render them as a single dynamic actionsManifest section; per-phase guidance shrinks to compliance + domain context, and section selection becomes near-static.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Closest to the catalog's 'available_actions are injected every turn' invariant, and eliminates the drift risk between the sections map and the engine's actual legality. But actions alone do not carry domain knowledge (product facts, questionnaire context, payment schedules) — the model still needs phase-scoped CONTEXT sections, so this replaces nextBestAction and workflowInstructions, not the map itself. Best treated as the evolution of the briefing within option 1, not an alternative to it.

**Rationale:** Section selection is the mechanism by which the derived phase actually changes agent behavior, and the target phases have genuinely different information needs: the DNT gate needs consent/needs-analysis framing (CONSENT's complianceGuidance moves to APPLICATION/dnt where the sign_dnt decision is made), payment recovery needs schedule/failure facts and must NOT receive sales coaching, and post-sale servicing needs policy/document context. A (phase, subphase)-keyed pure function preserves the determinism and unit-testability that replaced the reasoning gate, while the briefing evolves from hardcoded nextBestAction prose toward rendering the legality engine's computed actions — the map provides context, the engine provides legal moves, and neither duplicates the other.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, tool-mapping, payments, policy-post-sale, dnt-sessions, questionnaire-consequences

#### T10.D5 — Backward compatibility of phase names: how to migrate TurnTrace/TurnDebug records, debug UI, the model-visible get_current_state contract, and the test suite off the old 6-value strings?

- **✅ Recommended — Clean break: rename everywhere, no aliases, tolerant readers for history**: Replace the Phase union in one change; update phase-sections-map, the orchestrator's compliance-trigger list and DISCOVERY fallback literal, state-handlers, state-rows, and all pinned tests; retire lib/chat/phase.ts's 3-value ConversationPhase in the same move by keying the compliance checker off the new top-level Phase. Historical TurnTrace.phases / TurnDebug records keep old strings; readers (state-rows.ts already prints raw strings; the debug drawer replay) must merely tolerate unknown values.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One vocabulary, zero translation layers, and the dual-phase-model inconsistency (trigger vs rule-set, orchestrator.ts:638 vs 651) dies with it. Verified safe because the strings are not a persisted contract: no DB column stores the 6-value phase, no external API exposes it, and the debug UI renders untyped strings. Costs: historical debug replays show retired names (cosmetic), and the rename must consciously sweep the two NON-type-checked sites — the untyped string-array membership check at orchestrator.ts:638 (compiles fine with stale values, silently disabling compliance) and any prompt/seed prose mentioning phase names (checked: prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts line 46's 'DISCOVERY' is Romanian sales prose, not the enum).
- **Alias layer: keep old values, add target vocabulary alongside**: DerivedState retains phase (legacy 6-value) and adds targetPhase/subphase; consumers migrate gradually; a mapping function translates for analytics continuity.
  _Tradeoffs:_ TurnTrace dashboards see continuous series and tests migrate incrementally, but the codebase carries THREE phase vocabularies during the transition (3-value, legacy 6-value, target), the compliance trigger and sections map must pick one and drift from the other, and the model sees two phase fields in get_current_state — ambiguity injected exactly where determinism was the point. Transitional duplication of a source-of-truth concept is the failure mode this whole transformation exists to remove.
- **Versioned DerivedState snapshot**: Stamp DerivedState (and the persisted debug:gate payload) with a phaseModelVersion; readers branch on version to render/interpret old records faithfully.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Maximal fidelity for historical TurnDebug replay and future-proofs further phase reworks. But it buys fidelity only for a debug surface that already renders unknown strings harmlessly, at the price of permanent version-branching in every reader — versioning is warranted for durable external contracts, and this is an internal, display-only one.

**Rationale:** The grep-verified consumer set is entirely in-repo: lib/chat/{derive-state, phase-sections-map, orchestrator}.ts, lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.ts, lib/debug/state-rows.ts, components/debug/sections/state-section.tsx, and seven test files — plus freeform JSON in TurnTrace/TurnDebug that nothing parses back into the enum. With no durable contract, aliasing or versioning adds permanent complexity to protect transient cosmetics. The single-vocabulary outcome also fixes a live inconsistency (compliance trigger keyed by 6-value, rule selection by 3-value) rather than preserving it. The change must include rewriting __tests__/integration/phase-transition.test.ts against the new derivation (it currently tests only the legacy 3-value model) and adding commit-driven transition tests (start_application → APPLICATION/dnt, sign_dnt → /questionnaire, last answer → /quote_gen, generate_quote → QUOTE, accept_quote → PAYMENT, payment success → POLICY).

**Depends on / interacts with:** testing-bdd, tool-mapping, commit-envelope

### Risks

- Unreachable-phase dead code: if the accept_quote Conversation.status=COMPLETED write (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:375-382) and the orchestrator COMPLETED guard (lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:351-353) are not changed in the same effort as the phase enumeration, PAYMENT and POLICY ship as derivable-in-theory but unreachable-in-practice values, and every @payment/@policy Gherkin scenario silently has no runtime path.
- Silent compliance-check disablement on rename: the trigger at orchestrator.ts:638 is an untyped string-array .includes(derived.phase) — renaming Phase values compiles cleanly while the check stops firing for every renamed phase. It must become an exhaustive typed predicate (e.g. Record<Phase, boolean> or a switch) as part of the rework.
- Compliance behavior shift when unifying the dual vocabulary: today rule-set selection uses the 3-value getConversationPhase (orchestrator.ts:651) whose 'presentation' deliberately narrows the rules (compliance-checker.ts PRESENTATION_RULES) to stop premature flagging — a past pathology fix. Re-keying off the new Phase must map DISCOVERY → the narrow rule set explicitly or the over-flagging pathology returns.
- Prompt-behavior regressions invisible to unit tests: formatDerivedBriefing text and per-phase section sets directly steer the model; the advance-flow history shows unit-green pipelines still stalling live. Any enumeration/sections change needs the scripted conversation sim re-run (the verified pattern from Plan B: runtime-verified 6/6) covering the full funnel including the new accept → pay → policy tail.
- Model-visible contract change: get_current_state (lib/tools/handlers/state-handlers.ts) returns the raw DerivedState to the LLM; renamed/added fields (subphase) change what the model reasons over, and stale phase names may linger in agent prompts or skill-pack guidance text — sweep Agent.systemPrompt rows and seeds, not just TypeScript.
- Regenerate-loop persists if the QUOTE predicate is wrong: the new QUOTE phase must key on the existence of a non-expired DRAFT quote, not merely Application.status=COMPLETED, or the current 'phase says call generate_quote after the quote already exists' loop (derive-state.ts:42,61-62 ignoring draftQuote) survives the rework under a new name.
- DNT predicate churn: APPLICATION/dnt sub-stage predicates written directly against Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil will be invalidated by the dnt-sessions rework (session entities, product-type coverage, new/update sessions). The phase derivation should consume a single dntValidFor(productType) seam so the storage change does not re-open the phase model.
- Sub-stage exhaustiveness drift: with a (phase, subphase) hierarchy, TypeScript's Record exhaustiveness protects the phase dimension but subphase-conditional logic (sections, briefing, compliance) can silently miss a sub-stage; tests should iterate the full phase×subphase matrix the way phase-sections-map.test.ts:42 iterates phases today.
- Historical debug replay shows retired phase names: TurnDebug rows persisted before the rename carry old strings into the debug drawer's replay; rendering is tolerant (state-rows prints raw values) but any future test pinning replayed row values against the new enum will flake on old fixtures.

---

## T11. Product data model: key_value_product_points, sell_specific_info, pricing_examples, eligibility_bounds, addon info

> Topic key: `product-data`

### Current state (code-grounded)

PRODUCT MODEL (prisma/schema.prisma:104-141): Product has code, name/description (localized Json en/ro), insuranceType, subType, eligibility (free-form Json), features String[] (EN-only), exclusions String[], defaultPlaybook @db.Text, pricingExplanation @db.Text, targetCustomer, targetAgeRange (marketing string '25-45', distinct from eligibility 18-64), premiumRange Json ({min:190,max:430,RON,annual} — base product only), paymentFrequencyOptions Json, insightKeys Json, quoteValidityDays. None of the catalog's target fields exist: no key_value_product_points, no sell_specific_info, no pricing_examples, no eligibility_bounds, no sell_specific_addon_info.

PRICING STRUCTURE (schema.prisma:143-244; seeded in prisma/seeds/seed-product.ts:798-1025): PricingTier (standard/optim) -> PricingLevel (level_1..3; premiumAnnual 190/290/390 and 230/330/430 RON) -> CoverageAmount (54 age-banded DEATH_ANY_CAUSE rows across 9 bands 18-64 + 18 fixed rows) referencing a 7-entry CoverageType legend. One Addon 'TREATMENT_ABROAD_BD' with 4 AddonPricingRule age bands (18-30:200, 31-45:350, 46-55:500, 56-64:700 RON/yr) and 3 fixed EUR coverages (2,000,000 treatment / 100/day hospitalization / 50,000 medication). The quote engine (lib/engines/quote-engine.ts:77-101) is a pure function: premiumAnnual = level.premiumAnnual + (addonRule?.premiumAnnual ?? 0); monthly/semi/quarterly are simple rounded divisions. This is the exact arithmetic any pricing_examples must reproduce.

get_product_info TODAY (lib/tools/registry.ts:294-374, registered :429-461): loads the full pricing tree, resolves customer age best-effort (Customer.dateOfBirth -> extractedProfile.age, registry.ts:349-363), and calls shapeProductInfo (lib/tools/shape-product-info.ts). The shaper deliberately REMOVES PricingLevel.premiumAnnual and Addon.pricingRules (Plan A 'no pre-quote premium leak'; verified by __tests__/lib/tools/shape-product-info.test.ts:120-136 and __tests__/lib/tools/handlers/product-handlers.test.ts:33-46) and trims age-banded coverages to the matching band when age is known. BUT it passes pricingExplanation, premiumRange, features, exclusions, and the raw eligibility Json through verbatim — and pricingExplanation prose hardcodes all six level premiums ('Standard I=190, II=290, III=390 RON. Optim I=230, II=330, III=430 RON', seed-product.ts:446-447), so structured premiums are withheld while the same numbers leak as prose. The tool is intentionally uncacheable because output is shaped per customer age (registry.ts:457-460).

ADDON SURFACE: no get_product_addon_info tool exists (full registerTool inventory at registry.ts:407-1109 — 33 tools, none addon-scoped). Addon details ride inside get_product_info.addons[] (premium-free) and inside the productContext prompt section (lib/chat/context-loaders.ts:281-295: coverage amounts + waiting period, no premiums). Conversation tracks candidateProductId/candidateConfidence/candidateSetAt (schema.prisma:304-306) but there is NO candidate-addon pointer, and the set_candidate_product handler (lib/tools/handlers/candidate-handlers.ts) contains zero addon handling.

DISCOVERY PROMPT USAGE: catalogOverview (context-loaders.ts:326-371, cached 10min, always present) is one line per product (type + name + short description) for breadth grounding — specifics deferred to get_product_info. productContext (context-loaders.ts:209-299) shows features, addon coverages, and ONLY the product-level premiumRange ('never per-level numbers', :262), with 15 lines of defensive parsing for premiumRange's possible shapes (:266-275). coachingBriefing falls back to Product.defaultPlaybook (context-loaders.ts:390-415) — a ~270-line Romanian playbook (seed-product.ts:172-445) full of HARDCODED prices ('53 lei pe luna', 'Standard Nivelul I (190 RON/an = 16 lei/luna)', '0,52 RON pe zi'). The discovery skill pack additionally forbids mentioning prices in the first turns (prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts:35,107).

ELIGIBILITY TODAY: Product.eligibility is an opaque Json blob ({minAge:18, maxAge:64, residency, healthRequirements, notes}, seed-product.ts:146-152) that NO code ever evaluates — it is only echoed by shapeProductInfo. generate_quote (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:19-128) performs no age-eligibility check at all and fabricates age 30 when dateOfBirth is missing (:63), using age only to pick coverage bands/addon rules. The only deterministic eligibility check in the codebase is check_bd_eligibility for the BD medical questionnaire (lib/tools/handlers/bd-handlers.ts:16-110). deriveState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts) computes phase + nextBestAction but carries no eligibility concept.

GOVERNANCE TODAY: there is no admin UI for products (app/admin/(protected)/ has agents, skill-packs, conversations, applications, policies, users, proposals, ab-tests, self-improvement — no products page) and no versioning of product content (only Workflow has a version int, schema.prisma:373). A Proposal review pattern (ProposalStatus PENDING/APPROVED/REJECTED, schema.prisma:94-98, plus admin proposals UI) exists for self-improvement content.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** "full registerTool inventory at registry.ts:407-1109 — 33 tools, none addon-scoped"
  **Correction:** The tool count (33) and the absence of get_product_addon_info are both correct (verified: no addon-info read tool exists anywhere). But "none addon-scoped" is overstated: check_bd_eligibility IS an addon-scoped tool — it is registered at registry.ts:922-936 ("Check medical questionnaire eligibility for BD ... products") and its handler flips the addon off the application (sets Application.includesAddon=false on a positive medical answer). The report itself cites this tool elsewhere, so the intended meaning is clearly "no addon-INFO tool", but as written the parenthetical is false. _(lib/tools/registry.ts:922-936; lib/tools/handlers/bd-handlers.ts:58-65)_
- **Claim:** "with 15 lines of defensive parsing for premiumRange's possible shapes (:266-275)"
  **Correction:** The defensive premiumRange parsing block in loadProductContext is 10-12 lines, not 15: the shape-handling chain runs from `const pr = product.premiumRange as unknown` at line 266 through the string/localized-object/min-max branches to the `if (range) ... else ...` fallback at lines 276-277. The cited line range :266-275 is itself accurate; the "15 lines" count is not. _(lib/chat/context-loaders.ts:266-277)_
- **Claim:** "generate_quote (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:19-128) performs no age-eligibility check at all"
  **Correction:** The behavioral claims are fully verified (no age-eligibility check anywhere in the handler; `let customerAge = 30 // fallback` is exactly at line 63; age is used only to filter coverage age bands at :84-93 and select the addon pricing rule at :122-124). However the cited range :19-128 under-covers the function: the generateQuote handler actually spans lines 19-255 (payment-frequency detection, calculateQuote call, Quote row creation, and the success return all fall in :140-255). I confirmed the omitted portion also contains no eligibility check, so the substantive claim stands; only the line-range citation is wrong. _(lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:19-255 (handler closes at :255; quote creation at :189-214))_

### Gaps

- All five catalog target fields are missing: key_value_product_points, sell_specific_info, pricing_examples, eligibility_bounds, sell_specific_addon_info — nothing in schema, handlers, or seeds provides them.
- Price truth is triplicated across unguaranteed sources: PricingLevel/AddonPricingRule rows (engine truth), pricingExplanation prose (hardcodes all six premiums), and defaultPlaybook sales scripts ('53 lei pe luna', '16 lei/luna'). Repricing the DB rows would silently strand the prose copies; get_product_info simultaneously withholds structured premiums and leaks them via pricingExplanation.
- The Gherkin invariant 'example prices are quoted only from pricing_examples' is currently unsatisfiable: the agent's only legitimate pre-quote price surface is premiumRange (base product only, excludes up to +700 RON addon premium), while the playbook feeds it hardcoded per-package prices.
- Product.eligibility is never evaluated by any code; there is no deterministic eligibility check anywhere in the funnel — generate_quote quotes ineligible ages without complaint (fallback age 30, quote-handlers.ts:63), so even the FINAL gate is missing, let alone the early discovery-phase signal.
- features[] is EN-only in a bilingual (ro-first) agent — the agent must paraphrase/translate claims on the fly, which for compliance-reviewed selling points means inventing wording.
- No content governance: no product admin UI, no versioning, no audit trail linking a conversation to the marketing claims that were in force when it happened.
- No candidate-addon concept: Conversation has no addon-in-focus pointer and set_candidate_product ignores addons, so the catalog's 'candidate addon in focus' exposure rule has no state to key on.
- Age resolution is duplicated with divergent fallbacks (get_product_info: DOB -> extractedProfile.age -> undefined; generate_quote: DOB -> hardcoded 30) — the CustomerProfile SSOT (specced, not implemented) is the strategic fix; until then derived pricing examples and quotes can disagree about the same customer.

### Decision points

#### T11.D1 — How are pricing_examples and eligibility_bounds stored: authored JSON on Product, derived at read time, or hybrid (derive numeric, author narrative)?

- **Authored JSON fields**: Add pricingExamples Json and eligibilityBounds Json columns to Product (and Addon), hand-authored in seeds/admin, returned verbatim by get_product_info.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Simplest read path and full editorial control over which examples to showcase, but creates a THIRD copy of pricing truth that can diverge from PricingLevel/AddonPricingRule — exactly the failure mode pricingExplanation already exhibits today. The agent could quote a price the quote engine would never produce, violating the catalog's core invariant; consistency is enforceable only by convention/tests, not by construction.
- **Fully derived at read time**: get_product_info computes pricing_examples by invoking calculateQuote (lib/engines/quote-engine.ts — pure, no DB) over a representative parameter grid (e.g. ages 25/35/45/55 x tiers x levels I/III x with/without BD), and eligibility_bounds by projecting structured eligibility data. No stored example prices anywhere.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Example prices are guaranteed identical to engine output by construction (same pure function, same rows); repricing the DB instantly updates examples. But narrative fields (key points, sell info) cannot be derived, and the example-selection grid becomes presentation logic baked into code; purely numeric output loses the authored framing the playbook relies on.
- **✅ Recommended — Hybrid: derive numbers, author narrative**: pricing_examples derived via calculateQuote over a small per-product declared parameter grid (the grid itself is data: which parameter varies — age for protect — and which sample points to show); eligibility_bounds derived from eligibility promoted to structured, schema-validated fields (minAge/maxAge Int + structured residency/health entries). key_value_product_points, sell_specific_info, sell_specific_addon_info are authored, localized (en/ro) content with NO numerals permitted (lint/validation rule), referencing derived figures by placeholder if needed.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Single source of numeric truth (the engine) plus compliance-reviewed prose where prose belongs; the no-numbers rule on authored fields is what makes the guarantee total — otherwise prose re-smuggles prices as pricingExplanation does today. Requires purging hardcoded prices from pricingExplanation/defaultPlaybook and declaring the variation parameter per product instead of hardcoding 'age' (future products may price on other inputs).

**Rationale:** The only design under which the agent can NEVER state a price the pricing engine would not produce is one where every example price is emitted by the same pure function the quote path uses — calculateQuote already exists, is DB-free, and get_product_info already loads the full pricing tree and resolves age, so the derivation slots into the existing read without new state. Authored numbers (option 1) structurally re-create today's divergence (pricingExplanation hardcoding premiums that rot on repricing); full derivation (option 2) cannot produce selling narrative at all. The hybrid also fixes eligibility_bounds correctly: bounds become typed columns the engine can evaluate (DP4) rather than an opaque blob only the LLM could interpret.

**Depends on / interacts with:** quote-lifecycle, legality-engine, tool-mapping, testing-bdd

#### T11.D2 — How are the compliance-sensitive marketing fields (key_value_product_points, sell_specific_info, sell_specific_addon_info) governed — plain columns, versioned content table, or columns plus revision log?

- **Plain localized Json columns**: Add the fields as Json columns on Product/Addon (same pattern as name/description), maintained through seeds and migrations; git history is the only audit trail.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Matches every existing content field and keeps the read path trivial, but provides no runtime-visible history: you cannot prove which claims were live during a given conversation, there is no draft/review state, and a bad claim can only be retracted by redeploy. For regulated insurance-distribution marketing content this leaves the compliance question ('what did we tell this customer and under whose approval?') unanswerable.
- **✅ Recommended — Versioned ProductContent table with publish workflow**: A ProductContent model (productId, addonId?, field, locale, content, version, status DRAFT/PUBLISHED/RETIRED, authoredBy, approvedBy, publishedAt); get_product_info and prompt loaders read only the latest PUBLISHED version; edits go through the existing Proposal-style review pattern (ProposalStatus + admin proposals UI already establish it).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Full audit trail and draft/approve/retract lifecycle for exactly the content the Gherkin pins as the agent's only permitted selling claims; paired with the always-on TurnDebug persistence it closes the loop 'utterance X cited published claim-set version Y'. Costs are architectural, not effort: an extra resolution step in reads, cache invalidation on publish, and the risk of over-modelling if applied beyond the marketing fields (operational fields like quoteValidityDays should NOT move into it).
- **Columns plus append-only revision log**: Content lives as Json columns for reads; every write appends a ProductContentRevision snapshot row (no draft state — publish equals write).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Keeps reads simple and gives history, but no review gate: a claim is live the instant anyone writes it, which inverts the desired control for regulated content (audit without approval). Also two write paths to keep honest (column update + log append) instead of one.

**Rationale:** These fields are not decoration — the spec makes them the exclusive source of every selling point the agent may utter, which makes them a regulated boundary equivalent in kind to DTO validation: the system, not convention, should guarantee only approved claims reach the prompt/tool surface. Versioning with a publish gate is the only option where 'approved' is a machine-checkable state, retraction is immediate and auditable, and a conversation can be correlated with the exact claim set in force (an IDD/complaints requirement). The maintenance answer is currently a hole either way: NO product admin UI exists (verified app/admin/(protected)/ inventory), so a products content page — or routing through the existing proposals flow — must be added; until it exists, seeds remain the de facto authoring path regardless of storage choice.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, testing-bdd, tool-mapping

#### T11.D3 — Addon information surface: dedicated get_product_addon_info(product_id, addon_id) per the catalog, or fold addon selling info and pricing examples into get_product_info?

- **Dedicated get_product_addon_info**: New read tool returning sell_specific_addon_info + addon pricing_examples, exposed when a 'candidate addon is in focus' — which requires adding candidate-addon state to Conversation and addon handling to set_candidate_product (neither exists today).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Catalog-faithful and scales cleanly to many addons, but it introduces a second in-focus pointer (candidate addon) beside the candidate product — exactly the 'second store of the selection that can diverge' the spec's own regression guard forbids — plus another engine exposure rule and a two-call read for what is one sellable surface. With one addon in the catalog, every cost is real and the scaling benefit is hypothetical.
- **✅ Recommended — Fold into get_product_info addons[] (drop the dedicated tool)**: Each entry in get_product_info's addons[] carries sell_specific_addon_info and its derived pricing_examples (expressed as base vs base+addon deltas from the same calculateQuote pass). No addon-focus state, no extra tool; the catalog's simplification license applies.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One read returns one consistent snapshot of the entire sellable thing — base and addon prices computed in the same engine pass can never disagree, and the customer's actual question ('what does BD add to my price?') is answered by construction. Payload grows with addon count, but content is bounded and the shaper already dedups; if addons ever multiply, the surface can be re-split without data-model change since addons remain product-scoped rows (Addon.productId FK, @@unique([productId, code])).
- **Both: summary inline, detail on demand**: get_product_info keeps addon summaries (id, name, short_desc) and a dedicated detail tool returns the full addon info.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Mirrors the catalog's list/detail split, but creates two sources for overlapping content that must be kept consistent, doubles the exposure rules, and still needs the candidate-addon state. The consistency burden buys nothing while one addon exists.

**Rationale:** Addons are existentially product-scoped — there is no addon identity outside its product — so the product read IS the natural consistency boundary. The decisive architectural argument is state minimalism: the candidate product is contractually the sole owner of product-in-focus, and a parallel candidate-addon pointer reintroduces the divergence class the spec explicitly guards against. Pricing correctness also favors folding: the meaningful addon price is the delta on top of a base selection, which is only guaranteed coherent when both come from one calculateQuote evaluation in one response. The catalog framing explicitly permits eliminating tools when the flow simplifies; this is that case.

**Depends on / interacts with:** tool-mapping, legality-engine, commit-envelope

#### T11.D4 — Where does the discovery-phase early eligibility pre-check run — agent compares eligibility_bounds itself, the engine injects a computed verdict into per-turn state, or a separate check tool the agent calls?

- **Agent-side comparison**: get_product_info returns eligibility_bounds; the agent compares the customer's stated age against them and warns before the funnel.
  _Tradeoffs:_ The catalog's literal phrasing, and zero engine work — but the comparison itself becomes LLM judgment, directly violating the engine invariant 'compliance and eligibility are deterministic, never LLM judgments'. Untestable at the engine boundary, and the agent can mis-compare, miss the check entirely, or hallucinate bounds; a GUI client would get no signal at all (fails the swap test).
- **✅ Recommended — Engine-computed verdict injected in derived state**: A pure eligibility evaluator (bounds x derived age -> eligible | ineligible(reason) | unknown(missing_age)) runs inside deriveState when a candidate product exists; the verdict lands in the injected state grounding and in available/blocked_actions (set_application blocked with reason ineligible_age). The SAME evaluator runs inside generate_quote as the final gate. eligibility_bounds stays on the get_product_info read so the agent can explain WHY ('the limit is 18-64'), but never decides.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Deterministic, swap-test clean (a GUI sees the same blocked action), unit-testable as a pure function, and single-implementation: the early signal and the final quote gate cannot disagree because they are the same code. Requires a reliable derived age (DOB or declaredAge per the CustomerProfile SSOT direction) and an honest 'unknown' state — the cost is that the signal is silent until age is known, which is correct behavior, not a defect.
- **Dedicated check_eligibility tool**: A read/commit tool the agent calls with the candidate product to get a deterministic verdict.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Deterministic too, but pull-based: the protection depends on the agent remembering to call it, and the documented failure history of this codebase (advance-flow deadlock, navigation stalls) is precisely agents not making the expected call. Its result duplicates what every-turn injected state can carry for free, and a forgotten call reproduces the Gherkin anti-scenario (customer sent into a questionnaire that will reject them).

**Rationale:** The target architecture already commits to engine-computed available/blocked actions injected every turn; eligibility is a legality input to set_application and generate_quote, so it belongs in that same derivation. Option 1 contradicts the spec's own invariant, and option 3 makes a compliance guarantee contingent on agent diligence — the one component the system is designed not to trust. The non-negotiable companion fix: generate_quote currently has NO age gate and fabricates age 30 on missing DOB (lib/tools/handlers/quote-handlers.ts:63), so the evaluator must be wired there in the same change; an early signal backed by no final gate is theater. Pre-check placement in discovery means the evaluator keys off the CANDIDATE product (deriveState already resolves committed-else-candidate, derive-state.ts:87-95), satisfying 'before the funnel'.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, identity, phase-model, quote-lifecycle, questionnaire-consequences

#### T11.D5 — What content migration does the 'protect' seed need for the new fields, and what happens to the overlapping legacy fields (features, pricingExplanation, premiumRange, targetAgeRange, playbook prices)?

- **Additive only**: Add the new fields beside the legacy ones; both keep feeding the agent until someone cleans up later.
  _Tradeoffs:_ No re-authoring risk, but perpetuates price triplication and gives the agent two competing claim sources, directly contradicting the Gherkin rule that every selling point comes from the new fields; the prompt loaders keep their defensive reconciliation logic forever. Worst option for data integrity.
- **Map content, keep legacy fields**: Author the new fields from existing material (features -> localized key points; playbook value-prop -> sell_specific_info; eligibility Json -> structured bounds) but leave features/pricingExplanation/premiumRange in place for backward compatibility of existing consumers (compare_products, list_products, productContext).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Lower blast radius on existing read paths, but the stale fields remain live ammunition: pricingExplanation still hardcodes six premiums into every get_product_info response, and premiumRange (base-only 190-430) keeps anchoring customers below real base+addon totals (up to 1130 RON). Divergence risk persists by design.
- **✅ Recommended — Map content and retire overlapping legacy fields**: Author: (a) ~8-10 localized key_value_product_points distilled from features[] + the playbook's value proposition; (b) sell_specific_info — BD-led framing, complement positioning, cost-anchoring narrative WITHOUT figures; (c) sell_specific_addon_info for TREATMENT_ABROAD_BD — the component breakdown currently buried in the playbook, with EUR amounts referenced from CoverageAmount rows rather than retyped; (d) structured eligibility {minAge:18, maxAge:64, residency, healthRequirements, cumulativeSumCap:50000 EUR}. Retire: features[] (superseded), pricingExplanation (replaced by derived pricing_examples + a short authored numbers-free 'how pricing works' note), premiumRange (derivable as min/max over PricingLevel +/- addon rules), targetAgeRange (folded into sell_specific_info as audience framing, clearly separated from eligibility). Purge every hardcoded price from defaultPlaybook, replacing with 'present figures from pricing_examples' directives; update compare_products and productContext/catalogOverview loaders to the new sources.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Restores a single source of truth for every number and a single authored source for every claim; eliminates the targetAgeRange-vs-eligibility confusion hazard (an agent telling a 50-year-old 'this is for 25-45' when eligibility runs to 64). Requires compliance re-review of re-authored Romanian/English copy and touches the consumers of the retired fields — but leaving them is precisely the ambiguity the new model exists to remove.

**Rationale:** The new fields only deliver their guarantee if they are the ONLY source: the Gherkin pins selling points to the new fields exclusively, so legacy near-duplicates are not harmless leftovers but standing violations. Every number currently embedded in prose (pricingExplanation premiums, playbook lei/luna figures, premiumRange) either derives from pricing rows or is stale risk; every claim in features[]/playbook either graduates into the authored, localized, versioned fields or was never reviewed and should not be uttered. The playbook keeps its legitimate role (tone, pacing, objection choreography) — it loses only the embedded facts, which move to surfaces the engine guarantees.

**Depends on / interacts with:** testing-bdd, quote-lifecycle, legality-engine, tool-mapping

### Risks

- Age-resolution divergence: three inconsistent resolutions exist today (get_product_info: DOB -> extractedProfile.age -> undefined; generate_quote: DOB -> hardcoded 30; CustomerProfile SSOT specced but unimplemented). If derived pricing_examples trim by one age and the quote uses another, the agent shows an example the quote then contradicts — the exact failure the design is meant to preclude. The eligibility evaluator and example derivation must consume one shared derived-age function.
- Until pricingExplanation and defaultPlaybook are purged, the agent carries prompt-injected hardcoded prices that bypass any pricing_examples discipline; repricing PricingLevel/AddonPricingRule rows already silently strands them today. Partial adoption (new fields added, prose not purged) is worse than the status quo because it creates apparent-but-false safety.
- Prompt-rule conflict: the discovery skill pack forbids prices in early discovery (prisma/seeds/seed-skill-packs.ts:35,107) while the catalog mandates serving pricing_examples on request; unreconciled, the agent will either refuse legitimate price questions or leak at the wrong moment. The pack rules must be rewritten against the new surface.
- Cache staleness vs governance: productContext and catalogOverview are cached 10 minutes (lib/chat/context-loaders.ts:28-30) and only the overview has a flush hook; with versioned content, a compliance retraction could keep serving retired claims until cache expiry. Publish must invalidate all product-content caches.
- get_product_info is uncacheable because output is shaped per customer age (lib/tools/registry.ts:457-460); derived pricing_examples keep it so. Any future caching must key on age band or one customer's pricing view leaks to another.
- Unknown-age degradation: the 'early eligibility signal before the funnel' only fires when age is derivable. The evaluator needs an explicit unknown state surfaced as such — collapsing unknown into eligible silently kills the Gherkin scenario; collapsing it into ineligible blocks legitimate customers.
- Anchoring gap: premiumRange covers base product only (190-430 RON/yr) while the BD addon adds up to 700 RON/yr; customers anchored on the range can face a 1130 RON quote. Derived pricing_examples must label base vs base+addon explicitly or the addon-led sales strategy (playbook leads with BD) produces systematic sticker shock.
- Localization of claims: features[] is EN-only today; if key_value_product_points inherits that, the ro-first agent paraphrases compliance-reviewed claims on the fly — i.e., the authored field stops being the thing compliance reviewed. Localized variants must be first-class and reviewed per locale.
- Single-product overfitting: 'protect' prices on age alone with annual premiums in RON; baking 'age' in as THE variation parameter of pricing_examples (rather than a per-product declared parameter list) will not survive the forward-looking multi-product catalog the docs anticipate.
- Governance vacuum: no product admin UI exists, so whatever storage is chosen, seeds remain the authoring path; a versioned-content design without an authoring/review surface risks version 1 being the only version forever while appearing governed.

---

## T12. Testing strategy: making the Gherkin spec actionable

> Topic key: `testing-bdd`

### Current state (code-grounded)

TEST RUNNERS. Vitest only — no cucumber/BDD tooling anywhere (package.json devDependencies: vitest, @playwright/test, tsx; no @cucumber/* packages). Two configs: vitest.config.ts runs __tests__/**/*.test.ts (112 files); vitest.e2e.config.ts runs e2e/scenarios/**/*.test.ts with 120s test timeout. npm scripts: `test` (unit), `test:e2e`, `simulate` (scripts/simulate.ts).

UNIT/INTEGRATION LAYER (__tests__/**). Every test that touches the DB mocks prisma via vi.mock('@/lib/db') — including ALL of __tests__/integration/* (verified in __tests__/integration/navigation.test.ts:3-15, __tests__/lib/chat/derive-state.test.ts:4-17, __tests__/lib/tools/consent-tools.test.ts:3-7). There is NO real-test-DB practice anywhere in __tests__ (grep for PrismaClient/TEST_DATABASE/DATABASE_URL in __tests__: zero matches). The one genuinely pure-engine suite is __tests__/lib/engines/quote-engine.test.ts: lib/engines/quote-engine.ts exposes calculateQuote(QuoteInput) as a pure function tested with literal inputs mirroring prisma/seeds/seed-product.ts — the only existing example of the "pure decision core" test seam. questionnaire-engine.test.ts (39 its) and question-groups.test.ts use mocked prisma.

E2E LAYER (e2e/). 5 scenario tests (happy-path, bd-rejection, change-of-mind, dnt-pause-resume, objection-handling) drive a LIVE app at APP_URL/localhost:3001 over POST /api/chat SSE. Harness: e2e/lib/sse-parser.ts (ParsedTurn = content + toolsCalled + uiActions + errors + done + rawEvents), e2e/lib/client-simulator.ts (hybrid responder: deterministic answersMap for show_question, scripted reactions for product cards/quote/payment, OpenAI gpt-4o-mini fallback for free-form), e2e/lib/personas.ts (DEFAULT_ANSWERS keyed by question code), e2e/lib/turn-tracker.ts (assertToolCalled/assertNoErrors/assertTurnCount), e2e/lib/db-verifier.ts (per-scenario Prisma checks against the REAL dev DB — verifyHappyPath asserts Conversation COMPLETED, Application COMPLETED + tier/level/addon, dntSignedAt, Quote ACCEPTED, Policy PENDING_SUBMISSION|SUBMITTED, Payment COMPLETED), e2e/lib/test-reporter.ts. No DB isolation/teardown; not part of `npm test`.

SCRIPTED-SIM LAYER (scripts/). scripts/verify-advance-flow.ts is the pattern that caught bugs unit tests missed: drives lib/chat/orchestrator.handleChatTurn directly (no HTTP), live LLM, real dev DB, a fixed opening script to convergence, then question-aware regex answer-picking (pickAnswer), then asserts deterministic predicates per trial — ADVANCED (Answer rows for dnt-phase questions / Application / dntSignedAt in DB) && !CEREMONY (regex over assistant messages) — with n-of-m trial pass policy. scripts/verify-pathology1-4.ts follow the same shape. A SECOND, parallel sim stack exists at lib/simulation/* (driver.ts, runner.ts, personas.ts, sse-client.ts, scenarios/* with trigger/response ScenarioStep DSL incl. 'abandon'), persisting SimulationRun rows and feeding lib/self-improvement (scorer.ts scores conversations 0-1 by quote/application/policy milestones — outcome scoring, NOT an LLM judge; no judge/rubric code exists anywhere, verified by grep).

REPLAY/EVIDENCE INFRA. TurnDebug table (prisma/schema.prisma:661-672: conversationId, messageIndex, traceId unique, payload Json) persists per-turn debug payloads; lib/debug/reducer.ts DebugTurn carries userMessage, prompt, toolCalls[{name,args,partition,result}], toolNarration, totals, and lib/chat/debug.ts:45-48 includes the full DerivedState snapshot per turn. lib/debug/conversation-export.ts (pure, tested in __tests__/lib/debug/conversation-export.test.ts) assembles a self-contained ConversationExport (messages + chronological turns) served by app/api/conversations/[id]/export/route.ts and downloadable from components/debug/debug-drawer.tsx. Nothing currently consumes exports for assertions.

DETERMINISTIC AGENT GUARDS ALREADY IN CODE. lib/chat/tool-narration-detector.ts and lib/chat/side-effect-validator.ts (tested in __tests__/lib/chat/) deterministically police success-narration claims against actual tool side effects — directly relevant to the @contract scenarios "A commit that fails is surfaced, never narrated as success" and "never advances a phase by narration". lib/chat/derive-state.ts computes the 6-phase model + nextBestAction (a prose string, not available_actions/blocked_actions).

THE SPEC. docs/tools as wokflow scenarios/zeno_workflow.feature: 9 Feature blocks, 61 scenario blocks (68 cases with the two Scenario Outline Examples tables expanded: 5 modify-consequence rows, 4 generate_quote outcome rows), tagged @contract/@architecture/@regression, @discovery/@consultancy, @application+@dnt+@consent, @application+@questionnaire, @application+@quote_generation, @quote, @payment, @policy, @lifecycle+@regression, plus a commented EXTENSION BACKLOG (lines 450-461). It declares itself a LIVING spec extended via Examples tables (line 6). No test anywhere references the .feature file; zero traceability exists. Most tools the spec names (get_dnt_state, start_dnt_session, sign_dnt-with-session, identify_customer, acknowledge_disclosures, resume_payment, retry_payment, change_payment_option, get_policy_status, request_cancellation, withdraw_consent as specced) do not exist in lib/tools, and the engine vocabulary the spec's Given/Then clauses use (available_actions, blocked_actions, consequence values) has no code referent.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** questionnaire-engine.test.ts (39 its) and question-groups.test.ts use mocked prisma.
  **Correction:** Only half true. __tests__/lib/engines/question-groups.test.ts does mock prisma (vi.mock('@/lib/db') at line 6), and the 39-it count for questionnaire-engine.test.ts is correct — but __tests__/lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.test.ts contains no vi.mock at all. It is a pure-function suite: it imports shouldShowQuestion, validateAnswer, and checkForFlags from @/lib/engines/questionnaire-engine and tests them with literal inputs (Maps and plain objects), never touching prisma, mocked or real. _(__tests__/lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.test.ts:1-6 (imports only pure functions, no vi.mock anywhere in the file; grep for vi.mock across __tests__/lib/engines/ matches only question-groups.test.ts:6))_
- **Claim:** The one genuinely pure-engine suite is __tests__/lib/engines/quote-engine.test.ts ... the only existing example of the "pure decision core" test seam.
  **Correction:** quote-engine.test.ts is indeed pure (calculateQuote(QuoteInput) tested with literal inputs mirroring prisma/seeds/seed-product.ts — that part is verified), but it is not the only pure-engine example. __tests__/lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.test.ts is also a mock-free pure-function suite over lib/engines functions (shouldShowQuestion/validateAnswer/checkForFlags), and __tests__/integration/auto-candidate-assignment.test.ts (inferCandidate from lib/chat/candidate-inference) and __tests__/integration/phase-transition.test.ts (getConversationPhase from lib/chat/phase) are likewise pure-function tests with zero mocks. The 'pure decision core' seam already has at least four existing examples, not one. _(__tests__/lib/engines/quote-engine.test.ts:1-2 (pure import of calculateQuote/QuoteInput; lib/engines/quote-engine.ts:77 export function calculateQuote); __tests__/lib/engines/questionnaire-engine.test.ts:1-6; __tests__/integration/auto-candidate-assignment.test.ts:1-13; __tests__/integration/phase-transition.test.ts:1-7)_
- **Claim:** Every test that touches the DB mocks prisma via vi.mock('@/lib/db') — including ALL of __tests__/integration/*.
  **Correction:** The core statement (no real-DB usage anywhere in __tests__; grep for PrismaClient/TEST_DATABASE/DATABASE_URL yields zero matches — verified) holds, and the three cited line references (navigation.test.ts:3-15, derive-state.test.ts:4-17, consent-tools.test.ts:3-7) are accurate. But 'ALL of __tests__/integration/*' is imprecise: 2 of the 6 integration test files (auto-candidate-assignment.test.ts, phase-transition.test.ts) contain no vi.mock('@/lib/db') at all — they are pure-function tests that never touch the DB. Only the 4 DB-touching integration suites (navigation, simulation-runner, skill-pack-orchestrator, ab-test-assignment) mock prisma. The related gap phrasing 'every __tests__ suite mocks prisma' is similarly overbroad — several suites use no prisma at all. _(grep -L "vi.mock('@/lib/db'" __tests__/integration/*.ts returns auto-candidate-assignment.test.ts and phase-transition.test.ts; __tests__/integration/auto-candidate-assignment.test.ts:1-13 and __tests__/integration/phase-transition.test.ts:1-7 show pure-function tests with no mocks and no prisma)_

### Gaps

- No BDD harness and no spec<->test link of any kind: zero references to zeno_workflow.feature from any test; the .feature is currently documentation only.
- The spec's core vocabulary has no code referent: available_actions/blocked_actions, the 14-value consequence taxonomy, and most named tools do not exist, so the majority of scenarios cannot be bound to code today regardless of harness choice (depends on legality-engine, commit-envelope, dnt-sessions, quote-lifecycle, payments, policy-post-sale topics).
- No real-DB test ring below e2e: every __tests__ suite mocks prisma, so DB-enforced invariants the spec demands (idempotent double-submit, one-application-one-quote uniqueness, concurrent GUI+agent serialization, answer-uniqueness) are tested only against mocks of the code's own assumptions — the project's own history (advance-flow deadlock: unit-green but live-broken) proves this seam misses real bugs.
- E2E scenarios run against a live dev server and the shared dev DB with no isolation, seeding contract, or teardown; they need localhost:3001 plus an OpenAI key and are excluded from `npm test` — they cannot gate anything as-is.
- Two parallel, divergent simulator stacks (e2e/lib/client-simulator.ts vs lib/simulation/driver.ts) duplicate persona/answer-map/SSE-parsing logic with no shared assertion vocabulary.
- No LLM-judge infrastructure exists at all (verified by grep over lib/self-improvement and lib/simulation); scorer.ts scores sales outcomes, not behavioral compliance — scenarios like 'politely declines', 'explains the benefit once and does not push' have no verification path.
- TurnDebug + ConversationExport replay infra exists but nothing consumes it for assertions — the richest behavioral evidence (per-turn DerivedState, tool calls with results, narration checks) is currently display-only.
- The consequence taxonomy in the catalog has no TypeScript union/enum, so the Scenario Outline Examples (modify_answer consequences, generate_quote outcomes) cannot be type-checked for closure against the implementation.
- Several spec scenarios are untestable even in principle today because their substrate is missing: payment reconciliation/double-charge (single-transaction Payment model, no webhook/reconcile path), disclosures gate (no acknowledgment model), free-look cancellation (no request_cancellation), requires_identity (no identify_customer).
- No flake policy for gating: __tests__/lib/events/instrumentation.test.ts is known-flaky, and live-LLM tests are inherently non-deterministic — there is no n-of-m or quarantine convention except the ad-hoc one in scripts/verify-advance-flow.ts.

### Decision points

#### T12.D1 — Harness: how do the ~50 Gherkin scenarios become executable — cucumber-js binding the .feature directly, translation into vitest with the .feature kept as the normative contract, a hybrid split by scenario class, or a vitest-native Gherkin plugin?

- **cucumber-js as a second runner**: Install @cucumber/cucumber; write step definitions (Given/When/Then glue) that bind zeno_workflow.feature directly; scenarios execute as written; agent-behavioral steps delegate to the sim harness.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: the spec is literally executable, so spec<->test drift is impossible by construction for bound scenarios; Examples-table rows become test cases automatically. Con: the glue layer is a stringly-typed regex-matching API surface that is itself untested and cannot be type-checked against engine types (a consequence string in the spec that drifts from the TS taxonomy fails at runtime, not compile time); step-reuse pressure produces generic steps with weak assertions; it bifurcates the test estate into two runners with separate fixture/lifecycle/reporting systems while the deterministic engine tests want to share fixtures and the pure-core seam with the existing 112-file vitest estate; and the agent-behavioral half of the spec is not step-bindable deterministically anyway, so 'executable spec' is only half-true.
- **✅ Recommended — Vitest translation with machine-checked traceability (.feature stays the contract)**: Each scenario becomes a vitest it() carrying a stable scenario ID (e.g. spec('dnt/refused-consent-blocks-funnel')); the .feature remains the single normative contract document; a meta-test parses the .feature with @cucumber/gherkin (parser only, no runner) and enforces a bidirectional 1:1 registry: every scenario/Examples-row must map to >=1 test ID or carry an explicit @backlog/@agent-judge tag, and every test-declared scenario ID must exist in the .feature.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: one typed surface — assertions are first-class TypeScript with compile-time access to the consequence-taxonomy union, engine snapshot types, and DebugTurn shapes, so taxonomy drift is a build error; engine tests, sim assertions, and the existing vitest estate share fixtures, seam, and reporting; traceability is enforced mechanically rather than by glue-binding. Con: the spec is not directly executable — fidelity of each translation is a human judgment at review time (the meta-test proves coverage exists, not that the assertion faithfully encodes the Then-clause); Examples-table rows need explicit enumeration in test code (mitigated by importing the parsed AST rows as test.each inputs).
- **Hybrid by scenario class (cucumber for engine features, vitest sims for agent features)**: Engine-deterministic Feature blocks run under cucumber-js step definitions; agent-behavioral scenarios run as sim-based vitest tests.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: each class gets its notionally best-fit tool. Con: the classification is per-SCENARIO, not per-Feature — the @contract, @discovery, @dnt, @questionnaire, @payment and @lifecycle blocks all mix classes (verified below), so this split fractures single Feature blocks across two harnesses, destroying exactly the 1:1 spec-to-suite traceability the exercise exists to create, and doubles the glue surface (regex steps AND sim assertions) with two divergence points against one spec.
- **Vitest-native Gherkin plugin (quickpickle / @amiceli/vitest-cucumber)**: Bind the .feature inside vitest via a community Gherkin-to-vitest bridge, keeping one runner while executing the spec directly.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: single runner plus directly-executed spec. Con: the binding DSL is still stringly-typed with the same generic-step pressure and no compile-time taxonomy checking as cucumber-js; it additionally couples the contract's executability to a thin community bridge whose Gherkin semantics (Backgrounds, Outline expansion, tag filtering) become a correctness dependency of the compliance suite itself — the contract layer should not have a third-party interpretation layer between it and the assertions.

**Rationale:** The decisive architectural facts are: (1) the spec's classification is per-scenario, so any framework split by class fractures Feature blocks; (2) the strongest available drift defense is type-checking the spec's vocabulary (consequence taxonomy, tool operation names, DerivedState phases) against the implementation, which only first-class TypeScript assertions provide — regex glue can never do this; (3) drift prevention does not require executing the .feature, it requires mechanically proving bidirectional coverage, which a gherkin-AST meta-test provides while keeping the .feature normative; (4) the engine tests must share the pure-core seam and real-DB ring with the existing vitest estate to stay coherent. cucumber-js buys direct executability at the cost of an untyped parallel API surface and a bifurcated estate, and it still cannot execute the agent-behavioral half deterministically.

**Depends on / interacts with:** tool-mapping, legality-engine, questionnaire-consequences

#### T12.D2 — Scenario classification: which Feature blocks are engine-deterministic, agent-behavioral, or both — and at what granularity is the classification maintained?

- **Per-Feature classification**: Tag each of the 9 Feature blocks with one class and route the whole block to one verification style.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: simple routing. Con: verifiably wrong — 6 of 9 blocks mix classes scenario-by-scenario (e.g. @discovery contains both 'set_application returns requires_identity' (pure legality) and 'consultative pushback without pressure' (linguistic)); forcing one class per block either over-tests prose with engine harnesses or under-tests legality with sims.
- **✅ Recommended — Per-scenario classification with primary class + optional secondary assertion**: Classify each of the 61 scenarios individually; a scenario can have a primary class (engine / agent) plus a secondary assertion in the other class where a Then-clause spans both (e.g. generate_quote outline: engine-primary outcome test + agent-secondary 'relays the reason without inventing a price' transcript assertion). Classification is recorded as tags in the .feature (@engine / @agent / @agent-judge) so the traceability meta-test can route and audit coverage by class.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: matches the actual structure of the spec, where most scenarios have a deterministic engine core and a thin conversational rendering clause; tags live in the contract document itself so the classification is reviewable and machine-readable; lets CI gate the engine class hard while the agent class gates on n-of-m or trends. Con: requires touching the .feature to add tags (acceptable — it is a living spec by its own declaration) and demands discipline that secondary clauses are not silently dropped.
- **Per-clause (Then-line) classification**: Classify every Then/And line independently and generate separate test obligations per clause.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: maximal precision. Con: explodes the traceability registry below the granularity at which humans review the contract; scenario names are the stable unit of communication with the spec's authors, and clause-level IDs are unstable under routine spec edits, making the registry churn-prone without adding verification power beyond what primary+secondary already captures.

**Rationale:** The actual feature-by-feature classification (verified against the .feature, lines cited from docs/tools as wokflow scenarios/zeno_workflow.feature): F1 @contract/@architecture (9 scenarios, lines 26-71): BOTH — engine-deterministic: 'changes reality only through exposed operations' (executor gating), 'every demanded action maps to an exposed tool' (pure registry-consistency check), 'idempotent on double-submit' and 'concurrent GUI+agent serialisation' (real-DB ring); agent-behavioral: 'renders only injected state', 'failed commit never narrated as success' and 'never advances phase by narration' (already partially deterministic via lib/chat/tool-narration-detector.ts + side-effect-validator.ts over TurnDebug), 'blocked action explained', 'outage degrades without fabrication'. F2 @discovery (9, lines 74-129): BOTH, agent-leaning — engine: 'set_application returns requires_identity', 'application frozen + advance_phase', candidate-switch handler; agent: out-of-scope decline, catalog-grounded answers (deterministic tool-trace assertion), candidate-set-without-approval-ceremony (the verify-advance-flow.ts CEREMONY regex is the existing precedent), prices-only-from-pricing_examples (deterministic price-token leak detection over transcripts — prior art exists from the pre-quote premium-leak work), early eligibility signal, pushback-once (judge-only). F3 @dnt (15, lines 132-241): BOTH, engine-heavy — engine: DNT validity/coverage gating, session uniqueness and second-session refusal, walk/finish signals, modify-without-consequence, sign/refused-consent, update/renew, type-coverage mismatch, withdraw-halts-processing; agent: resume-not-restart selection, explain-and-stop on refusal. F4 @questionnaire (9 + 5 outline rows, lines 244-303): BOTH, engine-heavy — engine: get_next_question, write/rejected-invalid, branching_metadata emission, the entire modify-consequence Examples table, cancel-consequences, completion gate; agent: explaining branching provenance, refused-mandatory-not-fabricated. F5 @quote_generation (1 + 4 outline rows, lines 306-329): ENGINE — pure deterministic outcomes; one agent-secondary clause (relay without inventing price/approval).
