F6 @quote (5, lines 332-366): BOTH, engine-heavy — engine: requires_disclosures gate, accept→advance_phase with express consent, quote_expired rejection, cancel terminal, pre-fill via get_last_application_info; agent: the cancel-and-re-apply explanation and re-confirmation dialogue. F7 @payment (6, lines 369-405): BOTH — engine: retry/resume exposure rules, reconciliation idempotency (real-DB), change_payment_option re_rating, auto-issue-on-first-payment as a system effect; agent + structural: 'never handles card data' (structural: assert no tool schema accepts card fields; behavioral: never asks). F8 @policy (3, lines 408-427): ENGINE-heavy — free-look-window rule and outside-window rule outcomes; agent-secondary: relay-without-promising. F9 @lifecycle (3, lines 430-447): BOTH — agent: 'funnel never deadlocks' (live sim, the exact class of bug only scripts/verify-advance-flow.ts has ever caught); engine: one-application-one-quote (DB uniqueness + handler), candidate-as-single-source (structural: only set_candidate_product writes candidateProductId). Net: roughly 65-70% of clauses are engine-deterministic, ~25% deterministically assertable over transcripts/TurnDebug, and only ~6 scenarios (pushback-once, polite decline, explanation quality) are irreducibly linguistic. Per-scenario tagging with primary+secondary is the only granularity that matches this texture.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, dnt-sessions, questionnaire-consequences, quote-lifecycle, payments, policy-post-sale, identity, phase-model

#### T12.D3 — Engine test seam: what interface do the engine-deterministic scenario tests hit?

- **Mocked-prisma handler tests (extend the status quo)**: Continue the dominant __tests__ pattern: vi.mock('@/lib/db'), script the mock returns, assert handler outputs and prisma call shapes (as in __tests__/integration/navigation.test.ts).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: fully hermetic and parallel-safe. Con: it tests the code against the code's own assumptions about query shapes — the mock agrees with whatever the implementation does, so relation mistakes, constraint violations, and transaction semantics are invisible; the project has a documented precedent (advance-flow deadlock: 636 unit tests green, agent broken live) that this seam produces false confidence; legality scenarios expressed as Given-state become tedious mock choreography rather than declarative state, which degrades exactly the spec-fidelity the Gherkin translation needs.
- **✅ Recommended — Pure decision core + real-DB commit ring (layered)**: Two seams by responsibility. (1) Legality and consequence computation become pure functions over an explicit snapshot type — computeAvailableActions(snapshot) -> {available, blocked:[{action, reason}]} and per-commit consequence functions — following the proven lib/engines/quote-engine.ts calculateQuote pattern; Gherkin Given-clauses translate to snapshot literals and the legality matrix is exhaustively enumerable. (2) Commit handlers (persistence, cascades, idempotency) run against a real dedicated Postgres test database with per-test transactional rollback or truncate-and-seed from prisma/seeds, covering the scenarios whose substance IS the database: double-submit idempotency, one-application-one-quote, concurrent serialization, cascade_invalidate actually deleting dependent Answer rows.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: each scenario tests the layer that owns the rule — legality rules get exhaustive, deterministic, declarative coverage with zero I/O, and data-integrity rules are verified against the only system that actually enforces them (Postgres constraints, transactions, unique indexes); the snapshot type doubles as the injected-state contract the agent renders, so engine tests and prompt-grounding share one type; Given-state literals keep the vitest translation close to the Gherkin text. Con: requires the legality engine to be DESIGNED with a pure core (a constraint on the legality-engine topic, though the right one); two seams means classification discipline about which scenarios belong where; real-DB tests need a managed test database and serialized access for the concurrency scenarios.
- **Real-DB everything (no pure core)**: All engine scenario tests run handlers against a real test Postgres; legality is tested by constructing DB state and calling handlers.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: one seam, maximal realism, constraints always live. Con: the legality matrix (every action x every state x every block reason) requires combinatorial DB-state construction, which couples hundreds of declarative rule-tests to seed/fixture plumbing and serial execution; it also lets the legality engine grow as DB-entangled code with no pure core, which directly harms the 'swap-testable client / GUI calls the same operations' goal — a legality function that can only be evaluated against a live database cannot be injected per-turn cheaply or reasoned about exhaustively.
- **HTTP route seam**: Drive engine scenarios through POST /api/chat (or future operation endpoints) as the e2e suite does, asserting on responses and DB state.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: tests the deployed contract end to end. Con: conflates engine legality with agent/streaming/prompt concerns — an engine rule failure and an LLM behavior change are indistinguishable at this seam; it injects LLM non-determinism into what the spec defines as deterministic; and it cannot reach engine states the conversation cannot naturally produce (expired quotes, expired DNTs, abandoned payments) without time-travel fixtures that the HTTP surface does not expose.

**Rationale:** The Gherkin engine scenarios split cleanly by what owns the rule: legality/consequence DECISIONS (exposed-when conditions, block reasons, consequence selection) are pure logic and deserve exhaustive enumerable tests against a snapshot — the catalog itself frames the engine this way ('available_actions computed and injected every turn'), and the swap-test invariant requires the decision core be evaluable independent of conversation or storage. Data-integrity EFFECTS (idempotency, uniqueness, cascades, serialization) are properties of Postgres-backed code and are simply not testable against mocks — the @contract scenarios 'idempotent on double-submit' and 'concurrent GUI and agent' are vacuous unless a real database arbitrates. The current all-mocks practice is the documented false-confidence seam; the current quote-engine pure-function practice is the documented success seam. This option generalizes the success and quarantines the failure.

**Depends on / interacts with:** legality-engine, commit-envelope, application-lifecycle, questionnaire-consequences, product-data

#### T12.D4 — Agent-behavior verification: how are the agent-behavioral scenarios (declines politely, explains once, never narrates success, never deadlocks) made enforceable?

- **Per-scenario assertions inside live sims only**: Extend the e2e client-simulator/TurnTracker with per-scenario assertion hooks (tool-sequence predicates, regex checks like verify-advance-flow's CEREMONY, db-verifier checks) evaluated inline while the sim runs.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: assertions see the full live system, the only class of harness that has historically caught the deadlock/loop bugs. Con: evidence is ephemeral — a failed run must be fully re-run (live LLM, minutes, money) to investigate; assertions written against in-flight SSE shapes are not reusable against recorded conversations; and inline assertion code accretes inside each scenario script rather than forming a shared, testable assertion library.
- **TurnDebug offline replay assertions only**: Run conversations once (sim or real), persist TurnDebug, and run all behavioral assertions as fast deterministic vitest tests over ConversationExport JSON (lib/debug/conversation-export.ts): tool sequences, DerivedState phase transitions per turn, narration-vs-side-effect consistency, price-token leaks, block-reason relay.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: separates expensive generation from cheap assertion — assertions re-run in milliseconds during development and over historical real conversations (regression mining from production transcripts); failures are replayable artifacts. Con: by itself it never generates fresh behavior, so it cannot detect new failure modes the recorded corpus lacks; assertion-only testing of stale recordings silently rots as prompts/tools evolve unless generation is also scheduled.
- **LLM-judge rubrics as the primary verifier**: Build judge rubrics per scenario ('was the decline polite', 'did it push more than once') and gate on judge verdicts over sim transcripts.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: the only verifier capable of grading linguistic qualities. Con: a judge is itself a stochastic component — gating the contract suite on it makes compliance non-reproducible and disputes unfalsifiable; most agent scenarios in this spec are NOT linguistic (they are tool-trace and state facts: called set_candidate_product, did not call start_dnt_session twice, no price before quote) and judging them is strictly weaker than asserting them deterministically; no judge infra exists, so this also builds the most fragile layer first.
- **✅ Recommended — Layered evidence architecture: scripted sims generate, TurnDebug is the assertion substrate, judge quarantined to linguistic-only scenarios**: Promote the verify-advance-flow pattern into the e2e harness as the GENERATOR (scripted personas, question-aware answer-picking, n-of-m trial policy, direct-orchestrator or HTTP drive); persist every sim turn to TurnDebug; implement ALL deterministic behavioral assertions as a shared library over ConversationExport (tool-call sequences and absences, DerivedState transitions, tool-narration-detector verdicts, price/phase-narration leak scans, db-verifier state checks) so the same assertions run against live sims, recorded sims, and real production conversations; add an LLM-judge stage ONLY for the ~6 irreducibly-linguistic scenarios, with verdicts persisted and trend-tracked, never hard-gating merge.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: deterministic facts are asserted deterministically and reused across three evidence sources; the expensive/flaky parts (LLM generation, judge) are isolated at the edges with explicit n-of-m and non-gating policies; failed runs are self-contained replayable artifacts via existing export infra; production conversations become free regression corpus. Con: three cooperating stages need an owner and a clear contract for what gates CI (engine suite + recorded-assertion suite) versus what gates nightly (live sims) versus what only trends (judge); requires consolidating the two existing sim stacks to avoid a third.

**Rationale:** The classification shows agent-behavioral clauses are mostly deterministic facts about traces and state, not vibes — so the architecture should maximize the deterministically-assertable surface and minimize what depends on judges or live runs. TurnDebug + ConversationExport already exists as the canonical per-turn evidence record (tool calls with results, DerivedState, narration analysis) and is the only substrate that lets one assertion library serve live sims, replays, and real conversations — that reuse is the structural defense against the two-sim-stack divergence already present. Live scripted sims remain mandatory as generators because they are the only layer that has ever caught the deadlock-class bugs (project history: advance-flow), but their non-determinism is contained by the established n-of-m trial policy rather than leaking into every assertion. The judge is kept where it is irreplaceable and kept out of the gate where it would make compliance unfalsifiable.

**Depends on / interacts with:** commit-envelope, phase-model, tool-mapping

#### T12.D5 — Living-spec process: how do Examples tables get extended as rules firm up, and how is spec<->test drift prevented?

- **Convention and review discipline**: Tests carry comments naming their scenario; PR review checks that spec changes come with test changes.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: zero machinery. Con: unenforced bidirectionality is exactly how the current state arose (a rich .feature with zero test references); silent drift is undetectable until a behavioral regression surfaces in production; comments cannot fail CI.
- **✅ Recommended — Bidirectional gherkin-AST traceability meta-test + taxonomy closure**: A vitest meta-suite parses zeno_workflow.feature with @cucumber/gherkin into its AST each run and enforces: (1) every Scenario and every Examples row maps to >=1 registered test ID (registry populated by a spec() helper each translated test calls), with explicit escape tags @backlog (not yet implemented — counted and reported, not failed) and @agent-judge (verified by rubric, linked to its rubric ID); (2) every test-registered scenario ID exists in the .feature (no orphan tests claiming dead scenarios); (3) taxonomy closure — every value of the TypeScript consequence union appears in >=1 Examples row or scenario assertion, and every consequence string in the .feature is a member of the union, so extending an Examples table with a new consequence row fails CI until both the engine emits it and a test covers it; (4) classification tags (@engine/@agent) drive a coverage-by-class report. Examples extension workflow: add the row to the .feature first (it is the contract), watch the meta-test fail with the unmapped row, implement engine rule + test, green.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: drift becomes a CI failure in BOTH directions; the .feature stays the single normative document while remaining plain Gherkin (any stakeholder can read/extend it); the Examples-first workflow makes the spec the forcing function for engine work, which is the 'living spec' intent stated in the file header; taxonomy closure ties catalog, spec, and code into one checked loop. Con: the meta-test is itself contract-layer code that must be kept honest (it must fail loudly on parse errors, not skip); stable scenario naming becomes load-bearing, so renames in the .feature require coordinated registry updates — which is the desired property, but must be understood.
- **Codegen test skeletons from the .feature**: A generator emits a stub test file per scenario; humans fill assertions; regeneration diffs reveal new scenarios.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Pro: new scenarios visibly produce empty stubs. Con: generated stubs decouple immediately after first edit — regeneration cannot merge into hand-written assertions, so the generator degrades into a one-shot scaffold while providing no ongoing bidirectional guarantee; it also tempts vacuous auto-passing stubs, which is worse than visibly missing coverage.

**Rationale:** A living spec is only living if extending it changes what CI demands. Parsing the real .feature at test time makes the document itself the machine-read source of obligations — no parallel YAML manifest to rot — and bidirectionality kills both failure modes: spec-without-test (new Examples row, new scenario) and test-without-spec (assertions enforcing rules the contract no longer states). The taxonomy-closure check is the piece specific to this domain: the consequence taxonomy is the semantic spine shared by the catalog, the .feature outlines, and the engine's return types, and it is the highest-leverage single point to weld them together at compile/CI time. Codegen and convention both fail the bidirectionality test.

**Depends on / interacts with:** questionnaire-consequences, quote-lifecycle, tool-mapping, legality-engine

### Risks

- Binding tests to the catalog's literal tool names before the tool-mapping topic settles couples the suite to names the framing explicitly says may change; mitigate with a single operations map (scenario-facing operation -> implemented tool name) imported by tests and the traceability meta-test, so a rename is a one-line change instead of suite-wide churn.
- Gating CI on live-LLM sims or LLM-judge verdicts makes the pipeline non-reproducible and expensive; if the gating tiers (engine suite + recorded replay assertions gate merges; live sims gate nightly with n-of-m; judge only trends) are not made explicit policy, flake pressure will erode trust in the whole compliance suite — the known instrumentation.test.ts flake already demonstrates how one flaky suite corrupts 'suite green' as a signal.
- A large fraction of the spec is currently unbindable (no legality engine, no DNT sessions, no disclosures/payment-recovery/policy tools); if the traceability meta-test launches with most scenarios tagged @backlog, the tag can become a permanent escape hatch — the backlog count must be a reported, monotonically-decreasing metric, otherwise the suite certifies far less than the spec implies.
- The e2e layer's lack of DB isolation (shared dev DB, no teardown, live server dependency) makes any promotion of sim scenarios into gating tests order-dependent and polluting; the real-DB commit ring and the sim harness both need a dedicated, reset-per-run database before their verdicts are trustworthy.
- Two simulator stacks (e2e/lib vs lib/simulation) plus a new scenario harness risks a third divergent implementation; if consolidation is not an explicit step, behavioral assertions will be written against whichever ParsedTurn variant is closest, splitting the evidence model the TurnDebug-substrate design depends on.
- Translated vitest tests can drift semantically from their Gherkin text even with perfect ID-level traceability — the meta-test proves a mapping exists, not that the assertion faithfully encodes the Then-clause; review convention must require quoting the scenario text in the test body so fidelity is inspectable at review time.
- Several scenarios (payment reconciliation/double-charge, concurrent GUI+agent serialization, free-look windows) require substrate that does not exist (webhook reconcile path, GUI action source, policy lifecycle); writing their tests against mocks now would produce vacuous green — they must stay @backlog until the owning topics (payments, policy-post-sale, commit-envelope) deliver real seams.
- The .feature's own assumptions can be wrong (the catalog says 'correct these if wrong'): e.g. its DNT product-type coverage list (home, car, life-...) contradicts the verified single-product catalog ('protect', LIFE only); tests must encode the engine's actual rule, and the spec text must be amended through the living-spec process rather than tests quietly diverging from the document.

---

## T13. Full tool mapping: current 33 tools vs catalog ~35 — keep/rename/eliminate/add

> Topic key: `tool-mapping`

### Current state (code-grounded)

All tools are registered in exactly one place: `lib/tools/registry.ts` (1,122 lines, 33 `registerTool` calls — verified no other runtime registration site exists; other hits are docs/plans only). Gating today is the union of `WorkflowStep.allowedTools` + active `SkillPack.allowedTools` + per-tool `alwaysAllowed` flags read via `isAlwaysAllowed()` (registry.ts:72). Note: the `ALWAYS_ALLOWED_SET` constant at registry.ts:380 is DEAD CODE — nothing reads it; the real mechanism is the per-definition `alwaysAllowed` boolean. 13 tools are always-allowed including two COMMITS (`record_gdpr_consent`, `acknowledge_ai_disclosure`, `set_candidate_product`, `switch_product`) — a legality-engine must replace this static union or "exposed when" stays fiction. `deriveState` (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:51-66) hardcodes tool names in `nextBestAction` strings (list_products, set_candidate_product, change_selection, start_application, record_gdpr_consent, sign_dnt, generate_quote, accept_quote) — every rename touches it.

## Table 1 — Current 33 tools → disposition

| # | Current tool | R/C | What it actually does (file) | Disposition |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | `list_products` | R | DB query by insuranceType (registry.ts:253) | **keep-as-is** → catalog `list_products`; payload must add `addons[id,name,short_desc]` |
| 2 | `get_product_info` | R | product + tiers/levels/addons, age-trimmed via shapeProductInfo (registry.ts:294) | **keep-as-is**; product-data topic owes explicit `pricing_examples` + `eligibility_bounds` fields |
| 3 | `compare_products` | R | side-by-side 2-5 products (handlers/product-handlers.ts) | **keep-as-is** (no catalog row; inert with 1 product but matches catalog backlog "multiple candidates explored in parallel"; pre-quote premium leak already fixed per Plan A) |
| 4 | `preview_product_requirements` | R | carry-over vs missing questions for a candidate switch, read-only (handlers/preview-handlers.ts) | **keep-as-is** (no catalog row; it is the non-mutating replacement that makes eliminating `switch_product` safe) |
| 5 | `get_current_state` | R | deriveState dump (handlers/state-handlers.ts) | **absorb-into ambient state injection** (catalog invariant: state + available_actions injected every turn); may survive as a thin explicit read — see DP8 |
| 6 | `set_candidate_product` | C | Conversation.candidateProductId + confidence (handlers/candidate-handlers.ts) | **keep**, reshape params: drop `confidence` (agent-internal judgment in a commit payload), add `addon_ids[]` per catalog |

| 8 | `get_objection_strategy` | R | sales-strategy content lookup (handlers/objection-handlers.ts) | **keep-as-is** as agent-side conversational aid; it commits nothing, so it does not break the swap test (conversation is the one agent-specific surface) |

| 13 | `save_dnt_answer` | C | validate + upsert Answer, returns next question / finish signal (dnt-handlers.ts:127) | **keep-rename** → `write_dnt_answer` (session-scoped) |
| 14 | `sign_dnt` | C | sets Conversation.dntSignedAt + 365d validity after 100% progress (dnt-handlers.ts:273) | **keep**, rework: session_id + `consent{gdpr, ai_disclosure}` bundle; absorbs #32/#33 — see DP6 |
| 15 | `start_application` | C | creates Application, optional tier/level/addon binding recorded as Answers, DNT-gated (handlers/application-handlers.ts:29) | **keep-rename** → `set_application` (freeze candidate snapshot; add `requires_identity` gate) |
| 16 | `save_application_answer` | C | validate, flag/escalate check, upsert answer for CURRENT question, tier/level/addon side-effects, auto-completes app (application-handlers.ts:127) | **keep-rename** → `write_question_answer`; gains typed consequence envelope (`applied`/`cascade_expand`/`rejected`) |
| 17 | `set_answer` | C | generic answer-any-question-by-code across DNT+application groups, edit support, NO cascade logic (handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts) | **absorb-into `modify_answer` + `modify_dnt_answer` and eliminate** — see DP1 |
| 18 | `resume_application` | C | PAUSED→OPEN + next question (application-handlers.ts:432) | **keep**; broaden to catalog semantics (resume any incomplete application, R-flavored position read) |
| 19 | `get_application_status` | R | status + progress + flagsForReview (application-handlers.ts:392) | **absorb-into injected state** (same payload deriveState already computes) — see DP8 |
| 20 | `cancel_application` | C | sets status **COMPLETED** — cancelled is indistinguishable from completed in data (application-handlers.ts:496) | **keep**; semantics fix mandatory: real CANCELLED status + `requires_confirmation`→`terminal` (application-lifecycle owns) |
| 21 | `change_selection` | C | tier/level/addon change on existing app, mirrors to Answers, expires DRAFT quote (handlers/change-selection-handlers.ts) | **absorb-into `modify_answer`** (PACKAGE_CHOICE/PREMIUM_LEVEL/BD_ADDON_INTEREST are questions; consequence `re_rating`) — see DP2 |
| 22 | `generate_quote` | C | consent check, requires COMPLETED app + tier/level, prices, creates Quote DRAFT (handlers/quote-handlers.ts:19) | **keep-as-is** name; gains `rejected`(reason)/`referred`/`advance_phase` outcomes — deterministic eligibility/compliance moves here (legality-engine + quote-lifecycle) |
| 23 | `accept_quote` | C | DRAFT→ACCEPTED, creates Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION) BEFORE payment, marks Conversation COMPLETED (quote-handlers.ts:316) | **keep**, rework: `payment_option` param, `requires_disclosures` gate, idempotency, Policy creation moves post-payment (payments topic) |
| 24 | `get_quote_details` | R | quote payload (quote-handlers.ts:261) | **keep-rename** → `get_quote_info`; add `payment_options` + `disclosures_required` |
| 25 | `modify_quote` | C | expires quote, reopens app (status OPEN, completedAt null), DELETES selection answers (quote-handlers.ts:449) | **eliminate** — violates one-application-one-quote + immutability; see DP2 |
| 26 | `check_bd_eligibility` | C | reads 6 bd_medical answers, any "true" → mutates application.includesAddon=false (handlers/bd-handlers.ts) | **absorb-into consequence engine** (`eligibility_recheck` on BD answers) — see DP7 |
| 27 | `initiate_payment` | C | creates PaymentIntent + NEW Payment row per call for PENDING_SUBMISSION policy (handlers/payment-handlers.ts) | **keep-rename/rework** → `resume_payment`; current handler is non-idempotent (new Payment row each call) |
| 28 | `collect_customer_field` | C | validates + saves one field (CNP encrypted), flips isAnonymous=false when all 5 collected (handlers/data-handlers.ts) | **keep** as KYC data-capture op, distinct from new `identify_customer` — see DP4 |
| 29 | `escalate_to_human` | C | Conversation→IDLE + console.log only (handlers/utility-handlers.ts) | **keep-as-is** (catalog cross-cutting); persistence/handoff is an impl gap, not a disposition issue |
| 30 | `profile_extractor` | bg | `stubHandler` returning "Not yet implemented" (registry.ts:1003) | **eliminate** — dead stub; background extraction is pipeline infra, not an LLM-callable tool |
| 31 | `summarizer` | bg | `stubHandler` (registry.ts:1020) | **eliminate** — dead stub, same reasoning |
| 32 | `record_gdpr_consent` | C | Customer.gdprConsentAt/scope; alwaysAllowed (registry.ts:1042) | **absorb-into `sign_dnt`** consent bundle — see DP6 |
| 33 | `acknowledge_ai_disclosure` | C | Customer.aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt; alwaysAllowed (registry.ts:1067) | **absorb-into `sign_dnt`** consent bundle (NOTE: this is the AI-act disclosure, NOT the IDD/IPID `acknowledge_disclosures` of the @quote phase — they must not be conflated) |

Tally: keep 14 · rename 8 · absorb 7 · eliminate 4.

## Table 2 — Catalog tools (39 counted in zeno_tool_catalog.md) → disposition

| `withdraw_consent` | cross | **new-build** — verified: zero matches for "withdraw" in lib/ | identity (+dnt-sessions) |

| `get_product_info` | discovery | exists; owes `pricing_examples` + `eligibility_bounds` | product-data |

| `get_quote_list` | discovery | **new-build** (same folding note) | quote-lifecycle |

| `update_dnt` | dnt | **new-build** — no renewal/update flow exists | dnt-sessions |

| `resume_application` | questionnaire | exists (broaden from PAUSED-only) | application-lifecycle |
| `get_last_application_info` | questionnaire | **new-build** — pre-fill flow absent; blocked on cancel_application semantics fix (cancelled apps currently look COMPLETED) | application-lifecycle |
| `cancel_application` | questionnaire | exists (semantics fix: CANCELLED status, confirmation, terminal) | application-lifecycle |
| `generate_quote` | quote-gen | exists (gains rejected/referred/advance_phase) | quote-lifecycle + legality-engine |

Current-only keeps with no catalog row: `compare_products`, `preview_product_requirements`, `get_objection_strategy`, `collect_customer_field`, (`get_current_state` pending DP8) — the catalog should be extended to list them rather than treating them as illegitimate.

### Fact-check corrections

_The adversarial verifier corrected these claims from the section above — where they conflict, the correction wins:_

- **Claim:** Gating today is the union of WorkflowStep.allowedTools + SkillPack.allowedTools + per-tool alwaysAllowed flags read via isAlwaysAllowed() (registry.ts:72); ALWAYS_ALLOWED_SET at registry.ts:380 is dead code and 'the real mechanism is the per-definition alwaysAllowed boolean' (repeated in gaps: 'gating is a static union ... + alwaysAllowed flags in lib/tools/registry.ts').
  **Correction:** Half right: ALWAYS_ALLOWED_SET (registry.ts:380-392) is indeed dead code. But the per-definition alwaysAllowed boolean is ALSO dead with respect to runtime gating. isAlwaysAllowed() (registry.ts:72-73) is the only reader of the flag, and it has zero runtime callers — its sole reference outside the registry is a vi.fn mock in __tests__/performance/bench-pipeline.test.ts:239. The actual 'always available' mechanism is the hardcoded DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS list (10 tools) in lib/chat/default-tools.ts:9-20, merged via withDefaultDiscoveryTools(WorkflowStep.allowedTools) at lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:417-419, then unioned with pack tools via computeAllowedTools (lib/skills/skill-pack-loader.ts:169-190) at orchestrator.ts:791-794. So the true union is DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS + WorkflowStep.allowedTools + SkillPack.allowedTools; the alwaysAllowed flags gate nothing. _(lib/tools/registry.ts:72-73 (only read of .alwaysAllowed); project-wide grep for isAlwaysAllowed → only registry.ts:72 and __tests__/performance/bench-pipeline.test.ts:239 (mock); lib/chat/default-tools.ts:9-20; lib/chat/orchestrator.ts:417-419 and 791-794)_
- **Claim:** 13 tools are always-allowed including two COMMITS (record_gdpr_consent, acknowledge_ai_disclosure, set_candidate_product, switch_product); risks section restates 'Four always-allowed COMMITS exist today ... registry alwaysAllowed flags'; DP6 says absorbing consent tools 'removes two of the four always-allowed commits'.
  **Correction:** Multiple count errors. (a) 13 definitions do carry alwaysAllowed:true, but by the report's own R/C taxonomy FIVE of them are commits, not two or four: update_customer_profile (registry.ts:642, classified C in the report's own Table 1 row 10) is the fifth, alongside set_candidate_product (552), switch_product (573), record_gdpr_consent (1104), acknowledge_ai_disclosure (1119). (b) Since the flags gate nothing at runtime (see previous error), the EFFECTIVE always-exposed set is DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS, which contains SIX commits: set_candidate_product, record_gdpr_consent, acknowledge_ai_disclosure, set_answer, change_selection, switch_product. set_answer and change_selection are always exposed despite alwaysAllowed:false in the registry (registry.ts:779, 847), while alwaysAllowed-flagged tools like update_customer_profile, get_customer_profile, compare_products, check_dnt_status, get_objection_strategy are NOT in the default list and are only exposed when a workflow step or skill pack grants them. _(lib/tools/registry.ts:642 (update_customer_profile alwaysAllowed:true), 779 (set_answer alwaysAllowed:false), 847 (change_selection alwaysAllowed:false); lib/chat/default-tools.ts:9-20 (set_answer, change_selection, switch_product in DEFAULT_DISCOVERY_TOOLS))_
- **Claim:** Gaps: 'post-payment logic (lib/payments/post-payment.ts) handles only magic-link issuance'.
  **Correction:** runPostPaymentFlow performs five steps, not one: atomic CAS of Payment PENDING→COMPLETED (post-payment.ts:28-31), Policy status→SUBMITTED (66-69), DNT suitability report PDF generation (72-84), magic-link issuance + isAnonymous=false (87-98), and purchase-confirmation email (135-153). The narrower Table 2 claim ('only identity infra is the post-payment magic link, post-payment.ts:87-100') is accurate; the gaps wording is not. _(lib/payments/post-payment.ts:26-176)_
- **Claim:** Gaps: 'ToolResult (lib/tools/types.ts) has success/error/data/uiAction/confirmation only'.
  **Correction:** ToolResult also has message?: string (and confirmation carries an optional provenance field). The substantive point — no consequence-taxonomy field — is correct, but the field inventory marked 'only' is incomplete. _(lib/tools/types.ts:49-68 (message at line 53, provenance at line 65))_
- **Claim:** Table 1 #19 / DP8: get_application_status can be absorbed because it is the 'same payload deriveState already computes' / 'deriveState already computes both payloads'.
  **Correction:** Overlap is partial, not same-payload. get_application_status returns flagsForReview (application-handlers.ts:407, 419) and raw tierId/levelId ids (416-417); DerivedState (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:12-28) contains no flagsForReview field — it computes phase, selection codes, consents, dnt, answered/required/missing, quote, answers, nextBestAction. Absorbing get_application_status into injected DerivedState as-is would drop the flagsForReview surface. _(lib/tools/handlers/application-handlers.ts:406-421 vs lib/chat/derive-state.ts:12-28)_
- **Claim:** Gaps (withdraw_consent): 'consent is two bare timestamps on Customer: gdprConsentAt, aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt'.
  **Correction:** Customer also stores gdprConsentScope (String?), written by record_gdpr_consent alongside the timestamp. Still no ledger and no withdrawal surface (verified: zero matches for 'withdraw' under lib/), so the substantive gap stands, but the data model is two timestamps plus a scope string. _(prisma/schema.prisma:285-287; lib/tools/registry.ts:1045-1048)_
- **Claim:** current_state: '33 registerTool calls — verified no other runtime registration site exists; other hits are docs/plans only'.
  **Correction:** 33 calls and no other runtime registration site are both correct, but 'other hits are docs/plans only' is inexact: __tests__/performance/bench-pipeline.test.ts also references registerTool (as a vi.fn mock of the registry module, ~line 240). Immaterial to the conclusion. _(grep registerTool → lib/tools/registry.ts, 5 docs/superpowers files, __tests__/performance/bench-pipeline.test.ts)_
- **Claim:** Gaps: 'get_product_info output has no explicit pricing_examples or eligibility_bounds fields ... the agent would have to infer bounds'.
  **Correction:** The exact catalog field names pricing_examples and eligibility_bounds are indeed absent, and per-level premiums are stripped (ShapedLevel has no premiumAnnual). However, ShapedProduct passes through the raw product's eligibility (Json), targetAgeRange, and premiumRange fields verbatim (shape-product-info.ts:139-149 and 222-240), so eligibility/pricing-range data is not entirely absent from the payload — it is unstructured passthrough rather than missing. 'Cannot pass / must infer' overstates; 'no structured catalog-shaped fields' is the defensible form. _(lib/tools/shape-product-info.ts:112-117 (ShapedLevel drops premiumAnnual), 139-149, 222-240 (eligibility/targetAgeRange/premiumRange passthrough))_

### Gaps

- Tools NEITHER side has but the Gherkin needs: a KYC field-collection operation is absent from the catalog — identify_customer is typed 'auth handoff', but policy issuance still needs CNP/DOB/address capture; current collect_customer_field (lib/tools/handlers/data-handlers.ts) fills this role and must be added to the catalog rather than dropped.
- Idempotency mechanism for commits (Gherkin '@contract: A committing action is idempotent on double-submit') exists nowhere: initiate_payment creates a NEW Payment row on every call (payment-handlers.ts:105) — a live double-charge path; accept_quote is merely fail-on-retry (status!=DRAFT), not idempotent-success. No commit carries an idempotency key. Owned by commit-envelope.
- available_actions/blocked_actions computation and per-turn injection (catalog engine invariant + '@contract: agent renders only injected state') does not exist — gating is a static union (WorkflowStep.allowedTools + SkillPack.allowedTools + alwaysAllowed flags in lib/tools/registry.ts); no per-tool 'exposed when' evaluation, no blocked-with-reason surface. Owned by legality-engine.
- No commit returns the 14-value consequence taxonomy; ToolResult (lib/tools/types.ts) has success/error/data/uiAction/confirmation only. Owned by commit-envelope.
- withdraw_consent: zero implementation surface — no handler, no consent-ledger storage (consent is two bare timestamps on Customer: gdprConsentAt, aiDisclosureAcknowledgedAt); withdrawal semantics (halt processing, preserve session) have no data model to act on.
- Cross-conversation/customer-scoped reads (get_open_items, get_application_list, get_quote_list, returning-user re-engagement scenarios) are structurally blocked: Application is unique on conversationId, DNT lives on Conversation — the CustomerProfile SSOT direction is a prerequisite, not an option.
- get_product_info output has no explicit pricing_examples or eligibility_bounds fields (lib/tools/shape-product-info.ts shapes tiers/levels/coverages); the 'early eligibility signal' Gherkin scenario cannot pass — the agent would have to infer bounds, which the catalog forbids. Owned by product-data.
- DNT renewal/update (update_dnt), DNT preview (get_dnt_questions), and DNT session entities do not exist — DNT today is Conversation.dntSignedAt/dntValidUntil + Answer rows, one-shot, conversation-scoped, no session lifecycle. Owned by dnt-sessions.
- Entire @payment recovery suite (get_payment_status, retry_payment, change_payment_option) and entire @policy suite (get_policy_status, get_policy_documents, request_cancellation) are absent; Payment is a single-transaction model with no schedule, and post-payment logic (lib/payments/post-payment.ts) handles only magic-link issuance.
- Disclosure model gap: catalog requires IDD/IPID acknowledge_disclosures gating accept_quote; nothing stores product-disclosure acknowledgment (only the AI-act disclosure timestamp exists) and accept_quote has no disclosure gate (quote-handlers.ts:316).
- Gherkin extension backlog items with no tool on either side (acknowledged forward-looking, flag only): GDPR data access/deletion request (@data), suitability-mismatch documentation (@compliance), installment failure/grace/lapse (@payment).
- escalate_to_human persists nothing (console.log only, utility-handlers.ts:26) — the '@contract: outage degrades gracefully → offers escalate_to_human' scenario has no auditable handoff record.

### Decision points

#### T13.D1 — DP1 — set_answer's fate: generic answer-by-code tool vs per-domain write/modify tools?

- **keep-generic-set_answer**: Keep set_answer (lib/tools/handlers/set-answer-handlers.ts) as the single answer/edit tool spanning DNT + application groups; retire save_dnt_answer and save_application_answer into it.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One tool, simplest agent surface. But DNT answers are flat/independent (consequence: applied only) while questionnaire edits carry cascades — a generic tool must infer domain from question code at runtime, making per-tool 'exposed when' conditions inexpressible (the engine cannot block 'modify application answer' while allowing 'write DNT answer' if both are one tool). It also collapses write vs modify, which have different legality windows (modify_answer is legal only while the application is incomplete).
- **✅ Recommended — per-domain-split**: Adopt the catalog split: write_dnt_answer / modify_dnt_answer (DNT), write_question_answer / modify_answer (questionnaire). Eliminate set_answer; its tier/level/addon side-effect logic moves into modify_answer's consequence handling.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Four tools instead of one, but each has a crisp exposure condition and a typed consequence envelope: modify_dnt_answer always returns applied (flat questions), modify_answer returns the full cascade set. Legality gating, consequence typing, and BDD testability all become per-tool properties instead of runtime branches. The duplicate upsert paths that exist today (set_answer vs save_application_answer write the same Answer rows with diverging side-effect code) disappear.
- **two-tool-hybrid**: One write_answer + one modify_answer, each spanning both domains, with the engine routing by question group.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Captures the write/modify legality distinction but still merges domains with different consequence semantics; exposure conditions ('a current DNT question is pending' vs 'a current questionnaire question is pending') differ per the catalog, so the engine would expose write_answer when only one domain is actually writable, reintroducing blocked-call ambiguity inside an exposed tool.

**Rationale:** The engine's whole value is that legality and consequences are computed per operation. set_answer is precisely the 'upsert without cascade logic' hole: it edits previously answered questions across both domains with no consequence model (set-answer-handlers.ts:45-49). Splitting by domain and by write-vs-modify makes every exposure condition and consequence type a static property of the tool, which is what makes the legality engine and the Gherkin scenario outline ('Modifying an earlier answer carries its consequence') implementable and testable.

**Depends on / interacts with:** questionnaire-consequences, dnt-sessions, commit-envelope, legality-engine

#### T13.D2 — DP2 — Fate of modify_quote and change_selection: in-place post-quote mutation vs cancel-and-reapply?

- **keep-both**: Keep modify_quote (expire quote, reopen application, delete selection answers — quote-handlers.ts:449) and change_selection (tier/level/addon swap that auto-expires DRAFT quotes).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Preserves today's working UX path. But modify_quote mutates a COMPLETED application back to OPEN and silently deletes Answer rows — a hidden cascade outside the consequence taxonomy, destroying the application→quote audit lineage; a quote that was presented to a customer becomes re-derivable from mutated inputs, which is a compliance liability (you cannot reconstruct what the customer was quoted on).
- **✅ Recommended — eliminate-both-cancel-and-reapply**: Eliminate modify_quote and change_selection. Pre-quote: tier/level/addon are questions (PACKAGE_CHOICE, PREMIUM_LEVEL, BD_ADDON_INTEREST already are), so modify_answer covers selection changes with consequence re_rating. Post-quote: cancel_quote / cancel_application + set_application pre-filled via get_last_application_info, per the catalog's one-application-one-quote rule.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Quote and application records become immutable after quote issuance — full audit lineage, idempotent re-quoting, and the Gherkin 'one application yields one quote' guard holds by construction. Customer pays a re-confirmation pass over pre-filled answers (the catalog explicitly mandates re-confirming every answer, which is itself a compliance feature, not a cost). Requires get_last_application_info and a real CANCELLED application status to exist first.
- **keep-change_selection-pre-quote-only**: Eliminate modify_quote; keep change_selection but restrict it to applications without an issued (non-DRAFT-expired) quote.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Avoids the audit problem post-quote, but keeps a second mutation path for data that is also stored as Answers — change_selection writes Application.tierId/levelId AND mirrors Answer rows (change-selection-handlers.ts:46-75), a dual-store that modify_answer's side-effect handling would otherwise own once. Two tools whose legality windows differ only by quote status invite drift.

**Rationale:** Quote immutability is the load-bearing compliance property: the engine must be able to prove what inputs produced the premium the customer saw. modify_quote's reopen-and-delete is the single worst offender against that. And since selections are already modeled as questions, modify_answer subsumes change_selection with a proper re_rating consequence — keeping change_selection would preserve a redundant dual-write path for the same data.

**Depends on / interacts with:** quote-lifecycle, application-lifecycle, questionnaire-consequences, commit-envelope

#### T13.D3 — DP3 — switch_product fate: in-place application migration vs candidate-recall + cancel-and-recreate?

- **keep-switch_product**: Keep the current tool (lib/tools/handlers/product-switch-handler.ts): repoint conversation.productId, reset tier/level/addon on the existing application, expire DRAFT quote, recompute totals, carry shared answers.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Convenient single call. But it mutates an existing application's product in place, so the application is no longer a frozen snapshot of any candidate selection — answer provenance becomes ambiguous (which product was HAS_DEPENDENTS answered under?), and the catalog's 'application freezes a snapshot at creation' invariant is unimplementable while this tool exists.
- **✅ Recommended — eliminate-split-by-phase**: Eliminate switch_product. Pre-application pivot = re-call set_candidate_product (catalog: 'no application exists yet, so nothing must be torn down'). Post-application pivot = cancel_application + set_application for the new product, with preview_product_requirements (already built, read-only) showing carry-over before committing and answer pre-fill on creation.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Two-step flow post-application, but each step is an auditable lifecycle event with its own consequence (requires_confirmation→terminal, then advance_phase); the frozen-snapshot invariant holds; the Gherkin 'candidate product is the single source of product-in-focus' guard becomes true by construction. Pre-application, this is strictly simpler than today.
- **demote-to-discovery-alias**: Keep the name but make switch_product a discovery-only alias of set_candidate_product that errors if an application exists.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Two names for one operation is pure surface redundancy; the agent must learn an arbitrary distinction, and the catalog already assigns this exact behavior to re-calling set_candidate_product.

**Rationale:** Single-owner product-in-focus (candidate_product) plus frozen application snapshots is the cleanest data-integrity story, and the codebase already has the supporting read (preview_product_requirements) that makes the destructive in-place migration unnecessary. Note the catalog's phantom-product caveat: with one 'protect' product in the catalog, switch_product is untestable against real data anyway — its current tests exercise a scenario the catalog cannot produce.

**Depends on / interacts with:** application-lifecycle, phase-model, product-data

#### T13.D4 — DP4 — collect_customer_field vs identify_customer: one identity tool or two distinct operations?

- **rename-collect-as-identify**: Treat field-by-field collection as identification: when all fields are collected, the customer is 'identified' (today's isAnonymous=false flip in data-handlers.ts:241-245), and call the whole thing identify_customer.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One tool, matches today's behavior. But it makes identity self-asserted: typing someone's email/CNP 'identifies' you as them, and identity gates cross-conversation disclosure (get_open_items, get_customer_info return prior apps/quotes/policies) — an unverified assertion unlocking another person's insurance history is an account-takeover and GDPR disclosure vector.
- **✅ Recommended — two-distinct-operations**: identify_customer = new-build authentication commit (auth handoff: OTP/magic-link verification — infrastructure partially exists post-payment in lib/payments/post-payment.ts, none in-funnel), returning requires_identity resolution. collect_customer_field = kept KYC data-capture commit writing validated fields (encrypted CNP, DOB) to customer-scoped storage, exposed after identity where the data feeds policy issuance.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Two tools, but they answer different questions ('who are you, provably' vs 'what are your details') with different security semantics, different exposure conditions (anonymous+funnel-action-needs-identity vs application/policy data needs), and different failure modes. Matches the catalog's explicit typing of identify_customer as 'auth handoff'. Requires adding collect_customer_field to the catalog (it is a genuine catalog gap).
- **fields-as-questionnaire-questions**: Eliminate collect_customer_field; model identity/KYC fields as questionnaire questions answered via write_question_answer.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Unifies all data entry under one engine, but KYC fields are customer-scoped (survive the conversation, encrypted-at-rest CNP, distinct retention/erasure obligations) while Answers are conversation-scoped questionnaire records — merging them re-creates the exact two-tier divergence the CustomerProfile SSOT spec exists to kill, and makes GDPR erasure of identity data entangled with underwriting answers that must be retained.

**Rationale:** Identity is a security boundary, not a data-completeness milestone. The returning-user scenarios (get_open_items surfacing pending payments days later) only work if identity is verifiable, and the requires_identity consequence is meaningless if any client can satisfy it by asserting fields. Keeping collect_customer_field separate also aligns with the customer-data SSOT direction: validated, encrypted, customer-scoped writes through one service.

**Depends on / interacts with:** identity, application-lifecycle, policy-post-sale, legality-engine

#### T13.D5 — DP5 — DNT read granularity: merge check_dnt_status's successor into one read, or adopt the catalog's four reads (get_dnt_state, get_dnt_questions, get_dnt_session_details, get_dnt_next_question)?

- **single-merged-read**: One get_dnt_state returning validity + products_covered + active session + progress + next question + full question list.
  _Tradeoffs:_ One call for the agent. But the four payloads have different scopes and exposure conditions: validity is customer-scoped and always relevant in @application; the question-list preview explicitly requires NO session; next-question and session-details require an active session. A merged read must compute all of it every call, couples invalidation scopes (a saved answer invalidates progress but not validity), and cannot express 'exposed when' per the engine model — blocked_actions reasoning becomes impossible for reads.
- **✅ Recommended — catalog-four-reads**: Adopt the split as specced: get_dnt_state (global validity/session pointer), get_dnt_questions (sessionless preview), get_dnt_session_details (per-session progress), get_dnt_next_question (stepper).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Four small reads, each with a static exposure condition matching a distinct Gherkin scenario (resume-not-restart, preview-without-session, progress-report, stepper). Reads are cheap and may be injected rather than called per the catalog header, so the count is not an agent-burden argument either way; what matters is that each read's freshness and legality are independently determinable.
- **two-reads-compromise**: get_dnt_state (validity + embedded session summary incl. progress) and get_dnt_next_question (stepper); fold the preview into get_dnt_questions=get_dnt_state(include_questions=true).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Fewer tools, but parameter-switched payloads put the exposure condition inside an argument (include_questions legal only when no session?) — the legality engine would have to validate argument-dependent exposure, a strictly more complex contract than per-tool conditions.

**Rationale:** Under an engine that computes exposure per tool, fine-grained reads with static conditions are the simpler formal object — every 'exposed when' is a row, not a branch on arguments. The merged options optimize for fewer registry entries, which is not an architectural property; the split optimizes for legality expressibility and independent cache/invalidation scopes, which are. check_dnt_status (dnt-handlers.ts:27) becomes get_dnt_state and sheds its progress fields to get_dnt_session_details once sessions exist.

**Depends on / interacts with:** dnt-sessions, legality-engine, phase-model

#### T13.D6 — DP6 — Consent commits: absorb record_gdpr_consent + acknowledge_ai_disclosure into sign_dnt, or keep standalone consent tools?

- **✅ Recommended — absorb-into-sign_dnt**: Per the catalog assumption: sign_dnt(session_id, consent{gdpr, ai_disclosure}) is the single consent-capturing commit; refusal returns requires_consent and preserves the session. record_gdpr_consent and acknowledge_ai_disclosure are removed from the tool surface; a consent ledger (who/what/when/withdrawn) lives in storage beneath it, which withdraw_consent operates on.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Atomic: no half-consented state (gdpr yes, ai-disclosure pending) for the phase machine to represent, and consent is captured at the legally meaningful moment (signing the needs analysis) with the session as evidence context. The CONSENT phase in deriveState (derive-state.ts:46 requires gdpr AND dnt.signed) collapses to one gate. Cost: consent timing is coupled to DNT timing — any future consent needed before DNT (e.g. data processing for the DNT conversation itself) has no tool; mitigated because talk-is-free and the ledger can record implicit conversation-start disclosures server-side.
- **keep-standalone-commits**: Keep record_gdpr_consent and acknowledge_ai_disclosure as separate commits; sign_dnt validates their existence (close to today's model).
  _Tradeoffs:_ Decoupled and flexible for future consent types, but creates partial-consent intermediate states the phase model must handle, three commits where one legal act occurs, and — as today — both are alwaysAllowed commits callable in any phase, which is exactly the unconstrained-commit pattern the legality engine exists to end.
- **consent-ledger-service-with-generic-record**: One generic record_consent(type, scope) commit over a consent ledger; sign_dnt references ledger entries.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Most extensible, but a generic consent commit pushes the 'which consents are required when' rule into the agent's choice of arguments — the engine should demand specific consents via requires_consent, not offer a freeform consent-writing tool.

**Rationale:** The catalog's no-standalone-CONSENT-phase assumption is sound: consent divorced from the act it authorizes is a state-machine complication with no compliance benefit, and the refusal path (requires_consent, session preserved) is well-defined only when consent and signature are one commit. The ledger-not-tool distinction keeps auditability without surface area. This decision rewrites deriveState's CONSENT phase and nextBestAction (derive-state.ts:46,57-58) and removes two of the four always-allowed commits.

**Depends on / interacts with:** dnt-sessions, phase-model, identity, commit-envelope

#### T13.D7 — DP7 — check_bd_eligibility: keep as agent-called verdict tool, or absorb into the consequence engine?

- **keep-agent-called-gate**: Keep the current tool (bd-handlers.ts): agent calls it after the 6 bd_medical questions; any positive answer flips application.includesAddon=false.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Explicit and visible in transcripts. But the agent decides WHEN (or whether) eligibility is evaluated — it can forget to call it, call it before all answers exist (handled by error today), or the addon silently stays included if the call is skipped. A commit whose omission changes the premium is a compliance hole, and it contradicts the invariant that eligibility is never an agent-orchestrated judgment.
- **✅ Recommended — absorb-into-consequence-engine**: Eliminate the tool. Answering a bd_medical question via write_question_answer returns consequence eligibility_recheck; the engine deterministically evaluates the BD gate when the last medical answer lands and flips addon eligibility itself, surfacing the outcome in the consequence payload (and re_rating if a draft premium changes).
  _Tradeoffs:_ The medical gate becomes un-skippable and ordering-deterministic — it fires because data changed, not because the agent remembered. The agent's job reduces to surfacing the consequence (exactly the Gherkin contract). Requires the consequence engine to exist; the BD rule itself (any-true → ineligible) is already trivial deterministic code that moves location, not complexity.
- **defer-to-generate_quote**: Eliminate the tool and check BD eligibility only inside generate_quote's eligibility pass.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Deterministic, but the customer learns at quote time that an addon they selected was silently removed — the catalog's eligibility_recheck consequence exists precisely so the surface happens at the answer moment; late surfacing also lets the conversation proceed on a false premise (discussing addon benefits the customer cannot have).

**Rationale:** 'Compliance and eligibility are deterministic decisions inside the engine, never LLM judgments' — an agent-invoked verdict tool is the halfway house that satisfies neither: the rule is deterministic but its invocation is probabilistic. eligibility_recheck-on-answer makes the gate a data-integrity property. The BD medical question group (bd_medical, 6 questions) and the addon-medical-gate rule survive intact; only the trigger moves from agent volition to engine consequence.

**Depends on / interacts with:** questionnaire-consequences, legality-engine, product-data, commit-envelope

#### T13.D8 — DP8 — Status reads (get_current_state, get_application_status) vs engine-injected ambient state: callable, injected, or hybrid?

- **keep-callable-reads**: Keep get_current_state (state-handlers.ts) and get_application_status as agent-called tools.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Works today, but the agent must choose to look — the entire class of stale-state bugs (acting on a phase that moved, narrating progress the engine didn't make) stems from optional freshness; the catalog invariant explicitly says state and available_actions are 'computed by the engine and injected every turn'.
- **injection-only**: No state read tools at all; deriveState's output + available_actions/blocked_actions are injected into every turn's context.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Guarantees freshness and makes the '@contract: renders only injected state' scenario true by construction. But deep payloads (full quote coverage tables, DNT question lists, flagsForReview details) injected every turn bloat context for information rarely needed that turn; reads with non-trivial payloads earn on-demand status.
- **✅ Recommended — hybrid-inject-summary-read-detail**: Inject the compact DerivedState + available/blocked actions every turn (retiring get_current_state and get_application_status, whose payloads the injection covers); keep targeted deep reads (get_quote_info, get_dnt_questions, get_payment_status, get_policy_documents) as callable tools.
  _Tradeoffs:_ Freshness where it prevents bugs (phase, legality, progress), on-demand where payloads are heavy. The line is principled: anything that gates legality is injected; anything that is presentation detail is read. Matches the catalog's own R-annotation ('ambient; may be injected rather than called').

**Rationale:** The legality model only works if the agent cannot be ignorant of the current legal surface — that must be pushed, not pulled. But pushing everything inverts into a context-bloat problem with no integrity benefit. The hybrid draws the boundary exactly where the catalog does: state/actions are engine-injected invariants; detailed payloads are reads. get_current_state and get_application_status are then redundant (deriveState already computes both payloads) and retire.

**Depends on / interacts with:** phase-model, legality-engine, commit-envelope

### Risks

- Rename/eliminate operations have hidden name-coupled consumers: deriveState.nextBestAction hardcodes 8 tool names (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:51-66), skill-pack allowedTools lists and DB-stored WorkflowStep.allowedTools reference names as strings — a rename silently desyncs gating (tool exposed under old name = never exposed), the exact failure mode that caused the advance-flow deadlock (prompt demanded tools the packs didn't grant).
- Prompt-driven sequences must be migrated atomically with the surface: eliminating set_answer/change_selection/switch_product while prompt sections still direct the agent to them re-creates the stall/loop pathology; unit-green will not catch it — only live sim did last time (verify-advance-flow lesson).
- initiate_payment is non-idempotent today (new Payment row + new PaymentIntent per call, lib/tools/handlers/payment-handlers.ts:105) — a real double-charge vector that exists NOW, independent of the transformation; the rework to resume_payment must include idempotency keys, and any interim period keeping the current handler exposed in @payment is live risk.
- cancel_application records status COMPLETED (application-handlers.ts:511-514) — cancelled and genuinely completed applications are indistinguishable in data; building get_last_application_info pre-fill on top before fixing this would pre-fill new applications from cancelled junk. Sequencing constraint: application-lifecycle status fix precedes the pre-fill tool.
- accept_quote currently creates Policy(PENDING_SUBMISSION) BEFORE payment and marks the Conversation COMPLETED (quote-handlers.ts:358-382), and initiate_payment locates the policy via the application→quote→policy chain — re-sequencing policy creation to post-payment (catalog: issue_policy is a system effect of first successful payment) breaks that FK walk; payments and quote-lifecycle must change together, not independently.
- DNT renames (check_dnt_status→get_dnt_state, start_dnt_questionnaire→start_dnt_session) ahead of the dnt-sessions storage migration produce tools whose contracts lie: get_dnt_state cannot report products_covered or session_active when DNT is two timestamps on Conversation — rename and re-platform must ship together or the agent reasons over fabricated fields.
- Four always-allowed COMMITS exist today (set_candidate_product, switch_product, record_gdpr_consent, acknowledge_ai_disclosure — registry alwaysAllowed flags); until the legality engine replaces the static union, every absorbed/eliminated consent tool removed from the surface must also be removed from skill-pack grants, or the old path remains callable in parallel with the new sign_dnt bundle (double-recording consent with diverging timestamps).
- 21 of 39 catalog tools are new-build, concentrated in payments (4) and policy (3) where no engine or data model exists — building tool fronts before their lifecycle topics land reproduces the profile_extractor/summarizer stub pattern (registered, exposed, returning 'Not yet implemented'); tools should land with their engines, gated by topic dependency order, not by catalog completeness.
- Single-product reality ('protect' LIFE only) makes several dispositions untestable end-to-end: switch_product elimination, get_product_addon_info deferral, compare_products retention, and the DNT products_covered field all reference multi-product behavior the catalog cannot produce — BDD scenarios for them pass only against synthetic fixtures, so green tests overstate confidence (testing-bdd must mark these as fixture-only).
- The consequence taxonomy is a breaking change to every ToolResult consumer (executor, pipeline, SSE debug surface, TurnDebug persistence, UI confirmation chips keyed on the current confirmation.category values) — commit-envelope must define the migration for lib/tools/types.ts before any per-tool rework starts, or each topic invents its own envelope dialect.

---

## Cross-topic contradictions (decide together)

_From the completeness critic: pairs of recommendations that conflict, or decisions that only make sense made jointly._

1. Identity tier × DNT ordering × DNT scope must be decided together: application-lifecycle recommends application-first with DNT as the first gate INSIDE @application, and the catalog gates set_application on requires_identity — so identity now precedes the needs analysis. identity recommends tiered-identity with tier-mapped gates but never names which tier unlocks set_application vs sign_dnt vs accept_quote, and dnt-sessions' customer-scoped Dnt aggregate is only meaningful if the customer identity attached to it is durable (an anonymous cookie-customer's 365-day DNT is worthless across devices). If the set_application tier is set high (verified email), the funnel demands verification before a needs analysis — a product-shaping decision currently owned by no single topic and not resolved consistently across the three recommendations.
2. Consent-truth migration is a three-way coupled change: dnt-sessions (fold GDPR+AI-disclosure into sign_dnt as the SOLE consent-writing commit), tool-mapping DP6 (absorb record_gdpr_consent/acknowledge_ai_disclosure into sign_dnt), and phase-model (drop the CONSENT phase) agree — but legality-engine's declarative predicates and today's deriveState gate (lib/chat/derive-state.ts:46, keyed on Customer.gdprConsentAt + Conversation.dntSignedAt) must switch to the Dnt aggregate as the consent source of truth in the SAME change, or the two divergent consent truths dnt-sessions flags persist into the new engine. Additionally, folding ALL consent into sign_dnt conflicts with the unowned GDPR topic: withdraw_consent and any non-DNT consent (marketing, data-processing for a customer who never signs a DNT) need a consent ledger that sign_dnt-only writing cannot provide.
3. Payment-frequency SSOT conflict: quote-lifecycle recommends persisting payment_option on the Quote at acceptance (Quote.paymentFrequency + acceptedAt), while payments recommends an engine-owned schedule and change_payment_option producing a derived-schedule-record WITHOUT mutating the accepted quote. After one pre-capture change_payment_option, Quote.paymentFrequency and the schedule disagree about the live frequency — recreating exactly the frequency drift payments flags today (quote engine vs payment handler domains). The two topics must jointly declare the schedule record the single live-frequency truth and demote Quote.paymentFrequency to acceptance evidence, and get_payment_status/initiation amounts must read only the schedule.
4. Selection-validity ownership conflict: application-lifecycle moves tier/level/addon selection OUT of the questionnaire into a select_coverage commit, while questionnaire-consequences' recommended explicit-dependency-edges engine computes invalidation over Answer rows. The canonical validity dependency — PREMIUM_LEVEL depends on PACKAGE_CHOICE (levelId is tier-scoped) — stops being an Answer↔Answer edge once selection leaves the questionnaire, so the cascade engine as scoped can no longer see it. Same for the BD addon: tool-mapping DP7 absorbs check_bd_eligibility into the consequence engine, but the eligibility_recheck triggered by bd_medical ANSWERS must mutate SELECTION state (includesAddon) owned by select_coverage. Either the dependency engine spans answers AND selection state (one graph, two node types) or select_coverage owns its own invalidation — decided together or tier-change/level-stale bugs survive the rewrite.
5. Policy issuance semantics: quote-lifecycle (no Policy at accept_quote), payments (payment-issues-policy), and policy-post-sale (PENDING_SUBMISSION→SUBMITTED→ACTIVE with back-office-owned transitions, freeLookEndsAt frozen at activation) are jointly coherent but jointly CONTRADICT the spec as written: the catalog's get_policy_status enumerates only active/lapsed/cancelled, and the .feature's 'First successful payment issues the policy automatically' (lines 402-405) cannot mean ACTIVE under the manual Allianz submission SOP. 'Issue' must be redefined as create-in-PENDING_SUBMISSION, and the free-look anchor must be chosen across topics (payment capture date vs Allianz activation date — policy-post-sale picks activation, but the legal cooling-off clock and the refund the payment module must execute both depend on this single definition). Three topics must define issued/effective/active once.
6. Single advance_phase computation: legality-engine (re-derive after every commit round), phase-model (derivation is truth; advance_phase is the pre/post-commit deriveState delta), and commit-envelope (effects[] carries advance_phase) each produce a phase-transition signal. These must be literally the SAME computation — the envelope's advance_phase effect must be the deriveState delta the legality engine computes when re-deriving — or one turn can show the agent contradictory phase signals (an envelope claiming advance_phase while the re-derived exposure still reflects the old phase, or vice versa). The three recommendations are compatible but only if implemented as one function with one call site per commit round.
7. DNT tool-surface arithmetic does not compose: dnt-sessions recommends a 'collapsed 6-tool surface (engine decides session type; one answer commit)' while tool-mapping DP5 recommends adopting the catalog's FOUR reads (get_dnt_state, get_dnt_questions, get_dnt_session_details, get_dnt_next_question). Four reads + collapsed commits (start/update merged into one session-opening commit, write/modify merged into one answer commit, plus sign_dnt) = 7 tools, not 6. One read must fold (most plausibly get_dnt_session_details into get_dnt_state) or the commit collapse is less aggressive than stated — the two topics must reconcile the exact surface before tool registration.
8. Idempotency × confirm-token ordering: commit-envelope recommends both 'replay returns original outcome' (natural-key CAS) and signed state-fingerprint confirm tokens for requires_confirmation commits. For accept_quote these interact: a double-submit AFTER the first accept succeeded carries a token whose fingerprint no longer matches current state (quote now ACCEPTED). If token verification runs before the CAS replay check, the replay returns rejected(state_changed) instead of the original success — violating the @contract idempotency scenario (feature:58-61). The envelope must specify check order: idempotency replay detection FIRST, token freshness second. Unspecified in the digest; must be pinned in the commit-gateway design.
9. Eligibility triple-implementation risk: product-data (engine-computed verdict injected in derived state), questionnaire-consequences (synchronous edge-scoped recheck), and quote-lifecycle (typed decision inside generate_quote with reason ineligible_age) each evaluate eligibility at a different funnel point. Unless all three bind to one rule source and one predicate (see missing topic 'Canonical eligibility rule representation'), the early signal, mid-questionnaire recheck, and final gate can disagree — e.g. discovery says eligible (authored eligibility_bounds) while generate_quote rejects (Product.eligibility Json) — the same triplication-and-drift failure mode product-data documents for prices.
10. Phase-rename sequencing couples three topics into one migration step: phase-model recommends a clean-break rename of the 6-value phase vocabulary; legality-engine's declarative per-action predicates are keyed on DerivedState phases; testing-bdd's taxonomy-closure meta-test type-checks against the same enums. The legality predicates cannot be written against the OLD names and renamed later without re-verifying every exposure rule, and the dual-vocabulary compliance checker (orchestrator.ts:651, 3-value) must die in the same change — otherwise the legality engine and compliance triggering disagree, the exact hazard legality-engine flags. These land as one coordinated change, not three independent ones.
11. Conversation terminality has agreement on what STOPS happening but no owner for what replaces it: quote-lifecycle (no Conversation COMPLETED at accept_quote), phase-model (Conversation stays ACTIVE through payment), and policy-post-sale (POLICY phase derived customer-scoped) jointly remove the only place Conversation.status=COMPLETED is ever set — but the orchestrator hard-rejects turns on COMPLETED conversations (orchestrator.ts:351-353) and nothing now defines when, if ever, a conversation completes or archives. Decide together with phase-model Q3: either conversations never complete (terminality fully decoupled) or a new terminal trigger (policy ACTIVE + n days idle) is specified — silently never-completing conversations change analytics, token budgets, and the returning-user entry path.
12. DNT exposure scope contradiction between catalog and customer-scoped recommendations: the catalog exposes get_dnt_state/get_dnt_questions/update_dnt only 'in @application', but dnt-sessions and application-lifecycle make the DNT a customer-scoped, 365-day, product-type-covering asset. A returning customer whose DNT nears expiry has no application — under catalog-literal exposure they cannot renew (update_dnt unreachable), yet the renewal scenario (feature:217-222) presumes they can. Either DNT tools get customer-scoped exposure conditions (legality-engine predicates over customer state, not phase) or renewal is only reachable by starting an application first — must be decided jointly by dnt-sessions, legality-engine, and phase-model.

---

## Additional topics the panel missed (completeness critic)

_Gherkin scenarios / concerns not owned by any of the 13 topics — each needs at least a parking-lot decision._

### M1. CustomerProfile SSOT delivery (cross-topic prerequisite with no owner)

Four panel topics (identity claim-and-merge, dnt-sessions customer-scoped Dnt aggregate, application-lifecycle customer-scoped applications, product-data age resolution) each name customer-scoped storage as their prerequisite, and the specced-but-unimplemented CustomerProfile SSOT (two-tier storage, age derived from DOB/declaredAge, extractedProfile/CustomerInsight divergence kill) is the strategic vehicle — but no topic owns delivering it or sequencing it relative to the topics that block on it. Without an owner, each topic will invent its own customer-scoping (e.g. dnt-sessions adds Dnt.customerId while application-lifecycle re-keys Application separately), recreating the divergence the SSOT exists to kill. Depends on: identity, dnt-sessions, application-lifecycle, product-data.

### M2. Cross-cutting customer-scoped reads + returning-user phase entry (get_customer_info, get_open_items, get_application_list, get_quote_list)

The catalog's cross-cutting table and @discovery table define four identity-scoped reads, and three .feature scenarios depend on them (abandoned-payment re-engagement lines 384-388, resume across conversations, post-quote re-apply). Payments, tool-mapping, identity, and application-lifecycle all FLAG them as absent, but none owns their contract: what counts as an 'open item', how a NEW conversation for a returning customer derives @payment/@policy exposure from customer-scoped state (the catalog's 'exposed when in @payment' is circular for re-engagement), and who triggers proactive re-engagement 'days later' (outbound email/notification — only magic-link templates exist in lib/email/templates/, and the post-payment magic-link URL is consumed by no route per the identity digest). Depends on: identity, phase-model, payments, application-lifecycle.

### M3. GDPR rights: withdraw_consent semantics + data access/deletion

'Consent withdrawn mid-flow halts processing' is a first-class normative scenario (zeno_workflow.feature:237-241, not backlog), and @data GDPR access/deletion is in the extension backlog (line 459). dnt-sessions and tool-mapping both flag withdraw_consent as nonexistent, but neither has a decision question for withdrawal semantics: what 'processing halts' means mechanically (block which commits? preserve the answered session per the refused-consent scenario?), scope parameter design, a consent ledger to act on (today consent is two bare timestamps on Customer), and erasure vs insurance-law retention obligations for signed DNTs/policies. No topic owns any of it. Depends on: dnt-sessions, identity, legality-engine, policy-post-sale.

### M4. GUI/uiAction surface and swap-test parity

The swap test ('a non-AI GUI client could call the identical operations', catalog Engine invariants) is the architecture contract, and a rich uiAction vocabulary already exists (show_question, show_quote, show_payment, show_policy_issued, show_data_field, show_bd_result/show_bd_rejected, show_product_cards across lib/tools/handlers/*; synthetic actions via lib/chat/action-adapter.ts). The transformation invalidates several (show_policy_issued at accept_quote must die per policy-post-sale; payments adds resume/retry sessions; data collection changes per identity), and the new envelope needs a GUI rendering contract: how requires_confirmation two-step tokens render as buttons, how blocked_actions render, whether synthetic actions pass the same legality filter and confirm-token flow. legality-engine covers executor enforcement and commit-envelope covers concurrency, but nobody owns the uiAction vocabulary redesign or the action-adapter migration. Depends on: legality-engine, commit-envelope, payments, policy-post-sale.

### M5. Operator/back-office surfaces: referral queue, escalation records, Allianz submission, refund execution

quote-lifecycle's recommended 'referred = Application REFERRED + operator work item' and policy-post-sale's 'back-office owns the transitions' both ASSUME an operator surface that no topic specifies: a referral work-item model and how an underwriter's decision re-enters the engine (the .feature's referred outcome at lines 327-329 is otherwise a dead end), escalate_to_human persistence (console.log only per tool-mapping, with no decision question anywhere), the admin policy status route that validates no transitions, the SOP activation-email stub, and who executes free-look refunds (PaymentStatus.REFUNDED is dead). Depends on: quote-lifecycle, policy-post-sale, payments, commit-envelope.

### M6. i18n: ro/en mid-conversation switch and language of engine-emitted text

Backlog item @i18n (zeno_workflow.feature:460) is owned by no topic. Substrate exists (lib/i18n/translations.ts, Conversation.language @default('ro') at prisma/schema.prisma:277, bilingual Question.text {en,ro} JSON), but the transformation creates new language surfaces nobody owns: blocked_actions reasons and consequence text injected into the prompt, new authored content fields (product-data flags features[] EN-only but its recommendation covers only product fields), DNT question text, document language (IPID, suitability report, policy docs), and the mid-conversation switch behavior itself. Depends on: legality-engine, product-data, dnt-sessions, policy-post-sale.

### M7. Suitability / demands-and-needs engine (@compliance)

Backlog item 'suitability mismatch documented (demands-and-needs warning)' (zeno_workflow.feature:458) has no owner, and it is the REASON the DNT exists: nothing maps signed DNT answers to a product-suitability verdict. The only artifact is the post-policy PDF (lib/compliance/dnt-report.ts), generated after the moment IDD requires the assessment. quote-lifecycle's generate_quote 'compliance_block' reason has no defined source; 'Consultative pushback' (feature:113-116) and candidate selection have no suitability input. A deterministic demands-and-needs check (engine, not LLM, per the catalog invariant) spanning DNT → recommendation → quote-gen is a whole missing engine. Depends on: dnt-sessions, quote-lifecycle, legality-engine, product-data.

### M8. Observability and audit of the new envelope (TurnDebug schema extension)

The catalog requires available_actions/blocked_actions injected every turn and a consequence from every commit; testing-bdd's recommended assertion substrate is TurnDebug — but no topic owns extending the TurnDebug/TurnTrace schema and debug drawer to persist the injected available_actions/blocked_actions, per-commit consequence outcomes, confirm-token lifecycles, and the content version in force (product-data versions content but doesn't link conversations to it). Without this, the testing-bdd recommendation has no data to assert on and the compliance audit trail (which actions/disclosures the customer was shown) doesn't exist. Depends on: legality-engine, commit-envelope, testing-bdd, product-data.

### M9. Migration and deploy sequencing across topics
